## Subject: Fw: Last letter
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:13:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Last letterFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 4 May 2009 13:57:42 +0000Dear family,    I don’t think it’s sunk in yet that I’m leaving.  This last week in some of the quieter hours, I’ve spent a lot of time pondering my mission- my successes, my faults, my high times and my low times.  I had fewer baptisms than I would have liked to have, but as I pondered, I realized; if every person that I taught and got an answer had been baptized, perhaps I could have baptized hundreds of people.  In fact, I do not doubt it.  I have seen hundreds of people feel the power of the spirit as I taught.  They knew it was true, for no one can deny the whisperings of the Holy Spirit.  Perhaps I wasted unnecessary time working with them and waiting for them to progress while they did not keep their commitments that lead to baptism.     This last week we had the Zone leader Counsel in Florianopolis.  I received several honors and was glad to know that Pres Queiroz thinks well of me.  President asked me to say the closing prayer, which he usually reserves for himself to bless us.  I shall miss dearly being a missionary, especially of our mission.  I feel that I have done well as a missionary.   When I arrived in the mission, Pres. Dansie requested that we write our own testimony of the living Christ, and prepare it throughout our missions to give to him at the end.  He is not here, but I will give you my testimony of the Savior Jesus Christ.Jesus Christ was chosen before this earth was created to be our savior and redeemer. He is the god of the Old Testament and the great I AM; Jehovah. All things exist by the grace of His glory. He is the Light and the Life of the world, a light that is endless, that never can be darkened; a light that gives life to all creatures in existence. He took upon Himself flesh and blood and walked among us, even the light which illumines our lives, yet he was rejected, for even as I have seen and bear witness, men loved darkness and reject the light.  He walked among us and grew grace for every grace, light upon light until He received a fullness of the Glory of the Father, and was and is One with the Father. He was pure, clean from all sin, and was worthy to fulfill His mission and bring to pass the eternal life and immortality of mankind by means of making atonement with us His brethren, and our very Eternal Father. It was He who created the earth and filled it with light. He was chosen from the beginning to overcome the natural effects of the fall and allow us, His brethren, to be redeemed from physical death through resurrection, and spiritual death on conditions of following His Gospel of having Faith on His name, Repentance, Baptism, Baptism by the receipt of the gift of the Holy Ghost and abiding in accordance with all other ordinances of His Gospel.  And as we abide by our promises made in our covenant, we are purified, with the promise of being sanctified and made perfect in Him.  He is the God of the Old Testament, the Hope of Israel, the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel.He was born to Mary, a virgin, and is the very Son of God in the flesh. He was born of humble circumstances and gave the perfect example of service and righteousness, walking before His Father with a broken heart and a contrite spirit, suffering pains and afflictions and temptations of every kind, yet He never ceded to sin. Being thus pure He qualified Himself to make Himself an offering for sin.In the Garden of Gethsemane, He suffered for our sins, making possible a remission of our sins. He took upon Him the pains and hurt of all men that have ever lived and have yet to live, that He might know how to succor them in their need, and bind up the broken hearted. These things I know, for I myself have felt His power to purify of sin, His matchless peace that comes to those who suffer, and I testify that this power is very, very real.  I know, and put forth my witness that in our darkest hours when all is seemingly lost and our hearts cry out for sympathy and justice, when our hearts cry, “is there no balm to my broken soul?!”; I know that the comfort of the loving arms of Him who suffers with us comes to bind up the broken hearted for he took upon Himself our pains in the garden of Gethsemane that He might know how to succor us in our need.After suffering in Gethsemane, He was imprisoned, judged unlawfully and delivered up to be given an ignominious and horrible death. Crucifixion, the death consigned to thieves and assassins was decreed on the only human being to walk blamelessly on this earth, even the creator of this world, and there, on Calvary, he poured out His whole soul unto death. His great heart literally broke for sorrow of the sins of His people. ‘Behold the wounds in His hands His feet, the Blood and tears both mingled down. Did ere such love and sorrow meet, or thorns compose so rich a crown?’After three days in the sepulcher, Jesus Christ, the Anointed One resurrected to life and immortality. I testify, with the energy of my living soul, that He does, indeed, live. And by so living, all men shall live again, raised from corruption to incorruption, from death to endless life, then to be judged by the very being that suffered their cause. As a resurrected being, He still lives, He still loves and He still speaks. After the long darkness of apostasy and absence of His holy Priesthood and men called after His holy order, He and our Eternal Father appeared to Joseph Smith and called him to be an Elias or restorer of the fullness of the Gospel. Jesus Christ has spoken again and sent forth angels to teach men the Plan of Salvation and ordain men to His Holy Order to teach these things to the rest of the children of men. I have been called to this Order, and having received an holy calling and ordinance, I testify, in the very name of Jesus Christ, that He Does live. All men can grow in His holy light through repentance and holy works, and see that light grow brighter and brighter until the perfect day. As I ponder His amazing sacrifice, I am want to sing the words; “Love so amazing, so divine demands my heart, my life, my all.” This is my testimony, This is my life, my force, my Hope and my dream, and I know that in accordance with my works in the flesh and my strivings in the spirit one day I too shall receive my body again, this time in absolute perfection there to be crowned with glory, immortality and eternal life- by the side of my dearest loved ones- never more to depart out of the arms of my Savior, my Captain, King and Dearest Friend, for it is By His power that it is done.And now I lift my voice to all souls to whom may read; I know that Jesus is the Christ the Holy Son of the Living God.  Come unto Him.  Come unto Him and receive the joy that was prepared for you since the foundation of the world!  I would that all men might come unto Him and feel as I feel, Know as I know and Hope as I hope.  That all that read may find the grace of this Jesus and reach His peace and salvation is my prayer, in the sacred name of Jesus Christ. AMENJoseph Levi AndrewsI love you all and am I look forward to seeing you on Friday. Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao 2
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:18:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao 2From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 4 May 2009 13:47:31 +0000Elder AndrewsElder M. PereiraUnião da Vitória IIZona União da VitóriaDear President,    I don’t think it’s sunk in yet that I’m leaving.  This last week in some of the quieter hours, I’ve spent a lot of time pondering my mission- my successes, my faults, my high times and my low times.  I had fewer baptisms than I would have liked to have, but as I pondered, I realized; if every person that I taught and got an answer had been baptized, perhaps I could have baptized hundreds of people.  In fact, I do not doubt it.  I have seen hundreds of people feel the power of the spirit as I taught.  They knew it was true, for no one can deny the whisperings of the Holy Spirit.  Perhaps I wasted unnecessary time working with them and waiting for them to progress while they did not keep their commitments that lead to baptism.  If I could give one piece of advice to the other missionaries, it would be to know when to drop investigators.  I thank you for your love, support, and the enthusiasm you brought to our mission.     When I arrived in the mission, Pres. Dansie requested that we write our own testimony of the living Christ, and prepare it throughout our missions to give to him at the end.  He is not here, but I will give you my testimony of the Savior Jesus Christ.Jesus Christ was chosen before this earth was created to be our savior and redeemer. He is the god of the Old Testament and the great I AM; Jehovah. All things exist by the grace of His glory. He is the Light and the Life of the world, a light that is endless, that never can be darkened; a light that gives life to all creatures in existence. He took upon Himself flesh and blood and walked among us, even the light which illumines our lives, yet he was rejected, for even as I have seen and bear witness, men loved darkness and reject the light.  He walked among us and grew grace for every grace, light upon light until He received a fullness of the Glory of the Father, and was and is One with the Father. He was pure, clean from all sin, and was worthy to fulfill His mission and bring to pass the eternal life and immortality of mankind by means of making atonement with us His brethren, and our very Eternal Father.It was He who created the earth and filled it with light. He was chosen from the beginning to overcome the natural effects of the fall and allow us, His brethren, to be redeemed from physical death through resurrection, and spiritual death on conditions of following His Gospel of having Faith on His name, Repentance, Baptism, Baptism by the receipt of the gift of the Holy Ghost and abiding in accordance with all other ordinances of His Gospel.  And as we abide by our promises made in our covenant, we are purified, with the promise of being sanctified and made perfect in Him.  He is the God of the Old Testament, the Hope of Israel, the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel.He was born to Mary, a virgin, and is the very Son of God in the flesh. He was born of humble circumstances and gave the perfect example of service and righteousness, walking before His Father with a broken heart and a contrite spirit, suffering pains and afflictions and temptations of every kind, yet He never ceded to sin. Being thus pure He qualified Himself to make Himself an offering for sin. In the Garden of Gethsemane, He suffered for our sins, making possible a remission of our sins. He took upon Him the pains and hurt of all men that have ever lived and have yet to live, that He might know how to succor them in their need, and bind up the broken hearted. These things I know, for I myself have felt His power to purify of sin, His matchless peace that comes to those who suffer, and I testify that this power is very, very real.  I know, and put forth my witness that in our darkest hours when all is seemingly lost and our hearts cry out for sympathy and justice, when our hearts cry, “is there no balm to my broken soul?!”; I know that the comfort of the loving arms of Him who suffers with us comes to bind up the broken hearted for he took upon Himself our pains in the garden of Gethsemane that He might know how to succor us in our need.After suffering in Gethsemane, He was imprisoned, judged unlawfully and delivered up to be given an ignominious and horrible death. Crucifixion, the death consigned to thieves and assassins was decreed on the only human being to walk blamelessly on this earth, even the creator of this world, and there, on Calvary, he poured out His whole soul unto death. His great heart literally broke for sorrow of the sins of His people. ‘Behold the wounds in His hands His feet, the Blood and tears both mingled down. Did ere such love and sorrow meet, or thorns compose so rich a crown?’After three days in the sepulcher, Jesus Christ, the Anointed One resurrected to life and immortality. I testify, with the energy of my living soul, that He does, indeed, live. And by so living, all men shall live again, raised from corruption to incorruption, from death to endless life, then to be judged by the very being that suffered their cause. As a resurrected being, He still lives, He still loves and He still speaks. After the long darkness of apostasy and absence of His holy Priesthood and men called after His holy order, He and our Eternal Father appeared to Joseph Smith and called him to be an Elias or restorer of the fullness of the Gospel. Jesus Christ has spoken again and sent forth angels to teach men the Plan of Salvation and ordain men to His Holy Order to teach these things to the rest of the children of men. I have been called to this Order, and having received an holy calling and ordinance, I testify, in the very name of Jesus Christ, that He Does live. All men can grow in His holy light through repentance and holy works, and see that light grow brighter and brighter until the perfect day. As I ponder His amazing sacrifice, I am want to sing the words; “Love so amazing, so divine demands my heart, my life, my all.” This is my testimony, This is my life, my force, my Hope and my dream, and I know that in accordance with my works in the flesh and my strivings in the spirit one day I too shall receive my body again, this time in absolute perfection there to be crowned with glory, immortality and eternal life- by the side of my dearest loved ones- never more to depart out of the arms of my Savior, my Captain, King and Dearest Friend, for it is By His power that it is done.And now I lift my voice to all souls to whom may read; I know that Jesus is the Christ the Holy Son of the Living God.  Come unto Him.  Come unto Him and receive the joy that was prepared for you since the foundation of the world!  I would that all men might come unto Him and feel as I feel, Know as I know and Hope as I hope.  And from henceforth let no man trouble me; for I bear in my body the marks of the Lord Jesus. That all that read may find the grace of this Jesus and reach His peace and salvation is my prayer, in the sacred name of Jesus Christ. AMENJoseph Levi AndrewsThank you for all you have done and continue to do to assist us.  God bless you and the missionaries of the Brazil Florianópolis Mission.Love Elder AndrewsBapt/Conf…….0/0Bat marc………15/7Pesq na igr…….6Lições................31Novos................11

## Subject: Fw: Epistle to the Andrews family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:19:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Epistle to the Andrews familyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 27 Apr 2009 14:21:18 +0000Dear Family,This week we had Zone Conference and interviews, and I learned a lot.  I got letters from Rebecca and Jason, Elder Paul Woodbury, President Ross and a recent convert that we baptized in Itajai.  Thank you for your inspiring and hope filled letters.  I am Excited to work and will not desist until the end.  This week we discussed the state of our branch here and we decided that we would make a covenant with the Lord to baptize a new branch president and other leaders until 17 of June.  Our lunch messages are also being revamped and we are trying to help the members know what they can do to repent and be worthy to receive the blessings of a branch presidency.    My testimony of the Priesthood grows ever stronger.  We gave a blessing to a little girl with a fever that wasn’t supposed to go away for another three or four days and the next day we saw her playing and active, completely cured.  Her parents accepted the message of the restoration but unfortunately are only passing through the city on vacation and will return to Sao Paulo this week.  This week we went and climbed Morro da Cruz (Cross Hill) and prayed to consecrate our covenant and area for the work we are doing.  The Spirit was strong and we feel Heavens aid with us.  I love to be a missionary and work with all my might mind heart and strength.  The Lord is our strength, the one true rock of our salvation, and those who do all to build themselves in the restored gospel will never, ever fall.  I know it with all that I am. I just got my travel Itinerary and I will be back next Friday at more or less 9:15 AM.  I will be in the Dallas airport for an hour for a layover.  It feels weird to know that I will be home again.  It seems like yesterday that I left.  I remember getting on the plane in KC and looking out the window at the city going away.  I thought to myself; “Joseph you idiot, why did you say that you thought you would do will in learning another language?”  I was going to a strange place, with a strange people who speak a strange language.  None of my knowledge would be of any use if I didn’t know how to express it.  Now its all so normal.  I want you to know that I love you all and pray for you.  Thank you for all the support and love that you have shown me throughout my life.  I love you and thank you.             Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao 2
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:20:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao 2From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 27 Apr 2009 14:07:31 +0000Elder AndrewsElder M PereiraUnião da Vitória IIZona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz,    I enjoyed the conference and came away feeling enthused to do the work.  Thank you for answering my questions that I had and making things clear.  I am Excited to work and will not desist until the end.  This week we discussed the state of our branch here and we decided that we would make a covenant with the Lord to baptize a new branch president and other leaders until 17 of June.  Our lunch messages are also being revamped and we are trying to help the members know what they can do to repent and be worthy to receive the blessings of a branch presidency.  Elder M Pereira is doing fine and I like working with him and will do my best to help him prepare for being senior.    This week we dropped a few investigators who never go to church no matter how many times they tell you they will.  It is sometimes difficult, both for us and for them.  We went to a house where live several recent convert girls who haven’t been to church in a while and it turns out that there father isn’t letting them go anymore.  He says that they are getting uppity and telling him that he shouldn’t drink, smoke, beat them, or do drugs anymore.  So he said that he doesn’t have a problem with any religion and he’ll let his girls go if he thinks its the right religion.  He was drinking the whole time and was jumping from excuse to excuse.  So I told him the way it is.  I asked him what he would do if the Savior appeared to him and said he was decepcionado with him.  He said he would change.  So I told him that the Savior WAS decepcionado with him and wanted him to repent.  I told him what he could do to repent and have peace and happiness in his life and it all started with letting his daughters go to church.  I bore my testimony with all the energy I had and told him he could repent and still have happiness.  I told him only the Gospel of Jesus Christ could heal his torn family.  He was crying the whole time, but in the end he wouldn’t let his daughters go.  I left sorrowing for the girls and what lies ahead for them.  I pray for them to have the strength and the courage to continue.  I said a lot of things to him, gave promises if he did what was right, and a caution of what would happen if he didn’t.  Afterwards I was in doubt if I had done the right thing in speaking in the way I did.  I asked my companion if he could feel the Holy Ghost when I was speaking and he said yes.  That made glad.  If the Spirit is felt, that’s what counts.     My testimony of the Priesthood grows ever stronger.  We gave a blessing to a little girl with a fever that wasn’t supposed to go away for another three or four days and the next day we saw her playing and active, completely cured.  Her parents accepted the message of the restoration but unfortunately are only passing through the city on vacation and will return to Sao Paulo this week.  This week we went and climbed morro da cruz and prayed to consecrate our covenant and area for the work we are doing.  The Spirit was strong and we feel Heavens aid with us.  I love to be a missionary and work with all my might mind heart and strength.  The Lord is our strength, the one true rock of our salvation, and those who do all to build themselves in the restored gospel will never, ever fall.  I know it with all that I am.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bat/ conf………….0/0Bat marc………….13/6Pesq na igr……….3Lições....................30Novos.....................16Website checked

## Subject: Fw: Dear Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:21:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 20 Apr 2009 15:03:42 +0000Dear Family,   This week was great, we got a lot accomplished and found thirty nine new people to teach.  All in all I like working with my companion.  He is quite the joke.  At first I thought he liked to complain, but I finally figured out that that’s just his way of joking around.  He’s a real laugh.  Our zone had an emergency transfer this week so we lost our buddy Elder Shipley and got Elder Vaz.  Everyone seems to be happy and the work is going better now, so we’re happy here.  The only problem is that the elders got here without money to buy food, so I gave away a lot of food this week.  My last two companions have had a lot of desire to work and are proactive, so I feel like I’m ending my mission well.   There is no problem if a lot of the family doesn’t come to KC to see me when I come home, I left like a thief in the night, I will come home the same way… literally.  You’d better hide all the peanut butter and maple syrup.  I will continue to work hard until the end, so have no fears about trunkiness interfering with my work.  I will however inform you that I will be home in eighteen days…   I don’t have a whole lot of time to write, so I will end with expressing my love to you all and my thank you for all you have done to sustain me.  The Lord’s work will always continue, so never get in the comfort zone.  I wish you all a happy week.    Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw:
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:22:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject:From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 6 Apr 2009 15:15:45 +0000Dear Family,                Im sorry to hear that it was a lousy week with work, Ive had a few of those in my life.  I am glad to read that Ruths delivery went well.  I am excited to get to know my new nieces and nephews.     I was a little sad to see elder Coburn leave, but that’s life I guess.  Elder M Pereira will help me out with getting people baptized, he has a bit of a strong personality and is very bold in his teaching.  I figure I will just go with it and see if it works.  So far, I think it is.  Elder Eliakim left the area in pretty good condition and there are a number of people who have good potential to get baptized this transfer.  I studied the message in the mission news letter about the power of prayer.  I really understand the importance of being obedient and have a greater desire to gain power through obedience.  In conference this week, I noticed that that seemed to be a repeated theme in what I was hearing.  I spoke with E. Pereira about how we can help our zone out and get more baptisms.  We came up with some good plans and decided that we need to help the zone be more obedient to qualify for the blessings we wish for.  This week I started to feel a temptation to get dissapointed about finishing the mission and that I have not done a good job, and while its true that there is always much more that we could have done, I was feeling that I haven’t done very well as a missionary.  But I know that the devil will try with all his might to weaken me with doubt.  I know the answer to such feelings is repentance and work.  So I prayed for more help and took more teaching experiences.  And it works.    Elder M Pereira is doing well, is good at giving invitations to be baptized or go to church, but his teaching could use some improvement.  So I am helping him there and he is already getting better.  I think he will be just fine as a senior missionary.  He will work, and work well.     I love you all and hope that all goes well back at home.  Have a great week.         Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao II
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:22:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao IIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 13 Apr 2009 13:25:20 +0000Elder AndrewsElder M. PereiraUnião da Vitória IIZona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz,  Thank you for your response to my email.  I am adjusting gradually to my companion.  He has something of a different kind of sense of humor and I have found that the best way to get used to another’s sense of humor is to go with it and adopt it.  This week we found two decent families and blessed them.  We’ll see where they go with the follow ups.  We had our zone meeting this week in Mafra and gave a training on obedience and having an obedient comportment.  We compared our mission to Zion’s Camp, how there was a call for 500, and only some two hundred went.  Of the two hundred, some were valiant and obedient, some complained and were good only when things went smoothly.  Later on, when the quorums of the twelve and seventy were organized, all except three were chosen from Zion’s Camp- those who were faithful and obedient.  We also read in D&amp;C 103:25-36 about the organization of the camp.  It appears that it was not in the original plan that the Prophet went with them, and they were told to ask that he might go with them and bless them.  So we told the elders to be obedient and pray so that an apostle might come and bless our mission.  I hope it gives them a greater desire to be obedient.       Elder M Pereira is doing well.  He is straightforward and is teaching well.  He also has a lot of good ideas.  I’m old and tired, and not very creative anymore, so it feels good to have a companion that can think up some new stuff.  He is obedient and as far as I can tell, he is doing just fine.    We have spent the last week and a half contacting and teaching the people that the other elders left for us to teach, and I was feeling like we should find some more people and keep looking for new investigators.  Interestingly enough, in the beginning of my mission, finding new people to teach was my hardest challenge, but since your arrival in July and the introduction of the new techniques, it transformed into my favorite thing to do.  With E. M. Pereira it will be easier to do the follow ups and decide who will get baptized or not.  We are working closer to the chapel and our own house, and after only one investigator went to church this week, I have decided to always chase them down and work them into the habit of going to church.  It worked last week, so it should work in the end.  It is really easy to get depressed at the end of your mission and I am being as careful as I can to work to get out of situations where I can get depressed and work hard to feel the Spirit.  I love the missionary work and will work as hard as possible until the end.  Our numbers this week were as follows;Bat/conf…………………0/0Bat marc………………....7/2Pesq na sacramental……..1Liçoes……………………23Novos…………………….11Website no processo de atualização e checked.............sim

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear familyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 13 Apr 2009 13:35:28 +0000Dear Family    Thank you for your response to my email.  I am adjusting gradually to my companion.  He has something of a different kind of sense of humor and I have found that the best way to get used to another’s sense of humor is to go with it and adopt it.  This week we found two decent families and blessed them.  We’ll see where they go with the follow ups.  We had our zone meeting this week in Mafra and gave a training on obedience and having an obedient comportment.  We compared our mission to Zion’s Camp, how there was a call for 500, and only some two hundred went.  Of the two hundred, some were valiant and obedient, some complained and were good only when things went smoothly.  Later on, when the quorums of the twelve and seventy were organized, all except three were chosen from Zion’s Camp- those who were faithful and obedient.  We also read in D&amp;C 103:25-36 about the organization of the camp.  It appears that it was not in the original plan that the Prophet went with them, and they were told to ask that he might go with them and bless them.  So we told the elders to be obedient and pray so that an apostle might come and bless our mission.  I hope it gives them a greater desire to be obedient.       Elder M Pereira is doing well.  He is straightforward and is teaching well.  He also has a lot of good ideas.  I’m old and tired, and not very creative anymore, so it feels good to have a companion that can think up some new stuff.  He is obedient and as far as I can tell, he is doing just fine.    We have spent the last week and a half contacting and teaching the people that the other elders left for us to teach, and I was feeling like we should find some more people and keep looking for new investigators.  Interestingly enough, in the beginning of my mission, finding new people to teach was my hardest challenge, but since the arrival of President Queiroz in July and the introduction of the new techniques, it transformed into my favorite thing to do.  With E. M. Pereira it will be easier to do the follow ups and decide who will get baptized or not.  We are working closer to the chapel and our own house, and after only one investigator went to church this week, I have decided to always chase them down and work them into the habit of going to church.  It worked last week, so it should work in the end.  I am glad to hear that all is going well back home and everybody is in good health or recovering well.  Easter went well.  I fasted for the gift of charity and for a greater comprehension of the Atonement of Jesus Christ.  The church didn’t really do anything special for Easter Sunday, which surprised me.  The leader that is currently responsible for the branch is rather inexperienced and said that he was chosen to preside over the branch for lack of having anyone more capable of peaceable.  He is a humble man and I admire him for his courage and goodness.  I love you all and pray for your well being.  I hope that on my return I can be a better person to you all than I was when I left.  Thank you all for your love, support and patience to me.  Have a great week and remember that I love you all.Love Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Telegramish letter do elder shique
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:24:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Telegramish letter do elder shiqueFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 30 Mar 2009 15:55:52 +0000Dear Family,    I did send out my return date to you but for some reason or other it didnt get through to you.  I will get home on Friday May 8th, sometime between 12:00 AM and 12:00 PM.  That’s just forty days away FYI…  I’m getting transferred again, this time to the other side of the river.  I’ll be attending the same branch so I can still see all my converts and friends from my last area. This week we got a lot more done and I think we’re leaving our area better than we found it.  If I’m correct, there is potential to have six baptisms this transfer in the area and perhaps more as well.  I don’t know that I’ve ever gotten to work an entire city before, but I’m excited to make a difference on the other side of the city now.  Now that I am at my last transfer, I will have to keep myself focused and not just wait and suck it up until the end.  I want my last transfer to be my best.  I’m going to work as hard as I can for the next five weeks.  I enjoyed the zone leader counsel this week and learned a lot and this transfer I will be doing better to help my zone out and increase the faith to obey and baptize.    I really enjoyed my transfer with Elder Coburn and we both grew a great deal.  After this transfer and then this next with the assistants, he should be well prepared to be a leader.  He is a great missionary with a strong testimony.   On Saturday, we taught a man who moved here and is living with his aunt (a member of the church) and is waiting for his family to move down here too.  His Aunt gave him a Book of Mormon and he read and liked it and had a great many questions.  So she invited us to come over on Saturday to teach him.  We taught him the first lesson and he promptly accepted the invitation to baptism.  He is not married to his wife, so he –not us- said that he would have to get married.  This man is the type of man that, depending on what his wife he has, will be firm in the church and perhaps a leader in the church.  A couple of weeks ago we knocked a door and it turned out to be a family of a member who had separated from his family and all of his kids were baptized except for the oldest and his (ex) wife.  We gave a powerful blessing there and guess who is looking for religion and went to church yesterday?  The oldest daughter- Kelli.  I’m pretty sure that the next elders will baptize her and her daughter within the next two weeks.     I love you all and hope you all have a great week.  Thank you for all your support and love.  I hope Erin and Jackson are doing alright and GmaZ as well.   Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao II
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:24:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao IIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 6 Apr 2009 15:09:31 +0000Elder AndrewsElder M. PereiraUnião da Vitória IIZona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz,   I was a little sad to see elder Coburn leave, but that’s life I guess.  Elder M Pereira will help me out with getting people baptized, he has a bit of a strong personality and is very bold in his teaching.  I figure I will just go with it and see if it works.  So far, I think it is.  Elder Eliakim left the area in pretty good condition and there are a number of people who have good potential to get baptized this transfer.  I studied the message in the mission news letter about the power of prayer.  I really understand the importance of being obedient and have a greater desire to gain power through obedience.  In conference this week, I noticed that that seemed to be a repeated theme in what I was hearing.  I spoke with E. Pereira about how we can help our zone out and get more baptisms.  We came up with some good plans and decided that we need to help the zone be more obedient to qualify for the blessings we wish for.  This week I started to feel a temptation to get desanimado about finishing the mission and that I have not done a good job, and while its true that there is always much more that we could have done, I was feeling that I haven’t done very well as a missionary.  But I know that the devil will try with all his might to weaken me with doubt.  I know the answer to such feelings is repentance and work.  So I prayed for more help and took more teaching experiences.  And it works.  Elder M Pereira is doing well, is good at giving invitations to be baptized or go to church, but his teaching could use some improvement.  So I am helping him there and he is already getting better.  I think he will be just fine as a senior missionary.  He will work, and work well.  He is doing fine with obedience as well.    Theres not a whole lot to report about our area, we basically spent the week finding the people on the lists left by Elder Eliakim.    One thing that has been bugging me recently is the fault of baptisms in the last year of my mission.  I have noticed that I have a strong tendency to talk a lot and I have given a lot of examples of finding people in my emails to you.  There would appear to be something that doesn’t add up between the number of people I find and in the number of my baptisms.  I love to teach, and if you talk to any of my companions, they may say I teach well and with the spirit, but something I feel that I lack is knowing how to take someone by the hand and lead them to the waters of baptism.  I had one transfer with my trainer who was a wonderful missionary and we baptized a lot.  Then, I spent four transfers with one companion who had no desire to work and kept few rules, and another who didn’t keep rules and we never baptized.  I didn’t really learn to baptize.  And then I turned senior and trainer.  From then on I have occasionally had good companions who helped me, but always for little time.  The elders need to know who to keep teaching, who it is worth to go back, when and why to stop finding when you’ve already found, and how and when to invite the people to make and keep commitments.  With my current companion, I think I will be just fine.  He knows when to invite and is bold in doing so and we will both learn from each other.  I want you to know that I have no doubt that you have been doing the right things for the mission and that my lack of baptisms is not because you came.  I feel that those who were seniors with Pres. Dansie may not be able to partake of the blessings of the mission as much as the rest that arrive and achieve maturity under the new president.  Perhaps we are the forerunners and then arrive the great baptizers.  I feel that the rising generation of the Missao Brasil Florianopolis will be the greatest and will be well prepared.  I will do all that I can to help them, and baptize as much as possible.  Thank you for all that you have done to help us and I love and sustain you.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/Confirmaçoes………..0/0Bat marcados………………7/2Pesq na sacr...........................6Lições....................................21Novos....................................8

## Subject: Fw: Epistle
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:25:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: EpistleFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 23 Mar 2009 15:59:52 +0000Dear Family,  This week we did alot of follow up on alot of the new invetsigators we found last week and some things went well and others not so well.  At least we could sift out the wheat from the tares.  On Wednesday night we ventured into unexplored territory into a distant neighborhood called Bom Jesus.  We had marked an appointment with the lady who works the ice cream stand in the center on our way to our area.  It was a real adventure because it is about an hour and a half walk from our house, and we didn’t know when the next bus would be.  When we got there I asked when the next bus would be and she said 11:30 PM.  It was already 8:30, so we needed to get a ride from somebody.  Her neighbors offered a ride and we got home on time just barely.  Needless to say, when we went back the next day we got a ride with a member and marked their baptisms for next week.  Apparently they have some doubts we’ll have to resolve before their baptisms go through.  We didn’t use the bus this week so we didn’t get to do any preaching, but there is this house that we always walk by with a crowd of people out front, so we decided to take the opportunity to teach a group.  We just gave a blessing, but I suppose we will go back again this week. My companion is doing well and is really learning to follow the spirit as he teaches and also how to invite the spirit.  Last night he really brought the spirit as we tried to resolve someone’s concerns about tithing.  I am enjoying teaching with him and doing the work together as well.  He is obedient and likes to work.  There is a boy of 11 years named Gustavo we have been teaching for some time and who has prayed to know if what we teach of the restoration is true and received and answer and wants to be baptized as his older brother and sister have been baptized, but his mom will not let him get baptized until he finishes catechism in three years.  She says that he is too young to make that kind of decision.  If I weren’t so smart, I would have told her that he was too young to make the decision to be baptized catholic when he was four days old.  I told her that it was not his decision, to get baptized in the true church, but that of God, because he had prayed and received an answer from God that it was the right thing to do.  We spent a lot of time there trying to get her to give in, but she just closed her heart to the spirit and rejected it.  It wasn’t the best way to end the week, but we still have faith that we can win her over.  It just wont be easy.    Last night I discovered that the majority of catholics do not have an understanding of what deity is, nor of who Jesus Christ really is.  As we taught this woman, the spirit told me that she does not have faith in Jesus Christ.  She really just believes that there is some God out there and the purpose of religion is to pray and feel peace.  The devil has gathered up all the apostasy that would make himself god and stamped it with the name of Christianity and leads away the greater part of mankind with a counterfeit and a fraud.  I got kind of sad to see that last night and then see her close her heart to the testimony of the spirit when the truth is before her.  Perhaps I can teach with greater testimony of the Living Christ and use the Book of Mormon not just as a proof that Joseph Smith is a prophet, but also that Jesus is the Christ manifesting himself unto all nations.  May I have the strength to open my mouth and spread the Father’s love wherever I go. Well it sounds like Carl is being a safado up there in Ohio.  I am glad to hear that Gma Z will be there when I get home.  I miss my grandmothers.  I wish good luck to dad as he heads up to Ohio.  I hope all goes well with Erin and Ruths births and wish a happy birthday to Anna, Dad and Sydney.  Yesterday I after lunch the members with whom we had eaten turned on BYU TV and the womens chorus was performing.  I was kind of disappointed because I was expecting to see Aurelia on the piano, but the performance must have been from a while ago cause I didn’t see her or any of my cousins.  From all the books listed in Dads last email, it sounds like when I get home, I’ll end up doing a lot of reading. I love you all and thank you for your love, support, prayers and help that you gave me in preparing to serve a mission.  I hope all is well with you and that the Lord bless you and keep you.Love,  Joseph

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Epistle
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:26:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: EpistleFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 9 Mar 2009 15:50:02 +0000Dear Family,    Question:  did I hear a hint that Ruth is pregnant?  I knew that Erin should be having a baby here in a month or something, but I haven’t heard anything about Ruth.  Sounds like its more or less uneventful back at home for now.  Yesterday morning while we were on our way to pick up a family at 7:00 AM to take to church and help carry their twins we saw a drunk guy on a motorcycle weave and crash.  Fortunately for drunk people, they don’t feel pain very well, so he just got up again and rode on.  Some people are brilliant.  This week we went out to the city of Mafra to have a zone meeting in preparation for zone conference this week, and while we were doing the training I felt a lot of doubts about the ways we are going about the work we are doing and a lot of the doubts were somewhat confirmed as I passed through Canoinhas to do two baptismal interviews in which I had to teach them what tithing was.  That night, my companion and I stayed up late and conversed with each other about baptism, qualifications for baptism, ways to prepare people better, etc.  This week I am going to talk to president about it to see if we are right about the conclusions we came to.   We started to teach that family that we found and who had prayed to find a path to peace, and boy, it has not been easy.  I had to tell the woman to stop beating her kids, repent and follow the gospel of Jesus Christ to have joy and peace.  She was honestly thinking of doing herself harm, so we told her with all the testimony we could muster that she was a child of God, and that she is precious.  My companion spoke with great power and in the end we gave her a blessing and left a Book of Mormon marked to Alma 36.  It is both applicable to pain caused by sin, as well as to pain caused by abuse, death, depression etc.  Her husband says that they don’t want to get baptized, but that “we have to get baptized”.  It will be a bit of a wait, because they will need to get married, and she was previously married to a guy who after being married for a month, ran away and disappeared, so getting a divorce is a lengthy ordeal.  But she could use the time to prepare herself and undergo the spiritual healing accessible  through repentance and that of receiving the spirit of Christ unto the remission of sins. I have a feeling that I might be “demoted” from being a zone leader this next transfer for not having sufficient baptisms, but I don’t really care that much.  I didn’t really come on a mission for positions, but to serve.  I have had a good amount of baptisms and I can say that when someone is baptized for the wrong reasons, or just isn’t prepared (meaning they haven’t really repented of their sins), I always came away with a sort of empty feeling, as opposed to when I baptize people like Heidy, Tati, Amalia, Marcos, Erica, Mariana, Naiza, Salete, Wilian, or Andressa, I can feel the true joy of having helped someone come unto Christ through faith, repentance, baptism and receiving the gift of the Holy Ghost.  And each of those people are my friends, and will not fall away if they follow a true course.  There are many others who were not baptized, but they did repent.  I love to be a missionary and a representative of Jesus, our beloved Savior.  I hope to serve Him in the best way possible.  I love each of you and pray for you always that the Lord bless you and keep you.          Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao da Vit 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:26:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao da Vit 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 16 Mar 2009 16:33:38 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CoburnUnião da Vitória 1Zona União da VitóriaDear President Quieroz,    we found alot of new investigators this week, going to appointments and teaching people’s friends with them .  On Thursday, we taught two power lessons in the evening and I think one of those people could easily be turned into a baptism in the coming two weeks.  It really will depend on his mom, but we are also working with the mom to soften her up for getting baptized.  With all the new investigators we have gotten in the last weeks, I think we can start to just cut people we don’t think will be baptized and stick with the people that have more potential.  Our new convert’s mom went to the baptism on Saturday and we have already invited her to get baptized, to which she said she would pray about it.  We ll get her in the end.  I really enjoyed conference this week and learned a lot about how I can improve my teaching skills and just how to be a better missionary in general. Elder Coburn is doing well and I am preparing him as best I can to be a senior missionary and work well.  I hope I can teach him how to baptize as well.  He is teaching with power and with the spirit and I am ever excited to see him grow.     Friday we went into all the radio stations in town to see if we could do some kind of a broadcast.  The first place said we would be able to do free radio invitations to activities such as football games and stuff, but to give a message, you would have to pay, and besides that, there were no more openings for speaking time because all the other evangelical churches have eaten up the time and even have their own radio spot set apart on the daily broadcast schedule.  That kind of upset me, because we are the true church.  Shouldn’t they just let us take the time to tell the truth?  We left that radio station feeling kind of down, but we just sang to ourselves the song from High School Musical 2- “We can work, work, work this out…”, knowing that if it’s the Lord’s true church, He would provide a way to spread the truth.  The next radio station had no one to attend us, so that just blew right over, and we went to the last radio station praying that the Lord would help us.  I asked Elder Coburn if he thought I always know what to do.  He said yes.  I just told him that I never know what to do and just wing it praying like there’s no tomorrow that the Spirit will guide me.  I always thought that companions knew what to do, but I think they were probably a lot more like me- lost, but guided.  We went to the last place with a prayer in our heart and managed to get permission to go upstairs and talk with the owner.  I knew that what I wanted to do (a broadcast of testimony and an invitation to come unto Christ and be baptized by someone with authority) would normally cost money, so I knew I had to offer an idea that wouldn’t work and was asking for a lot less than I wanted, and then bargain my way up to more or less what I was wanting, so I gave a weak idea.  The guy said there were some draw backs to my “idea” and saw that we didn’t have any money to offer, so I asked him to come up with an idea.  He said we could do something by way of journalism in stead of publicity.  They would do an interview with us in a way that we could put out our invitations in a safe, free way.  So we recorded an interview on the spot.  It should be broadcasting a few more times this week, and I think we might go back and see if we cant expand on the idea with them and do it again, this time for a little bit longer and for a more in depth interview.  We really came out of the station in high spirits!  Every time we ride the bus as well, we will teach a small lesson with power and when the spirit comes on, we will give an invitation to follow the Savior and be baptized.  If one out of every ten people invited has at least a desire to DO something, and accept the invitation, even if it be a tentative acceptance, most likely one out of every thirty people would be baptized.  If every week follows the standard of excellence, we should find a person to be baptized every three weeks knocking doors.  However, if you give an invitation to a bus full of people, lets say that one in every twenty five people accepts an invitation.  If you ride the bus six times a week, you should find, at the least, three people who accept.  If one in three go through with it, that increases our baptisms to one per week, not counting family members of the one accepting.  If we give an invitation over the radio with a decent follow up method, that would roughly reach the ears of 1000 people in a given day depending on the hour.  If one in every fifty is touched by the invitation, you have twenty people ready to be taught and maybe five would be baptized.  If we open our mouth, we can baptize.Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/conf………………………..1/1Bapt marc………………………..0/0Pesq na igr……………………….1Lições............................................33Novos............................................21

## Subject: Fw: The Coburn report...
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:26:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: The Coburn report...From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 16 Mar 2009 16:46:55 +0000Dear Family,  I talked with the assistants this week and Elder Stephanou, who is going home with my group, said that we are leaving the mission on the 7th of may, so I will be getting home on the 8th some time during the day, or morning.  That makes me a little trunky, bit it really makes me want to make the most of being a missionary for the last seven weeks.  I am working as hard as I can, so fear not;  Im not a fubecca…  We found alot of new investigators this week, going to appointments and teaching people’s friends with them .  On Thursday, we taught two power lessons in the evening and I think one of those people could easily be turned into a baptism in the coming two weeks.  It really will depend on his mom, but we are also working with the mom to soften her up for getting baptized.  With all the new investigators we have gotten in the last weeks, I think we can start to just cut people we don’t think will be baptized and stick with the people that have more potential.  Our new convert’s mom went to the baptism on Saturday and we have already invited her to get baptized, to which she said she would pray about it.  We ll get her in the end.  We had  zone conference this week and I really enjoyed it and learned a lot about how I can improve my teaching skills and just how to be a better missionary in general.   Elder Coburn is doing well and I am preparing him as best I can to be a senior missionary and work well.  I hope I can teach him how to baptize as well.  He is teaching with power and with the spirit and I am ever excited to see him grow.     Friday we went into all the radio stations in town to see if we could do some kind of a broadcast.  The first place said we would be able to do free radio invitations to activities such as football games and stuff, but to give a message, you would have to pay, and besides that, there were no more openings for speaking time because all the other evangelical churches have eaten up the time and even have their own radio spot set apart on the daily broadcast schedule.  That kind of upset me, because we are the true church.  Shouldn’t they just let us take the time to tell the truth?  We left that radio station feeling kind of down, but we just sang to ourselves the song from High School Musical 2- “We can work, work, work this out…”, knowing that if it’s the Lord’s true church, He would provide a way to spread the truth.  The next radio station had no one to attend us, so that just blew right over, and we went to the last radio station praying that the Lord would help us.  I asked Elder Coburn if he thought I always know what to do.  He said yes.  I just told him that I never know what to do and just wing it praying like there’s no tomorrow that the Spirit will guide me.  I always thought that companions knew what to do, but I think they were probably a lot more like me- lost, but guided.  We went to the last place with a prayer in our heart and managed to get permission to go upstairs and talk with the owner.  I knew that what I wanted to do (a broadcast of testimony and an invitation to come unto Christ and be baptized by someone with authority) would normally cost money, so I knew I had to offer an idea that wouldn’t work and was asking for a lot less than I wanted, and then bargain my way up to more or less what I was wanting, so I gave a weak idea.  The guy said there were some draw backs to my “idea” and saw that we didn’t have any money to offer, so I asked him to come up with an idea.  He said we could do something by way of journalism in stead of publicity.  They would do an interview with us in a way that we could put out our invitations in a safe, free way.  So we recorded an interview on the spot.  It should be broadcasting a few more times this week, and I think we might go back and see if we cant expand on the idea with them and do it again, this time for a little bit longer and for a more in depth interview.  We really came out of the station in high spirits!  Every time we ride the bus as well, we will teach a small lesson with power and when the spirit comes on, we will give an invitation to follow the Savior and be baptized.  If one out of every ten people invited has at least a desire to DO something, and accept the invitation, even if it be a tentative acceptance, most likely one out of every thirty people would be baptized.  If every week follows the standard of excellence, we should find a person to be baptized every three weeks knocking doors.  However, if you give an invitation to a bus full of people, lets say that one in every twenty five people accepts an invitation.  If you ride the bus six times a week, you should find, at the least, three people who accept.  If one in three go through with it, that increases our baptisms to one per week, not counting family members of the one accepting.  If we give an invitation over the radio with a decent follow up method, that would roughly reach the ears of 1000 people in a given day depending on the hour.  If one in every fifty is touched by the invitation, you have twenty people ready to be taught and maybe five would be baptized.  If we open our mouth, we can baptize. I love each of you and repremand you for not telling me that Ruth was pregnant...  But I forgive you, Im excited to see my awesome nieces and nephews when I go home.  I pray for you and thank you for your prayers, especially whoever it is who is praying for my health- my entire zone is sick except for elder Andrews…  I have been out for a year and ten months and I still have never gotten sick!  Knock on wood…  Have an excellent week!   Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:27:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 23 Feb 2009 15:21:54 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CoburnicusUnião da Vitória 1Zona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz,   This week was great.  I’m not going to lie, I was a little bit worried about the new standards of excellence, but in the end, things started to work out well.  Thank you for letting me be with Elder Coburn, we are having a good time together and we have a lot in common.  Every day this week, we have had a really good experience teaching and with the work in general.  We like singing before every lesson and it brings the spirit rather strongly.  On Thursday morning during companionship study, He taught me the 2nd lesson and I could feel the spirit as he taught.  The way that he taught reminded me of the beginning of my mission.  Its good to remember the fire that you come into the mission with.  He teaches well, bears testimony well and is just a good missionary.   I feel my faith increasing in the fact that the Lord is preparing people for us to teach.  We have found so many widows and widowers this last week that you might even think half the city died some years ago.  We taught the 2nd lesson to Salete, the woman who felt the presence of an angel last week during the blessing, so she knows what the plan is and where her parents are and that she can be with them again.  So I asked if we could come back teach her about how we do it.  She knows what the plan is, so now the only thing left is for her to follow.  On Saturday night we were invited with the elders of the other side of the city to a member’s birthday party that would have some non members there, but it wasn’t even in our area, so the investigators wouldn’t even be ours, so we declined and decided to go try and find some people.  It was tough, because everyone and there dog was partying or busy watching carnival on TV.  But after much rejection, and wading through tribulations of every specie…, we found a family who gladly accepted us and felt the spirit strongly during the blessing.  So we went back last night and taught the 1st lesson about the restoration of the gospel.  They understood well but the father and mother were kind of reluctant to accept baptism, but I could tell their 14 year old daughter felt the spirit and really wanted to get baptized.  We marked their baptisms for two weeks from now, though the daughter, Edna will probably get baptized first, then Alcioní, the father and then the mother.  We are going back tomorrow night.    I feel that a lot can happen here with E. Coburn, because he has faith, testimony and wants to work.  He’s not particularly concerned about himself as much as he is with the work.  Its been a while since Ive had a companion like that.  Its kind of a relief.  We will also be having a baptism this Saturday.  On Saturday morning, we did the dedication of our areas.  We climbed Morro da Cruz and upon getting to the top, there was a badly kept open area with a statue of the Savior and some private property with a huge open field.  So I decided we should ask the owner of the property if we could go out into the field and pray.  Elder Eliakim was somewhat reluctant to ask but I said I would do the talking.  So we clapped out hands outside the gate and out came a woman.  I said “Oi, nos somos quarto humildes servos de Deus, e subimos o morro para fazer uma oração, mas aqui fora não é muito bom para fazer a oração.  Será que  a gente pode usar o campo ai?”  She said yes.  So we went out about 200 feet from the house and started.  It went well.  I’m not sure though, because Elder Hill didn’t really seem too accepting.  I will ask the Lord to see if He accepts the dedication, and act accordingly.  It really was the perfect place to do it though.  As we left, we stopped at the house to thank the woman and she invited us to come back to pray any time we wanted.  I told E. Eliakim that they should probably go back and convert her –if they really wanted to brave the climb up the hill…  Well that is about how our week went and I feel confidant that the Lord will bless us with success as we serve him and love Him as best as possible.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/conf………………………0/0Bapt marc para 2 semanas..........4/2Pesq na reunião sacr....................1Lições..........................................21Novos pesq..................................16Endereços....................................23Lemb se disto..............................95%Qualificar se................................100%Have a great week president.  We love you and I pray for you and the other leaders always.  We are getting ready to BATIZAR O POVO!!!!             Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:27:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 16 Feb 2009 15:30:52 +0000Elder AndrewsElder MoodyUnião da Vitória 1Zona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz, This week was not the best in numbers, but I learned alot and I think that this week we are going to get a whole lot done.  On Tuesday, I went on a division with E. Hill to help him out, talk to him and give him a break.  Elder Eliakim was happy to let elder Hill be with another American for a day.  I think it turned out well.  Elder Hill teaches well and as he taught, I remembered the beginning of my own mission and how I didn’t really know how to say everything that I wanted to say, so the only thing that I could say was my testimony.  I think that I could revert my teaching back to the basics and have some more success.  I am always happy to see Elder Pimentel at the counsel and talk to him.  I always come away with more desire to be a better missionary and exercise my faith.  I was somewhat intimidated with the new standard of excellence, but at the same time I knew it was the right thing for the mission to be doing.  The next two days the Lord blessed me with assurances that if we increase our faith by making higher goals and expectations, he makes it work.  Elder Moody is doing well, though when I left on Thursday for a baptismal interview in Canoinhas, nothing happened in our area for two days.  I got a little worried when he told me.  Our numbers suffered for it too.  He seems excited to be going to Rio Grande do Sul.    Our branch seems to like us and is willing to help and our lider da obra is really starting to get excited and wants to imply some of our ideas to the maximum.  Tomorrow morning Elder Eliakim and I will go to some of the schools and “advertise” our English class so we can get more people to the class and ready to be baptized.  On Saturday, we were supposed to have an appointment at ten in the morning, but we missed the bus, so we kind of sat at the bus station wondering what to do.  So I asked E. Moody if he wanted to make a mass contact with all the people sitting in the station, but he seemed kind of doubtful.  So I told him what it was that we would say and as I was showing him, a lady and her family sat down next to us.  Instead of standing up and doing the contact, I turned around and started talking to her.  Her name is Salete and after a couple of minutes, I offered to go to her house and give her a blessing to which she complied.  We marked to go to her house on Sunday(yesterday).  Yesterday morning before going off to church, in our prayer I used the priesthood to invoke the ministry of angels to be with us for the day and work together with us.  I learned A LOT in church and when we went to Salete’s house, we discovered that she has lost both her parents and her husband as well.  I felt inspired to ask her “If the Lord showed you a way for you to be with your mother, father and husband again, not just till death do you part, but for ever;  would you do what He told you?”  She then said that she still misses her mother very much and just a day ago she cried for saudades for her mother.  She said that if she could be with her just one more time, she would do anything the Lord asked.  I would have been a fool to not have said something, so I promised her that He would show that way and even bore testimony of the sealing power which seals me to my own deceased mother.  I felt that surely after twenty years in the spirit world, her mother must have heard the gospel and felt the desire to follow.  So we did the blessing.  During the prayer, I felt prompted to invoke the presence of angels in the home and that they could even feel the love of their entes queridos comforting them.  Afterward, I told them the feelings they were feeling were the feelings of the spirit to which Salete said “Yeah, I do feel a relief and a peace.  During the prayer, I could feel that there was someone standing right there (pointing her finger to her side) praying with us.”  I assured her there had been someone present with us.  We are going back on Sunday to teach her and her family.     Just one more experience- more or less an hour later, our appointments fell through and there was nothing for us to do.  I prayed several times for inspiration as to what we should do and where to go.  Usually I receive an impression as to what we should do, but this time, nothing.  So we just walked aimlessly for a couple of minutes waiting.  We were about to pass a street when I felt like we should go there.  So we turned down the street and I felt that we were to encounter someone important.  We knocked the first door and nobody was home, so we crossed the street to another house and knocked and a woman came out.  So I started to talk and in the middle of the contact when I was talking about the blessing she invited us in.  Her husband was watching a soccer game, so we just talked for a while with them both and introduced ourselves.  So they turned off the TV and we got to talk about who we were and why we were there.  Beatriz, the woman, said she used to be catholic, but upon reading the bible she decided that the Savior didn’t want her to worship images so she stopped going to the catholic church and prays at home, and maybe the Lord would show her a better way someday.  When she said this, the spirit told me to say “The Lord has heard your prayers and sent us to your house to show you what to do.”  We got set up for the blessing and we knelt down when I remembered that we forgot to explain about how to recognize the spirit.  So really quickly I quoted Galatians 5:22 and how the spirit has the purpose and mission to testify of the truth, and that they would feel the spirit in the prayer testifying that we were true representatives of Jesus Christ.  As I explained all this, I felt  the spirit already testifying and when I got to the part where I explained that the Spirit would show that we were the true representatives of Jesus Christ, Beatriz said “Mas eu já senti isso quando deixei vocês entrar na portão.”  Needless to say we are going back tomorrow with a member and we are going to baptize that woman as soon as possible. What I gather from these two experiences is that the angels and the spirit are willing to do anything and everything if we just set out our intentions in humble prayer, exercise the Priesthood and act in faith.  This week on Thursday, we will go up on morro da cruz and do the dedication of our area.  I feel confidant that in the strength of the Lord, I can do all things, but alone, I am absolutely nothing.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt conf……………..0/0Bapt marked………….3/1Pesq na igr……………1Liç com membro…......16Novos………………...12Endereços……………..21Lemb s dis.....................91%Qualificar se..................100%

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:27:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 2 Mar 2009 15:18:03 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CoburnUnião da Vitória 1Zona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz, Elder Coburn and I are trying our best to better ourselves and find the elect so they can be baptized and confirmed.  Last week I wrote that we would be having a baptism on Saturday (28th of February), but as we continued teaching the prospective member, we thought there was a chance that we could turn one baptism into two.  His Mom hasn’t been taught yet, his brother is a recent convert, and I think it would be good if we could get the whole family baptized, so we decided to postpone the baptism.  He also needed to fulfill a couple more of the commitments in the first lesson.  Every day that passes has a great experience, be it finding someone, a powerful lesson, or some kind of miracle.  But I’ll cover some of those in the last part of my letter.  We met with the district counselor that is responsible for our branch this week to let him know what we are doing and of some of our concerns about retention and how we would like to help the branch grow.  We all like irmão Rodrigues, so I think all should go well there.    Elder Coburn is doing well and we both enjoy teaching together, though I need to put a little more pressure on him to teach and get used to doing the dirty work with me if he is to be a senior companion logo.  He is teaching well and I am working hard to make sure he knows how to teach the first two commandments and the commandments as well.  I have always noted that teaching the commandments has never been a strong point in our mission, perhaps in the rest of the missions as well, but I got a pretty decent idea from Pres. Monteigas’ address to the general priesthood in the district priesthood conference last week.  It’s a good way to focus on the family too.  First we read the parable of the talents in Matthew 25:14-30ish and talk about what the investigators “talents” of gold are with which the Lord has entrusted them.  They almost always respond with their family.  Then we tell them that the message of the parable is that the Lord expects a DIFFERENCE, not just that we bear through having kids and raising them until we are free.  So we teach them how to edify their family, to increase their “talent” two fold through first kneeling in prayer as a family every day, reading the scriptures every day, example of paying tithes, keeping high standards of moral worthiness etc, until you teach all the commandments.  I must say, it brings the spirit very strongly. Our area is doing well, the relationship with the members seems well and we will be doing some family nights this week with the members and lets find some people to be converted!!!  Nobody really likes the idea of getting to lunch and having to leave for fifteen minutes to do contacts, especially during the lunch hour, but this week, we decided to be obedient, so when we got to lunch on Tuesday, lunch wouldn’t be ready for another 20 minutes, so we left to do some contacts.  In that twenty minutes, we found someone that had been set for baptism some years ago but had not been allowed to be baptized.  So we offered to stop by another day and give a blessing to the family, which they accepted.  So we are going back tomorrow and we will see if we can’t get a baptism out of it.   The next afternoon after lunch, our appointments fell through, and as you probably already know, the hours immediately following lunch are the hardest, but we decided to knock some doors and find somebody new.  The second door we knocked was a woman who said that “to be completely honest”, if it were only a blessing we were offering and not a bible study, she would accept.  So we went in and talked for a few moments and found out she and her family, together with her daughter’s family had just moved to Uniao da Vitoria the day before.  We sang “Where can I turn for Peace” and the whole spirit of the house changed.  A feeling of calm came over everyone and we knelt and blessed them and their families.  When we got up, the woman, Anita, was crying and I told her the feelings she was feeling were the fruits of the Holy Ghost, testifying that we were true servants of the Savior.  She told us that less than an hour beforehand, she had been on the back porch weeping and praying that the Lord would show her a light and give a way to have peace.  She said that the Lord had answered her prayer.  She invited us to come back anytime too, despite the fact that before she had said that she “didn’t want to do any bible study”.  I even told her that we don’t do Bible studies.  We help people come unto Christ.  To say the LEAST, we were kind of happy when we left the house.  All in all, we are doing alright and look forward to zone conference next week, and we are going to prepare the zone for conference and give some trainings this week about teaching the lessons.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/conf…………………………0/0Bapt marc…………………………4/2Pesq na igr………………………...1Lições .............................................27Novos..............................................15

I love you all and pray for your well being and hope that the Lord protects you and blesses you for your spiritual and temporal support which you all give me,              Love, Elder Andrews
