## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:28:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 9 Feb 2009 14:48:13 +0000Elder AndrewsElder MoodyUniao da Vitoria 1Zona União da VitóriaDear President Queiroz, This week I did a fast and got our dedicatory prayer written out finally.  I felt relieved to have it done at last.  Now we need to choose a place to go and do the prayer.  If you would like, I can send you a copy of it later on.  I did a division with Elder Grisham this week and we talked a little about the progress of the work.  We both know that in this mission it has been prophesied that we will baptize thousands and we have been thinking about the scripture in Alma 26:22 about the formula for having so many baptisms.  We both agreed that it is impossible to attain this goal just by knocking doors.  I read all of Acts on monday and tuesday and saw that the apostles had success baptizing and converting thousands because they taught in groups.  Acts 1-5 it says that they taught in the TEMPLE.  On his mission, Paul always started his tour of the city going to the SYNAGOGS, and when that wouldnt work (which times were few) he would go to the market to preach, or a school.  It says that he taught in a school for three years and the whole city became advised.  D&amp;C 68 starts off with a command for all elders called to the work; That they go from place to place, land to land preaching in the synagogs of the wicked, reazoning with them and expounding the scriptures unto them in accordanceto what the spirit directs them to say.  In alma 21, it says that the sons of mosiah had great success in their preaching in the synagogs.  So I am thinking that this week I will stop by a start up church in my area that Ive noticed from time to time and request a few moments to bear my testimony of the savior, read some scriptures to them and follow what the Spirit directs.  There are some elders that have gone to churches already, but it has not been a repeated process.  It was done mostly for the glory of men, and therefore it came to nothing.  However, if we go in with the intent to find someone in that church to be baptized, the Lord will bless us with miracles.  When I was in Tubarao, I did an interview with the District Leader for Criciuma(E Cornaby) and he said that the elders in Criciuma 2 were desanimated.  I told him to spend a couple of afternoons with the other elders and split up and knock a street each companionship with the intent of finding at least one good person report afterward.  Its one thing to knock doors of an entire street, and another to excercise faith in finding.  The same is applicable to teaching in a church.  Begin with the end in mind.          Elder Moody is doing alright.  He gets frustrated if we get home after 9:00 though.  This week he got frustrated about several things and told elder Hill.  So Elder Hill told me what was going on.  It was all news to me.  From time to time I notice that Elder Moody is not happy, so I ask if anything is wrong and he says no.  But after all that he has been haveing a good time and has been happier these last few days.           Our area is doing well and those two young women that came to enlish class have a high chance at being baptized.  After english class on saturday, the youth started to play volley ball and the two girls (Gabriella and Kristina) played too.  now they feel comfortable with the members and coming to church, so as soon as the elders on the other side start teaching them, we ll be on a roll.             we figured out how to find Vera (that mom that wont let her daughter be baptized yet) at her member cousins house on Sunday nights, So last night we stopped by, chatted a little and asked the member if we could leave a message(just like we did last week...) so we sang a childs prayer and taught hte first lesson.  Vera kind of sat off to the side and tried not to pay attention.  We invited the member and her familyl to bear their testimonies to each other and the spirit was REALLY strong.  But Vera still wasnt really paying attention, so at last, she just got up to leave with someone else, but I told her we werent finished yet.  I looked straight into her eyes and said;  You probably think we are really smart and sneaky teaching all this while youre here and all, but Ill go ahead and tell you now that this lesson was taught specially for and to YOU.  I then felt the spirit give me a go ahead to speak freely and bear powerfull testimony of our purpose, the retored Gospel and of our Savior Jesus Christ.  I think weve got her.  Just another week and another conversation about her daughter and we should bew able to baptize her daughter.         Last night I had a long conversation with Elder Hill.  He is vry concerned about how many times a person needs to go to church to get baptized and some of the requirements to be baptized as well.  I dont think he sustains some of your decisions in the way of teaching.  Im talking to Elder Eliakim quite a bit as well and boy, I dont think its easy for them.  Elder Eliakim is tired.  Hes been working like a trainer for over six months and sometimes feels alone in the planning and decisions.  After talking to him, he seems to feel better.  We agreed to do a division tomorrow and see what we can do to be better.  I talked to Elder Burke this week as well and said some encouraging things to him.  I think his last week will be better.  As for me, I sustain you and know that you are called of God, that the prophecies made of our mission can and will be fulfilled if we do all that we can to bring the people to feel as we have felt, to see eye to eye as we have seen, and to know, even as we know, and the knowlede that we posess is not of men, but of God.  May the Lord bless you and keep you.  You, Sister Queiroz and the assistants are always in my prayers.        Our numbers this week are as follows;bapt conf......................0/0bapt markd....................4/2pesq na igr....................1liç c membro..................23novos..........................13endereços.....................28qualificar......................100%Lemb s dist....................91%Have a great week.  Love,            Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Happy Valentines day
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:28:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Happy Valentines dayFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 9 Feb 2009 14:56:10 +0000Dear Family    This week I did a fast and got our dedicatory prayer written out finally.  I felt relieved to have it done at last.  Now we need to choose a place to go and do the prayer.  If you would like, I can send you a copy of it later on (it may be a duzie to translate it though).  I did a division with Elder Grisham from mafra this week and we talked a little about the progress of the work.  He used to be my zone leader in Florianoplolis and I really respect him.  He requested to president to spend his last transfer in his favorited area as a district leader, so we have a "retired" zone leader in our zone.  As I talked with him, it became clear that we both know that in this mission it has been prophesied that we will baptize thousands and we have been thinking about the scripture in Alma 26:22 about the formula for having so many baptisms.  We both agreed that it is impossible to attain this goal just by knocking doors.  I read all of Acts on monday and tuesday and saw that the apostles had success baptizing and converting thousands because they taught in groups.  Acts 1-5 it says that they taught in the TEMPLE.  On his mission, Paul always started his tour of the city going to the SYNAGOGS, and when that wouldnt work (which times were few) he would go to the market to preach, or a school.  It says that he taught in a school for three years and the whole city became advised.  D&amp;C 68 starts off with a command for all elders called to the work; That they go from place to place, land to land preaching in the synagogs of the wicked, reazoning with them and expounding the scriptures unto them in accordanceto what the spirit directs them to say.  In alma 21, it says that the sons of mosiah had great success in their preaching in the synagogs.  So I am thinking that this week I will stop by a start up church in my area that Ive noticed from time to time and request a few moments to bear my testimony of the savior, read some scriptures to them and follow what the Spirit directs.  There are some elders that have gone to churches already, but it has not been a repeated process.  It was done mostly for the glory of men, and therefore it came to nothing.  However, if we go in with the intent to find someone in that church to be baptized, the Lord will bless us with miracles.  When I was in Tubarao, I did an interview with the District Leader for Criciuma(E Cornaby) and he said that the elders in Criciuma 2 were desanimated.  I told him to spend a couple of afternoons with the other elders and split up and knock a street each companionship with the intent of finding at least one good person report afterward.  Its one thing to knock doors of an entire street, and another to excercise faith in finding.  The same is applicable to teaching in a church.  Begin with the end in mind.          Elder Moody is doing alright.  He gets frustrated if we get home after 9:00 though.  This week he got frustrated about several things and told elder Hill.  So Elder Hill told me what was going on.  It was all news to me.  From time to time I notice that Elder Moody is not happy, so I ask if anything is wrong and he says no.  But after all that he has been having a good time and has been happier these last few days.           Our area is doing well and those two young women that came to enlish class have a high chance at being baptized.  After english class on saturday, the youth started to play volley ball and the two girls (Gabriella and Kristina) played too.  now they feel comfortable with the members and coming to church, so as soon as the elders on the other side start teaching them, we ll be on a roll.             we figured out how to find Vera (that mom that wont let her daughter be baptized yet) at her member cousins house on Sunday nights, So last night we stopped by, chatted a little and asked the member if we could leave a message(just like we did last week...) so we sang a childs prayer and taught hte first lesson.  Vera kind of sat off to the side and tried not to pay attention.  We invited the member and her familyl to bear their testimonies to each other and the spirit was REALLY strong.  But Vera still wasnt really paying attention, so at last, she just got up to leave with someone else, but I told her we werent finished yet. ## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao da Vit 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:29:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao da Vit 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 2 Feb 2009 14:05:09 +0000Elder AndrewsElder MoodyUnião da Vitória 1Zona União da Vitória.Dear President Queiroz,  These last few weeks my mind has been frequently reverted back to the beginning of my mission.  By far that was one of my favorite times on my mission;  I was learning the language and the only things I knew to talk about were the gospel and my testimony, I had alot of baptisms, and it seems my faith was stronger as left the MTC.  I realized I had more hope in finding people ready to be baptized, who were ready and elect.  So this week I spent a good amount of study time going through my study journals and reviewing lessons, inspirations and promptings during my stint at the MTC.  I must say, it is EXTREMELY profitable to keep your impressions noted in an organized manner.  I feel my faith increasing and I have a greater desire to bear testimony instead of preaching.  In the majority of my teaching situations I have also begun to ask myself "What would Jesus say to help them- how would he treat them?"  My faith increases and I am repenting daily- I seek not so much pardon from sin, but to be redeemed from my fallen nature and made a saint through the Atonement of Christ.         Elder Moody is very quiet, especially when he is tired, but I have noticed that as I listen to him bear testimony, I feel power.  I feel that he really does have a testimony and I am glad to see that I am not alone.  He has been really tired as of late, so I m going to see If we cant get done with our planning sessions earlier and maybe get an extra 1/2 hour of sleep at night for him.  Elder Hill likes talking, so sometimes it is dificult, but we ll manage.           Our area is doing well and on saturday in our english class someone came who heard the announcement on the radio and the class was a success in that we got two good adresses out of it- both for the other missionaries, but oh well.  I have been praying for the spirit to guide me and I have plead for the Lord to put in effect His promise that "I will go before your face; I will be on your right and your left and my spirit in your Heart..." and as I thought about it, I really ought to pay attention then.  If He is in front of me, He probably wants to lead, not just follow whereever we decide.  Adopting that perspective, I recognized alot of promptings to do contacts or teach in the streets.  We have an investigator who goes to church every week and goes to all activities but her mother wont let her get baptized.  We told the investigator, Silmara, to fast and that we would fast with her.  As I began the fast on Saturday afternoon, I was praying in the chapel.  As I prayed, I felt impressed to pray even more for her mother, beyond that her heart would be softened, but that she would also have a desire to be baptized.  Excercising hte priesthood, I invoked the presence of angels to be with her, to give her a manifestation and change her heart.  Yesterday we were at her cousins house( who is a member) and we decided to leave a message.  So we started reading 3Nephi 17 and afterward we sang "I wonder when He comes again".  As I bore my testimony after the song, I looked over my shoulder and saw Vera (Silmaras Mom).  I dont know when she arrived, but I continued to bear my testimony and then E. Moody bore his testimony as well.  I felt the assistance of angels as we taught.  On sunday we will have an FHE with them all and Silmara and her mother.  Lets see if we cant succeed in baptizing them both.  This week I was pondering the help which we are entitled to recieve from the other side of the veil.  Angels purposes are set forth in Moroni 7 31-36.  I would ask; do they want to help out with miracles when those with mouths do not open them?  The powers of heaven are excercised only as we courageoulsy use them in EXCEEDINGLY great faith.  I have to repent and use my resources.  I felt the prompting during zone conference to use the radio.  Its free on wednesdays and thursdays and besides, What do you think Ammon would do if he could get his hands on a radio?  Didnt Alma wish to have the voice of an angel to declare repentance to all the ends of the world?  Its time to get to work!         I really enjoyed zone conference, I learned alot and feel much more confident about the work we do.  This week after I read Sister Queiroz's message in the rede, I decided we souyld clean our apartment.  It took alot of work to bleach out Elder Wiricks name off mold in the wall, but we got it done and killed all the many spiders in our room too.  Our bedroom is my little sanctuary now.  I feel better.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/Conf.....................0/0bapt marc......................4/3pesq na igr.....................3liç com membro...............12novos...........................15endereços......................23lemb s dist.....................91%qualificar.......................100%Tenha uma otima semana e agradeço todo o teu trabalho.        Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao Da Vitoria 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:30:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao Da Vitoria 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 19 Jan 2009 14:53:44 +0000Elder AndrewsElder MoodyUniao da Vitoria1Uniao da vitoriaDear President Queiroz        The work in our area is going well, I am really surprised at how easy it is to talk to people here and get in their homes.  I have only been rejected maybe five times.  Whenever I mark down an adress, I mark on a scale of 1-10 what I think their receptivity and potential are, and I made a goal back in Tubarao to only contact 7-10s.  Here it seems like everybody is a 8-9!  This week when Elder Moody and I do our weekly planning session, we will put together a new system of adress "filtering".  I also talked with him as we were walking this week and he said he can usually tell if someone will get baptized or not based on their receptivity, their eyes, their movements etc., and I feel the same way.  You can usually tell if someone will follow or not, so we decided to just search out those who we can tell will have an attitude to follow.  we re going to plan that out tomorrow in our planning session as well.          Elder moody is a humble man and I am liking serving with him.  we are getting along fine and I try to compliment him on anything I can.  He is a good missionary.         This week we met with the branch mission leader and we got an english class planned out for saturdays and got it announced on the radio as well.  I think we will probably try to put on a short movie or message at the beginning of classes.  I think it will have a healthy turn out.  We also planned an integration night for the first week in Feb, and will start to train the ward missionaries how to get a family integrated.  We want to start focusing more on whole families for baptism.  I gave a 15 min. talk at the last minute in chuch yesterday, and it went well.  I talked about coming unto Christ, gaining a testimony and being converted.  I knew the key to gettingthe Branch presidents trust was to not say anything about it being a last minute talk, and just say I was happy to speak.  I think it worked.  As I left Tubarao, I felt that I was very distant with the ward leadership and did not really make a great difference in the ward, so I made a goal to help involve the members in the missionary work and help the ward grow in not only baptisms(Which I hope to have many here) but also in spirituality and unity as well.  I only have four months left of my mission and yesterday I felt a real desire to do a greater work than I have been doing, to perform the Lords work according to His will and in His way.  I will search out the elect and bring them to Zion and be healed of their sins and pains, and in the end, recieve Eternal Life.         In zone meeting on Friday we looked up a bunch of scriptures listed in the "Activity; Personal Study" part of Chapter four in Preach My Gospel after the section "The power of the Holy Ghost in Conversion" and we noticed a pattern in the process of what we feel in conversion; 1) we ponder on what had been spoken2) we hunger for further knowledge3) we pray and repent, we come to know for ourselves and we follow with full purpose of heart        I explained that the key to this happening is dependent on what we feel, and our level of conversion; And now, many have been brought to feel even as I have felt, and many have seen eye to eye even as I have seen, and do know even as I do know, and the knowledge that I have is of God(Alma 36: 21-28ish).  Ammon said that to him that REPENTETH, prays always and does good works, to him shall be granted success.  Repentance is not just repentance of sin, but is the act of giving up the natural man and delivering up our hearts to God.  We have to do that every day, just like Alma did, and retain our change of heart.            Our numbers this week were as follows;Bapt/Conf..........................0/0Bapt marked.......................3/2Pesq na igr..........................1liç c memb...........................3novos.................................19endereços............................48Lemb s disto.........................96%Qualifiar-se..........................100%I think we will do contacts like crazy and look for the elect who are ready to be baptized this week.  To be continued...       Thanks for all you do, we pray for you and are greatfull for your love and support,   Love Elder Andrews,

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Uniao Da Vitoria 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:30:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Uniao Da Vitoria 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 12 Jan 2009 16:44:17 +0000Elder AndrewsElder MoodyUniao da Vitoria IZona Uniao da VitoriaDear President Queiroz, This week when we went to the transfer meeting, I felt uplifted, inspired and that the Lord accepts my work in São Joao.  I always feel ready to work and repent at transfers.  Its a good feeling.  Elder Moody is doing alright and we get along just fine.  I really like my new area and I like the branch.  It seems alot stronger than many of the wards I have already served in.  My faith increases continually and I am grateful to be serving in the kindom of the Lord.    When I finally arrived in Uniao da Vitoria on Friday, I lost Elder Moody’s package that was sent to the office.  I felt really bad and know it must have been tough, but I think he forgave me.  From what I can see of E. Moody’s character, he should be an excellent missionary.  We have high hopes for our area.   Our first and second lunches in the area were with the branch president and the District President.  I want to take an active role in the branch and help it grow, so I managed to get myself invited to the executive commitee meeting on Wednesday and we spoke with the branch mission leader and got some ideas together for teaching families and how to train ward missionaries and have families integrate with another that is inactive and partmember for retention.  We also talked about getting on the radio and advertising an english class as well.  I think we are off to a good start with the leadership of the branch.  I love to find new people to teach and feel kind of like a detective searching out the people who the old missionaries were teaching.  The last entry in the area book was in November.  But I enjoy it. The busses were full on Wednesday night so we stayed the night with the assistants and staff.  As I studied in the morning, I pondered what Elder Pimentel had told me of dedicating areas and how he follows revelation in his procedures.  I felt the need to pray, so I went to another room to pray alone.  I found myself praying for success in my new area, for many things, and I felt the impression that I too should dedicate our areas.  So I started writeing down what needed to be done and start a fast to recieve revelation concerining the process.  I called Elder Eliakim and asked him to fast with me and seek revelation as well.  We know the majority of what we will do, but we are still wondering where we should do it and need to write out the dedicatory prayer.  We intend to carry out the dedication sometime this week with our companions and a member.  I also included your health in my personal fast.  I could not bear seeing you or Sis. Queiroz leaving due to health problems.  These last few weeks, I have felt the company and support of my Mother in my work and prayers.  I recommit myself to do the Lords work penitantly and walk with Him.  I will repent more fully and align my heart to His, that I may be an instrument in His hands.  Our numbers this week were low, seeing as we started working on Friday when I got here, and we are starting from nothing;Bapt/conf..................0/0Bapt marked..............0/0Pesq na igr.................0Liç com membro........1Novos.........................13Endereços..................18Lemb s dis..................91%Qualificar...................100%This week we will get much better and we will do our best to find the elect.  We love you and include you and Sister Queiroz in our prayers.  During the transfer meeting I remember when you said that you were trained to recieve missionaries but are not ready to let others leave.  I wished I could finish my mission out with you.  I thank you and Sister Queiroz for your example and love.  I sustain you and sustain our leader Jesus Christ.  I may not always be able to serve under you, but I will always be able to serve under Him.  Have a great week.                Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Salutations from me to you all...
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:30:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Salutations from me to you all...From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 26 Jan 2009 14:42:41 +0000Dear family,        This week was good and we discovered that walking from our area to our house can talke upwards of 87 minutes.  FYI Thats a long walk.  We did our first english class with limited success.  I think we will broadcast the anouncement this week again.  I dont know whats up with our house, but we see all kinds of wierd bugs here.  Elder Hill who works on the other side of the river with E. Eliakim is always putting things on my desk, such as a big knife with my name tag hanging on it, or a huge beetle in an upturned glass, etc.  The other night this wierd wood cockrouch flew into our house and just hung out until we kicked it out with a broom.  Its antenae were longer than it was and we learned that bugs can scream.  Unfortunately I didnt get a picture of that one, but I did get one of the big green beetle from four days ago.  It was actually kind of pretty.  Pretty but dumb, just like all beetles and june bugs.         My brown shoes that I ve been using for 20 months are just now getting a hole in the right sole.  Im surprised theyve lasted this long.  They still have another month and a half left in them though.  I took Charles advice and decided to think just a little bit about what I will do when I get home, and Im thinking of either doing something with law or physical therapy.  I guess Ill look into it more when I get home.           I give my ENTHUSUASTIC congradjulashtions to Charles on his engagement.  Im happy that I will be able to be there when He gets married.  Im pretty excited.  I got an email from Gma Woodbury this week and Im glad to know she is doing well.  It seems that she had a good holiday season.  Im glad Morgan is going teaching with the Elders.  I hope he learns to bear his testimony and listen to people.  I love to talk with people and see how I can help them and give them strentgh to overcome their fears and follow with faith.  Some people do, others dont, but when I see a person truly come unto Christ, Its worth all the pain.  What joy I have to look back on the past 20 months and remember the people who have been blessed through my service.  Its all worth it and more.  I hope you all have a great week and know that I love you and pray for you.         Love Joseph

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews Sao Joao
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:31:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews Sao JoaoFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 5 Jan 2009 19:54:15 +0000Elder AndrewsElder BrandãoSão JoãoZona TubarãoDear President Quieroz,   This week was na interesting one.  We did a division, had a holiday and went to Florianópolis as well for the conselho dos lideres de zona, which seeing as on both the divisions E Brandão went to the other área, so we really only got to work in our own área for three and a half days this week.  I think it shows a little in our numbers.  On Saturday, it rained cats and dogs and Wind got up to 80 kph.  My umbrella died in one of the gusts so I got a bunch of plastic bags and packed up my books and got a sweater on and we trudged on in the streets/rivers.  But it was OK.  This week I have learned alot, and I greatly enjoyed the conselho.  I feel uplifted and exited to do the work, which helped me out the next day during the rain.  As I look back on my time here, I can see that I lacked some of the charity that I usually have, and I would have liked to interact a little more in peoples lives and help them out in more ways.  So on Sunday I fasted that I might be able to have more charity in my next área, and really love and show love to the people.  All in all, I feel good as I leave Tubarão, and I feel that I really did do the best I could.  I like it here. When I told Elder Brandão that his companion would be Elder Dourado from his own city and stake, he lit up alot and laughed.  I think that they will do well together.  Elder Brandão hás really loosened up these last three months, not quite as much as I wanted, but I think he’ll be just fine.  This new transfer will be the first time I serve with another american, and I confess that Im rather nervous/excited.  I am definately optimistic though.    São joão is doing well.  We frequently play soccer with the Young men, and they like us, even though my mad soccer skills have earned me the nick name “train”.  We currently have more people marked for baptism in Capivari de Baixo than here in tubarão.  Thats kind of surprising and good.  Dilney who is responsible for Capivari was sad to see me go and Said some good things about me that make me feel better about the work we did here.  During the conselho on Friday when we gave an example of starting a first encounter, I testified of the healing power of Jesus Christ;  of how he suffered all our pains.  He knows what we pass through, and as I explained this and how our purpose is to help people to come unto Christ, “that they might be cured”, I remembered a woman we taught in Florianópolis named Salete, whose son was murdered and we helped her come unto Christ(in the end she was baptized) and was totally healed and even forgave the murderer, even though he got away Scott free and even lives in the house in front of her.  As I remembered this, it touched my heart.  I felt the same healing power of peace after my own Mother died, and for this, I knew and know how to help others to excercise faith in the Savior and come unto him and find rest unto their souls.  In every área that Ive passed I have left at least one person who is elect, who come what it may, they will serve the Lord.  I got a letter from one this last week who lives in Itajaí and whose house was inundated in the flood.  She quoted a bunch of scriptures and Said she was already in the book of Helaman in the Book of Mórmon.  She hás only had a Book of Mórmon for tem months.  I was pleased.  I love to see the fruit of my labors and how The Lord hás blessed me throughout my mission.  I know, from experience, that The Savior hás the power to heal our shattered souls, to bind up the broken hearted, to cleanse the repentant soul, and I know by the witness of the Holy Ghost that He lives.  I know He is our Savior and is the very Son of God.  I love Him.  I love to serve Him.   This week our numbers were as follows;Bapt/conf.................................0/0Bapt marked.............................6/3Pesq na igr................................7Liç c membro............................11Novos........................................14Endereços..................................12Lemb s disto..............................96%Qualificar..................................100%  Have  a great week and a happy new year.                    Love Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

I love you and am glad to hear that despite the bug going around up there, you are all doing well.  Last night we made four pizzas, and they turned out great.  I hope you all have a great week and I will write again on monday         Love, Joseph

## Subject: Fw: Glad tidings.
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:31:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Glad tidings.From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 5 Jan 2009 20:06:06 +0000Dear Family,  I am going to be transferred again on Wednesday to União da Vitória on the border of Santa Catarina and Paraná.  It will be interesting to leave the coast at last.  The furthest west of the coast I have ever been on my mission is forty miles.  The accent from paraná is hilarious.  I think Im going to have a fun time.  My Half companion(the other zone leader) is Elder Eliakim, who was my companion some seven or eight months ago in Florianópolis, and my official companion will be an american name E. Moody.  I hope his attitude dosnt reflect his name.  This will probably be my last área.  Today I finally broke down and bought a câmera.  I will send you some pictures next week or something.This week was na interesting one.  We did a division, had a holiday and went to Florianópolis as well for the conselho dos lideres de zona, and seeing as on both the divisions E Brandão went to the other área, we really only got to work in our own área for three and a half days this week.  I think it shows a little in our numbers.  On Saturday, it rained cats and dogs and Wind got up to 80 kph. This week I have learned alot, and I greatly enjoyed the conselho.  I feel uplifted and exited to do the work, which helped me out the next day during the rain. Elder Brandão hás really loosened up these last three months, not quite as much as I wanted, but I think he’ll be just fine. We frequently play soccer with the Young men, and they like us, even though my mad soccer skills have earned me the nick name “train”. He knows what we pass through, and as I explained this and how our purpose is to help people to come unto Christ, “that they might be cured”, I remembered a woman we taught in Florianópolis named Salete, whose son was murdered and we helped her come unto Christ(in the end she was baptized) and was totally healed and even forgave the murderer, even though he got away Scott free and even lives in the house in front of her. I know He is our Savior and is the very Son of God.  I love Him.  I love to serve Him.   Thank you all for your support and love.  It was good to talk to you on Christmas.  I will do my best to finish off the last four and a half months representing Jesus Christ to the people as much in His way as I can.  I love to serve in His kingdom.  What a glorious opportunity.  I love you all.    Love Elder AndrewsPs, I need to give the mission the stake presidents email and mailing adress as well as those of the bishop.  If you could send that to me, with a few pictures of mom and the family, Id appreciate it a ton.

## Subject: Fw: MERRY CHRISTMAS!!!!!
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:31:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: MERRY CHRISTMAS!!!!!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Wed, 24 Dec 2008 20:04:14 +0000Dear Family,          I am glad to hear everyone got to travel safely, it sounds pretty busy out there.  My half companion Elder Dewitt -the other zone leader- and I have been having some fun hunting cockroaches in his desk; its a yearly ritual down here, usually starting when the temperature gets above 95 degrees and continues through march.  One of the doorknobs in the house broke as well and refused disassemble, so we filmed E DeWitt break the door down.  The door frame was already somewhat damaged, so I suspect its not the first time this has happened.  I have discovered that longsleeve dress shirts can serve as good costume pieces for being a white ninja, arab, and many other things.  As you can all tell from these things, my mission is being very productive...         Being Christmas Eve, the brazilians usually have christmas supper at 1:00AM on the twenty fifth, and we are permitted to attend, but my companion and I opted to make our own dinner and sleep earlier and take advantage of the presidents permission to sleep in on christmas.  So I decided to make a pizza american style with a thick crust, the ever absent tomato sauce, never found on brazilian pizza, and a ton of mozzarella cheeze.  That is still on my schedule for tonight.  the ingredients were by no means cheap.          I look forward to talking to you all tomorrow, Ive been thinking about it all week.  I dont know if youll get this tonight or tommorow, but I hope you all have a merry christmas.  I love each one of you and pray for you every day.                 Love Joseph

## Subject: Fw: Happy Christmas...
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:32:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Happy Christmas...From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 15 Dec 2008 18:20:48 +0000           Dear Family,           This week was zone conference, and due to flooding in the north, we had seven of the tem zones of the mission there.  One hundred and ten missionaries together.  I havnt been with that many missionaries since the MTC!  We made a covenant with the Lord to have five baptisms for a Christmas to the Lord.  One of the things we agreed to do was loucuras(crazy things), like get up on the bus and preach and stuff like that.  I had a good week, conference was enjoyable and my following experiences were quite interresting.  After conference I went to Criciúma to do a baptismal interview and division.  It was me and Elder Cornaby.  We were comapnions in the MTC and it was good to see how much he hás grown.  I really miss serving with someone as humble and charitable as he is.  As we were waiting for the bus back to tubarão, we still had forty minutes and E Cornaby looked at me and Said, “vamos fazer uma loucura?”(shall we do something crazy?)  Well, we were in the bus station full of people, but I felt kind of nervous of how to go about preaching-what to say, how to start, etc- but I am a zone leader, so I felt like I had to be na example and at least pretend to be more determined.  If I couldnt do it, the rest of the zone wouldnt do it.  So we went out to one of the benches full of people, and Elder Cornaby stood there and started talking shyly with the same contact as we usally use with people.  No one really paid attention to him.  So we went inside, because I had no Idea what to do and I wanted to think up a way that we could do it more effectivly.  So we discussed how they must have done it anciently.  Get up and make some noise and seize some attention.  We Said a prayer and it came to my mind three scriptures; Amos 8:11-12, Mattew 5:6 and Matt 11:28-30.  Our new contact went somthing like this;   “Hey every body, we are representatives of Jesus Christ, and we have a quick message for you all.  In amos 8, the prophet amos spoke these words conscerning our days–then we read amos 8: 11-12- for centuries there have been people hungering and thirsting to know God, and have lived out their days searching for Him, but found it not, but the Lord also Said “blessed are those that hunger and thirst after righteousness, for they shall be filled” In mathew 11, Jesus Said, “comeunto me, all ye that are heavy laden and I shall give you rest..”(we read the rest of the scripture as well).  As representatives of Jesus Christ, our purpose is to help all people to come unto Christ, that their souls may be filled....”    After saying this we start getting adresses.  Afterward, Elder Cornaby looked at me with a smile and Said, “you know, Ive always wanted to do something like that, but I didnt know if we really could.”  I felt the same way.  We(this time E Brandão and I) did same thing on a bus ride here in tubarão.  I can say that it really gets peoples attention and the last time we did it, we got adresses from 50% of the people.  I am starting to wonder if we shouldnt do some baptismal invitations at the same time and add it into the end and just quote OurPurpose.  If we keep this up, we’ll have more adresses than we can contact.  We might as well see who really wants to come unto Christ instead of just getting a blessing.  I remember when we were in the MTC doing contacts.  We got five pass along cards to pass out on main street in São Paulo for two hours.  E. Cornaby and I were so nervous we cjouldnt hardly stop anyone.  I think we’ve changed alot.My companion is doing well aside from being sick for the last week.  As always, I am trying to help him speak out a little more. Our área is alright, though there are many people we teach who even after recieving an answer dont want to follow.  I got pretty down about it last night, after two great investigators in a row rejected the invitation to be baptized even though they knew it was true, but I remembered that Nephi(this being the one in third nephi) spoke so powerfully that no one could help but believe, and in the end, few followed.  It was the same with the priests of King Noah.  There is no way that they could not have believed Abinadi’s words. I really love being a missionary.  I want to do the best I possibly can.  I am glad that president told us to do some Loucuras.  I always felt that there could be a more effective way to go about doing missionary work than just knocking doors. I looked at the prices to call from here to the states, and its very expensive.  Its actually cheaper for you to call me than for the brazilians to call home just twelve ours away!  If you need to, you can take the money out of my personal account to pay for the phone call.  You can call me whenever you want, (only on Christmas of course) because  this number is my cell phone number.  I think last christmas you called me at 8 o clock your time and it was just about noon here.  I guess just dont call after six o clock your time.  To call me, the number is as follows;  011-55-48-8845-0183.  Thats 011-55-48-8845-0183.I love all of you and hope you all have a great Christmas vacation.Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: seasons greetings
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:32:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: seasons greetingsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 8 Dec 2008 16:30:44 +0000Dear family,  I hope Morgan had a good birth day.  Sixteen years old...  I remember those days.  That was the best time for me.  When I come home He’ll be driving and dating.  We’re going to have a blast...    This week I have been studying about the role of the Book of Mórmon in conversion and consequently I have taken my effort to re read the Book of Mórmon again seriously and not let a day go by without reading a chapter at least.  Reading in chronological order may not be the best way to seek light and knowledge, but it does increase perspective and help you find things easier as you familiarize yourself with where everything is located.    Elder Brandão is doing all right, though I want to see him take a more active and assertive manner in teaching.  Its hard because sometimes its just easier to do things myself instead of waiting for him to do something.  He is very quiet and dosnt give much input in study, teaching, planning what we will teach, etc.  I wonder if he will miss me or not when we are split up.  He is doing well though.   Capivari de Baixo is as always difficult to work during the afternoon.  But we are teaching a family that is very, very good.  When we gave a blessing three weeks ago, it went perfectly.  The second visit was during the leadership counsel, so I was in Floripa and it was two green elders teaching.  The next visit we retaught the first lesson, and I felt like they might fall.  But this week when we came back, we taught about the plan of salvation and the importance of following the Savior by faith, repentance, baptism and the gift of the Holy Ghost.  So I asked if they had any doubts or questions.  Terezinha, the mother, raised her hand and asked why baptism was so important, so we opened up to John 3;5 and explained that for them to get to the celestial kindom and have their family together, they would have to be baptized.  Sos he asked if her catholic baptism was valid.  I Said “você quer a resposta com açúcar ou sem açúcar?” (do you want the answer with sugar or without?) everbody laughed and she Said I could go ahead and just tell her, so I told her no.  When she asked why, I reminded her about the loss of authority with the death of the apostles, and then she started to say something but mid phrase she opened her eyes wide and Said “Oooh” as the connection clicked in her head.  From there, she told us of her search for the truth and I guess the rest will just be history.  Now we just need to get her husband to give up cachaça (an alcoholic drink that is pretty much 99.999999% alcohol) and we’ll be good.  We would be having a baptism this week, but it didnt work out with his work Schedule, so we moved the date to next Thursday.  This week as I Said a prayer before bed on Thursday, I was about to ask for the Lord to do something, but it occured to me that He dosnt ever really interfere and do that kind of work, like making someone go to church, read the book of mórmon, etc.  the answers to many of our prayers are what we and others do.  It is I that must help the people to do all this.  When the people follow my invitations to act, then and only then can the Lord do His part and let the spirit get in their hearts and make the cahnges.  I am glad to be a missionary and learn how to really get things done the Lord’s way through the grunt work and not just talking in front of a bunch of sypathisers in church.   I love you all and hope you have a great week.  We’ll be tlking to you here in a couple of weeks...                            Love, Joseph

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Sao Joao
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:33:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Sao JoaoFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 1 Dec 2008 16:13:47 +0000Elder AndrewsElder BrandãoSão JoãoZona TubarãoDear President Queiroz,  This week we put together our baptismal goals for december with the covenant of which we recieved instrucions last week.  I asked Elder Brandão what number he thought would be good, and he Said seven.  Thats alot for one month, and its rather ambitious, so I wanted to make sure he wasnt just popping out a high number to show bravado, so I asked him what he thinks we need to do to accomplish it.  He Said we just have to find two families and another person.  So we put our goal down and put out what we need to do to succeed.  It was a good experience.  One of those families we found last Sunday was elect.  It was hard to get a hold of them all together to teach the restoration, and we did finally get them together on Saturday night at nine o clock at night.  As I looked at my watch I wondered if we should just mark another day and run home, but I didnt want to lose the chance to teach the lesson.  I didnt know what to do and nothing came to mind of what we could teach them so I decided to just say a prayer and take it from there.  During the prayer I felt as though we could go ahead and teach the lesson.  So we did and marked their baptism for the twentieth because they couldnt make it to church on Sunday this week.  When I Said the date, the husband (Sidney) asked we what time the baptismal meeting would start, so that he could ask off work.  Wow.  We managed to get a ride home from some members to whom we expressed ALOT of thanks.  We are trying to do all that is possible to have a good follow up with our good investigators.  One of our agreements with the Lord is that we will teach at least 30 lessons a week, and we Just barely managed to do it on Sunday.  On Wednesday we went up to Capivari de Baixo and during the evening, I  had a strong feeling;  “Go find somebody”.  So instead of trying to teach someone that just wont progress, we went on a contacting frenzy.  I dont know what it was, but I felt an absolute need to find somebody, and not justa any body, but someone that was needing us and our message.  I felt my testimony burning within me and I felt a desire to talk to what ever soul entered our path.  So I did.  It was already about the time that the bus passes to go back to tubarão, and I even saw a bus coming by,  and was tempted to get on, but I felt the impression, “just one more person”, so we kept going and found a house with a senhora and her daughter, both of which are single and I felt that they were needing the message, so in preparation for the blessing, I focused alot on how our families can be together forever.  I dont know if they are divorced or widows or what, but I guess we’ll see when we go back on this Wednesday.  On Thursday, we found a widow who is probably about 50 and who had lost her husband some six years ago.  As I gave a blessing, I felt her husbands presence, and that he wanted very much to have his work done.  I didnt say anything about this to her naturally, but I did say to my companion after wards that I thought that her husband wanted her to accept the Gospel.  The next time we went there, we taught the second lesson with a sister from the ward who helped out alot.  I told the woman –Terezinha- that if she wanted to have her family together again, she should be baptized, and her answer was a little unsure, especially due to her past negative experiences going  to assembléia with her son.  She Said that after going there she cant sleep at night and feels flat out bad because they never say good things there.  So we will plan a FHE with the sisters family and try to integrate her and teach her the 1st lesson.  I wont let her go without first giving alot of exhortatinos and talking aobut the consequences of not following the Savior.  Some Elders think that since people have agency they can just choose what theyll do.  Thats true, but at the last day, theyre going to look at me during judgment and tell me you idiot, you just let me say no and walk away?!  Why didnt you tell me   this would happen?”  Sure we told them and taught them, and sure maybe we rid our garments of their blood, but our job isnt to rid our garments of their blood and put it on theirs.  It  needs to be on the Saviors garments.  Thats our mission.  So Its worth it to exhort, burn and advise.  All in all, we had a good week.    Elder Brandão has really started to loosen up now and as we put our goals togther We got to feel more comfortable talking to each other about how we can improve.  He is finally starting to give input and critique, instead of just following quietly and even interrupts and makes additions to what I say in lessons to bear testimony and teach.  I feel so much better now.  I like to be equals with my companions and grow together.   Our áreas are going well, though there seems to be some issues about lunches in Capivari.  Were getting it figured out though.  I have studied alot about conversion and the differences between testimony and conversion.  The apostle Peter had a testimony, revealed by the Holy Ghost that Jesus was the Christ the Son of the living God, yet the Savior Said to him, “when thou art converted strengthen thy brethren.  Conversion, or spiritual rebirth is not permanant.  Just as every being Born into this world needs nourishment three times a day for it to be healthy and live, every person spiritually re Born needs to have spiritual nourishment.  We can lose our conversion through sin, and our spiritual rebirth can be lost through spiritual death and we can no longer walk in the “newness of life”.  I discovered this week that there are two ways in which we may lose our conversion;  Spiritual poison,-sin- which induces spiritual death immediatly, and spritual malnutrition, which is a gradual and painful process.  Those who “hunger and thirst after righteousness shall be filled”, and nutrifying their souls through obedience to the ordinances of the gospel, they shall bel ed to the Fount of all righteousness.  Thank goodness for repentance.  I love the gospel and love the Lord.  What a blessing it is to be His servant. Our numbers this week were as follows;Bapt/conf................................0/0Bapt mark...............................7/4Pesq na igr...............................5Liç c memb.............................13Novos.......................................25Endereços................................44Lemb se dist............................91%Qualificar.................................100%Have na excellent week and thank you for all you do to help us.  You are in our prayersLove, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: E ai, querida familia...
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:33:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: E ai, querida familia...From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 24 Nov 2008 17:08:45 +0000Well Dad,    I’m going to have to decline on your invitation to come out and visit for thanksgiving.  Its looking like its not going to be an option for me.  However, maybe I can plan on coming out for memorial day or something...   Heres an update on weather in Santa Catarina, Brazil;  RAIN  It hás rained non stop for the last eternity.  Someone asked me this week if we get off when it rained.  I told them that if we did, we would have had the whole last month off without having to work one single day.  The week passed by well enough.  The rain slowed down our progress a little bit, along with the rest of the zone, but the zone had several baptisms to account for.  So that was good.  During the Leadership Counsel I learned a great deal, and I got some ideas to help me and my companion work better together.  Elder DeWitt and I spent the majority of Saturday traveling to Criciúma to give a zone meeting and even further south to Araranguá for a baptismal interview.  As a result of this combined with the rain, our numbers suffered.  On Saturday night, as we were planning, I looked at the Schedule for Sunday afternoon and felt like we should try to find some new people and knock some doors in São João, and it was almost as if I could picture the exact área in which we needed to knock.  So last night we turned up a little alley that ive noticed in the past and knocked some doors.  The first family that we gave a blesing tôo there was fantastic.  They were chock full of questions about why there exist so many churches and already know one of the good members of the ward here.  I saw that they had a guitar, so I asked if I could sing a hymn, to which they Said yes.  I played and sang “Onde há Amor” –where love is there God is also- and when I finished one of the elderly ladies was in tears already, and we gave the blessing.  It was good.  They told us that this was exactly what they were needing and God had sent us at the right moment.  As they Said that, I remembered how I had felt like we needed to go there that day.  We found yet another Young family who upon being asked if they’d like to recieve a blessing responded with a firm yes.  Upon asking them that if Jesus Christ showed them the way to follow to have their family together in eternity, if He showed them would they follow? They Said yes firmly and without hesitation.  And upon telling them about a mesage that would show them how to have the feelings of the spirit forever they Said yes.  Every time they Said it, you could tell they really meant it.   My companion is doing fine and I am trying to help him grow and teach better.  I told him how I felt in the beginning of my mission about desiring to bear testimony of everything and that whenever he wanted, he could bump me and speak up.  He dosnt really participate a whole lot.  When thinking about it, when we come out of the MTC and hearing about how we shouldnt memorize lessons, we still have the memorized mentality of teaching principles and switching off every so many parts with a memorized pattern.  Our message is baisically broken down into four parts though; 1st the plan of Salvation and thats the “Why” to everything; 2nd how we follow Jesus Christ, this being the Gospel of Jesus Christ with faith, repentance baptism and recieving the gift of the Holy Ghost, and 4th what the commandments of God are.  You can easily fit all four of those in any given lesson with the focus being on what ever the needs of the investigator are.  I’m really starting to like resolving people’s concerns or doubts.  I am trying to teach E. Brandão how to do it tôo.  We’ll see how well I succeed.     My half companion (the other zone leader who lives with us) E. DeWitt is from Arizona and pretty much hás convinced me to go out and visit him in Gilbert when I come home.  I guess that Works out just perfectly seeing Rebecca and Jason live out there in AZ tôo.  Well I hope all continues well and you dont get as much rain as we are getting down here.  Theres alot of flooding and land slides going on here.                      Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Sao Joao
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:34:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Sao JoaoFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 17 Nov 2008 14:52:23 +0000Elder AndrewsElder BrandãoBairro São JoãoZona TubarãoDear President Queiroz,  Our zone seemed to suffer a little numbers wise this week as we spent a day in Florianópolis, spending a day trying to get the baptismal font filled and Saturday was a holiday with lots of sun.  I think the majority of the people we wanted to teach were at the beach.  Its kind of funny how we pray for the rain to go away and when it gets sunny again, we pray for rain.  My companion is starting to open up a little bit and I am finally starting to understand his slangs from Bahia.  All my companions for the last year of my mission have been from São Paulo, so I think Ive only gotten accostomed to hear souther and Paulista slangs.  Elder Brandão is also starting to give a little more of his opinion on how we should work, so I am starting to really like working with him.  Elder Brough once told me that companionship makes all the difference.  It does.  As we were in the baptism of one of our investigators this week, E. Brandão looked at me and whispered “This makes number two!”  Up until then, I hadnt really thought much about how he was feeling about his success in his mission.  I’ve just been concentrating on getting more baptisms in general and had not even stopped to think of how many baptisms he already hás.  He told me that every one Said that his mission would be spent in the mall, or playing around or something, because no one baptizes around here.  As he told me, he gave a laugh.  Im glad that even though as a trainer I havnt gotten the highest numbers, I have shown him that we can focus on and achieve baptisms.  If all góes according to plan, we should have another baptism this Saturday for Capivari de Baixo.  This Saturday, I asked E. Brandão what he thought of the day (not alot had happened that day) and he Said he thinks its great that we are getting baptisms and having success, but we can do much, much more.  So I repented and decided to do much, much more.  Yesterday we went to Capivari for the afternoon and still had an appointment in Tubarão, so the bus Schedule was a little tight.  We had arranged for a lesson to take place in a members house, but the investigator –the one who is supposed to be baptized on Saturday- wasnt home, so that fell through.  So we went to catch the bus and while we were walking, the phone rang and it was the member calling to say that the investigator had arrived and she was marking for us to come back on Wednesday.  Right after I hung up the phone, I heard my companion say “there góes the bus” and start to laugh.  It would be another half na hour for another bus to come by and he Said that it didnt leave time for us to really get anything done but wait at the bus stop.  I told him “oh yeah?” and called up the sister and asked for her to keep the investigator there and wait for us.  So we gave a revised lesson on the restoration and got out of there with a tem minute walk to the bus stop ahead and five minutes to get there.  So I prayed.  And I prayed.  And I remembered Elder Ellis talk about our part, and walked faster.  And faster.  I prayed first for us to get the bus.  Then I prayed that the bus would be just slow enough for us to get there on time.  And then I prayed for us to be able to walk fast enough to get there on time.  As we aproached the intersection where we would turn to get to the bus stop –and consequently where the bus would pass by- I felt like I needed to go faster.  So I walked faster, and then I felt like I needed to run, so I ran to the intersection, and just as I got there to my right the bus was showing up, so I waved for it to stop, but it just went by, and so we ran like there was no tomorrow to get to the bus stop.  If we had been any slower, even by one second, we would have missed the bus and lost the appointment.  We got the bus, and consequently got to our teaching appointment on time.  There was nobody home.  But thats ok because  we found someone else who will probably get baptized.  As I was catching my breath on the bus, I Said a prayer of gratiutude for the answered prayers.  I was sure that there was someone laughing with us up there at our little adventure and lesson on how to “Pedir”, and “Lutar” for an answer.  We repented of running and risking injuries, so dont worry.   I enjoyed Elder Ellis’ visit and learned alot and we are trying to seek out more revelation.  It isnt easy, but I think it is worth it.  This week wasnt a week to be proud of with numbers, but next week should be better.  Our numbers this week are as follows:Bapt/conf..........................1/1Bapt marcados..................7/4Pesq na reunião.................4Liç c membro....................13Novos pesq........................18Endereços..........................17Lemb s dist........................96%Qualificar..........................100%Thank you for all you do.  We love you and pray for you.  Have an excellent week.

## Subject: Fw: Joy be unto you, o andrews family; a letter from Joseph
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:34:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Joy be unto you, o andrews family; a letter from JosephFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 10 Nov 2008 16:21:56 +0000Dear Family,   This morning, after a long night of troubled sleep due to mosquitos, I decided to go on a mad mosquito hunt.  Armed with an electric fan and a flip flop sandal, I got the air moving under beds and desks where they like to hide out during the day and discovered that there exists an abundance of mosquitos in Brasil.  The casualties among the enemies were over fourteen.  And that was just in our room.  Tonight we will close the door and Windows and sleep in perfect peace... Im hearing all kinds of different input from everyone about Obama.  The brazilians all worship him, mostly because the medias standpoint is based only on the sypathisers of the democrats.  I practically never found out who was running against him.    I got to do a division this week with the Elders from Criciúma and it was a blast.  The district leader down there is Elder Cornaby, my companion from the MTC, so it was good to see how much he hás grown.  I got to watch him give a district meeting and it was good to see how much he hás matured since being in the field.  I remember our first morning as missionaries, as we got off the plane and went into the MTC in São Paulo.  There were so many cool and prepared looking missionaries that I thought it would be cool to be companions with.  When they were calling out he companions, and they Said Elder Andrews and Elder Cornaby, I looked at him; he had the look of a child from primary in shock at being a missionary, open mouthed and smiling.  I thought “Oh no.  Its going to be a looooong 62 days...”  I love E. Cornaby.  He is perfectly humble and hás perfect charity.  I also got to eat lunch at one of my converts form Criciúmas house.  It was a good division.   This week I tried to get two people who had almost been baptized a couple of times this last year to get baptized, but it didnt work.  As we taught them, the spirit wasnt as strong as I had intended it to be, so they didnt want to change or accept the invitation.  The next day we went to another investigators house who we didnt succeed in following up on and I didnt feel anthing, so I started to get a little down and lose confidence.  So we stoppeed by a members house so I could pray and think of what we could do next.  We left not knowing what to do, so I figured we should just knock doors.  I remembered what president Queiroz told me in his reply to my email last week about trusting in the Lord and the new techniques and so we pressed on and found three families to start teaching, one of which we marked to visit today to teach the first lesson.  Its been a while since I got a good feeling about the people we bless and I felt MUCH better upon leaving.  The power of the priesthood is real and helps us to bring hte spirit.   My companion is doing well, I am trying to think of how I can help him to grow and to trust in him more.  Sometimes I want to just hear his testimony and see if he feels what he says, but Ill just wait.  He is a very closed person, and I hope to be able to help him open up a little bit.  I will work on communicating with him a little more as we go on this week. Interresting things are happening as we continue to go to Capivari de Baixo.  People are giving us plenty of refferences and we are doing our best to contact them.  I need to get a hold of some investigators and get a baptismal date marked.  As always, following up remains the all time champion of obstacles in our work.  I have been wanting to meet with the bishop in São João and present a plan in regards to this involving ward missionaries inviting small groups of investigators to be taught simple priciples such as faith repentance and baptism.  I looked at the examples of Peters 3000 converts, Almas 204, Ammons 14000, King benjamins entire people, and of the 2500 of the Savior in bountiful.  Those who feel the spirit together feel unity, hence the importance of spiritual activities in a families every day life.  In the five cases listed above, the people more or less had “all things in common”.  If I can succeed in getting ward missionaries to give small lessons in their own homes and in the homes of investigators, we can succeed in getting more people in church and to progress together as well as caring for one another.  This would involve having a firm ward mission leader to give training and alot of work from members.  All this would go in as formatted in Almas plans listed in Mosiah 18, seeing as he too had serious obstacles with following up(if he came into town, he was toast).  People had to get together more than once a week(the appointed day) “as much as it were possible”.    We managed to mark six more baptisms this week and four of them have a possibility of being baptized in the next two or three weeks.  Ill have to break my back over getting that done, but Im more or less absolutley positive itll be worth it.  I remember when I turned sênior in february, and how I focused on finding people to teach and fill up our days.  I succeeded.  It was a bad week if we had less than thirty five new investigators and forty lessons with a member present, or less than fourteen people in church.  We only baptized four people though.  Im focusing more now on who we can baptize now rather than who we can teach and at least for now, it seems that the future is smiling brightly before us.  We will have a baptism on thrusday and if we work our cards right and actually manage to get in the desired follow ups, one more towards the end of the week.  We’ll see.     I love each of you and I pray for your saftey and well being.  Have a good week.        Love Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Behold, an epistle from me to you
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:34:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Behold, an epistle from me to youFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 17 Nov 2008 15:05:11 +0000Dear family, Saturday marks one year and a half as a missionary and it is kind of scary.  Im really liking to be a missionary.  Life is really quite simple, if not easy.  And I love to do what I do.  I love to excercise the priesthood and see its effects in others lives.  Our zone seemed to suffer a little numbers wise this week as we spent a day in Florianópolis, spending a day trying to get the baptismal font filled and Saturday was a holiday with lots of sun.  I think the majority of the people we wanted to teach were at the beach.  Its kind of funny how we pray for the rain to go away and when it gets sunny again, we pray for rain.  My companion is starting to open up a little bit and I am finally starting to understand his slangs from Bahia.  All my companions for the last year of my mission have been from São Paulo, so I think Ive only gotten accostomed to hear souther and Paulista slangs.  Elder Brandão is also starting to give a little more of his opinion on how we should work, so I am starting to really like working with him.  Elder Brough –an old buddy from the MTC- once told me that companionship makes all the difference.  It does.  As we were in the baptism of one of our investigators this week, E. Brandão looked at me and whispered “This makes number two!”  Up until then, I hadnt really thought much about how he was feeling about his success in his mission.  I’ve just been concentrating on getting more baptisms in general and had not even stopped to think of how many baptisms he already hás.  He told me that every one Said that his mission would be spent in the mall, or playing around or something, because no one baptizes around here.  As he told me, he gave a laugh.  Im glad that even though as a trainer I havnt gotten the highest numbers, I have shown him that we can focus on and achieve baptisms.  If all góes according to plan, we should have another baptism this Saturday for Capivari de Baixo.  This Saturday, I asked E. Brandão what he thought of the day (not alot had happened that day) and he Said he thinks its great that we are getting baptisms and having success, but we can do much, much more.  So I repented and decided to do much, much more.  Yesterday we went to Capivari for the afternoon and still had an appointment in Tubarão, so the bus Schedule was a little tight.  We had arranged for a lesson to take place in a members house, but the investigator –the one who is supposed to be baptized on Saturday- wasnt home, so that fell through.  So we went to catch the bus and while we were walking, the phone rang and it was the member calling to say that the investigator had arrived and she was marking for us to come back on Wednesday.  Right after I hung up the phone, I heard my companion say “there goes the bus” and start to laugh.  It would be another half na hour for another bus to come by and he Said that it didnt leave time for us to really get anything done but wait at the bus stop.  I told him “oh yeah?” and called up the sister and asked for her to keep the investigator there and wait for us.  So we gave a revised lesson on the restoration and got out of there with a tem minute walk to the bus stop ahead and five minutes to get there.  So I prayed.  And I prayed.  And I remembered Elder Ellis talk about our part, and walked faster.  And faster.  I prayed first for us to get the bus.  Then I prayed that the bus would be just slow enough for us to get there on time.  And then I prayed for us to be able to walk fast enough to get there on time.  As we aproached the intersection where we would turn to get to the bus stop –and consequently where the bus would pass by- I felt like I needed to go faster.  So I walked faster, and then I felt like I needed to run, so I ran to the intersection, and just as I got there to my right the bus was showing up, so I waved for it to stop, but it just went by, and so we ran like there was no tomorrow to get to the bus stop.  If we had been any slower, even by one second, we would have missed the bus and lost the appointment.  We got the bus, and consequently got to our teaching appointment on time.  There was nobody home.  But thats ok because  we found someone else who will probably get baptized.  As I was catching my breath on the bus, I Said a prayer of gratiutude for the answered prayers.  I was sure that there was someone laughing with us up there at our little adventure and lesson on how to “ask”, and “fight” for an answer.  We repented of running and risking injuries, so dont worry.     This week Elder Stanley G Ellis of the seventy toured our mission.  I enjoyed Elder Ellis’ visit and learned alot and we are trying to seek out more revelation.  It isnt easy, but I think it is worth it.  Im not sure if thanksgiving is this week or next week, but I hope it góes well for you.  I cant be there to eat a french silk pie, but there is a wonderful thing in the church called Proxy.  If one of you could eat a piece in my name, Id really apreciate it.  Have an good week.                                     Love Joseph

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Sao Joao
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:35:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Sao JoaoFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 3 Nov 2008 15:51:03 +0000Elder AndrewsElder BrandãoBairro São JoãoZona Tubarão  Well President, we finally managed to get a baptism down here.  After my fast last week, I had been feeling a little more optomistic, but as the week slowly passed by, I got a little stressed for lack of being able to contact and follow up with some of our investigators, and on Thursday we went up to Capivari to keep some appointments and then hurry back to tubarão to teach a family.  All of our appointments fell through and it turrned out to be a waste of time and money for passage.  As we just barely caught the bus to get back I was feeling kind of down and I thought that the family we were on our way to visit who is inactive ando n the way to activity again would want to wait to baptize their daughter untill the dad was able to do it and it would probably take a long time, so I was a little down hearted.  So I Said a prayer and asked for the baptisms I have been requesting and working to get for the last transfer.  We got to the familys house and they Said they wanted to baptize their 10 year old daughter on Friday.  That was a surprize, but we threw the baptism together and prepared everything in a ridiculously short amount of time and it turned out very well.  The Lord answers our prayers, even if it is in ways unsought.  My companion is doing alright.  He seems to be a little more shy about doing contacts and taking course in teaching, so Im going to put a little more pressure on him and invite him to plan out how he can help the investigators make and keep commitments.  He started to say some things about the United States that were less than positive to say the least and I got a little defensive.  I told him that if he wants to have success in the mission, he should never say anything bad about the place from where his companion is from.  I have already had a companion that just talked badly about the states to try to beat me into submission and though I tried to overcome my pride and just let it go by, it just put animosity between us.  It really had a negative effect on us both and especially on our work.  So I warned my compmanion about that for the future.  He is a good missionary and I need to think of how I can help him leearn all that he should know and do.  Our personalities are quite different, but we can make it if I plan out how I can help him in any way. We went to the cemetery yesterday to find new people and at first I was having limited success in getting poeples adresses, until I figured out that if, upon mentioning eternal families I asked them if they wanted to be with their families forever, they Said yes and we could offer the opportunity to them with a message and a blessing.  We got quite a few adresses as well as the others in our zone.  At this point, the hardest part of our work and the greatest hinderance to our succes is in a lack of follow ups.  I have been thinking of implementing a plan (this being especially neccessary seeing our adoption of Capivari) in which the ward missionaries and even perhaps other investigators take care of investigators and help each other progress.  When poeple feel the Spirit together, they feel charity for each other, hence the commandment to meet together oft and even more importantly the importance of seeking the spirit as a family.  Im going to have to plan that out in our weekly planning session. This week I went to church in Capivari and got to bless the sacrament.  It brought back the memories of when I was a priest and blessed the sacrament.  I love to do it, and act in the name of the Savior.  Truly, when we go to church seeking to feel the spirit of God, we shal ever surely find it.  I am ever so greatful to be a member of the church of Jesus Christ and have the opportunity to hold His Priesthood.our numbers this week are as follows; bat/conf.............................1/1 bat marcado........................8/1 pesq na reuniao sac...............4 liç com membro....................10 outras liç................................11 endereços................................31 novos......................................19 qualificar............................100% Lembre se disto....................86%I think we probably had a few other people in church that are not members that Elder Brandão didnt know wernt members.  We have a possibility of baptizing one or two people this week and maybe several more here in the next three weeks.  We love you and thank you for all that you do to help us have success.  Have a great week.

## Subject: Fw: TOP SECRET- update from Tubarao (the shark)
