[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: TOP SECRET- update from Tubarao (the shark)From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 3 Nov 2008 16:09:26 +0000Dear family, we finally managed to get a baptism down here.  Its my first baptism since april.  After my fast last week, I had been feeling a little more optomistic, but as the week slowly passed by, I got a little stressed for lack of being able to contact and follow up with some of our investigators, and on Thursday we went up to Capivari to keep some appointments and then hurry back to tubarão to teach a family.  All of our appointments fell through and it turrned out to be a waste of time and money for passage.  As we just barely caught the bus to get back I was feeling kind of down and I thought that the family we were on our way to visit who is inactive ando n the way to activity again would want to wait to baptize their daughter untill the dad was able to do it and it would probably take a long time, so I was a little down hearted.  So I Said a prayer and asked for the baptisms I have been requesting and working to get for the last transfer.  We got to the familys house and they Said they wanted to baptize their 10 year old daughter on Friday.  That was a surprize, but we threw the baptism together and prepared everything in a ridiculously short amount of time and it turned out very well.  The Lord answers our prayers, even if it is in ways unsought.     We went to the cemetery yesterday to find new people and at first I was having limited success in getting poeples adresses, until I figured out that if, upon mentioning eternal families I asked them if they wanted to be with their families forever, they Said yes and we could offer the opportunity to them with a message and a blessing.  We got quite a few adresses as well as the others in our zone.  At this point, the hardest part of our work and the greatest hinderance to our succes is in a lack of follow ups.  I have been thinking of implementing a plan (this being especially neccessary seeing our adoption of Capivari) in which the ward missionaries and even perhaps other investigators take care of investigators and help each other progress. Truly, when we go to church seeking to feel the spirit of God, we shal ever surely find it. Well Dad, President Queiroz hás been putting the heat on the zone leaders to start baptizing or else...  So I was thinking about this baptism and how perhaps we could maybe turn it into two if we played our cards right, so when president called this week after getting back from a traing with Elder Scott, I took advantage to ask him what he thought.  He told me that he would leave it up to me to decide, because “if you cant learn to make your own decisions, youll never learn to be a good leader.  You guys have the keys, so Ill just sustain whatever you and your companion decide to do.  But dont worry Elder Andrews, if I disagree, Ill just boot you down to Junior Companion again...”  to which he started to laugh.  I told him thanks for the reassurance.  I like our president and I am glad to be serving under him.  I hope your week góes well and remember that I love all of you.  I really miss my nieces adn nephews too.                              Love Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Happy Haloween!
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:35:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Happy Haloween!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 27 Oct 2008 14:01:06 +0000Dear family,       This week was a week in which I could grow, learn, excercise more faith and see the hand of the Lord in our work.  At the beginning of the transfer, I did a fast on fast sunday and requested of the Lord to let me have five baptisms this transfer.  So I put a list together of people that have potencial to be baptized or that were set to be baptized during the transfer.  We had a baptism set up for last saturday, but it fell through when the boys father wouldnt let him be baptized.  His family is inactive and said that they didnt think he was prepared sufficiently.  A bunch of other plans seemed to be falling through as well, and so I did a fast yesterday to be able to succeed with my goal of baptisms.  Two hours after starting the fast, we convinced Rodrigo, the father of the boy whose baptism fell through, to let his son be baptized and start coming back to church.  Yesterday I went to church in Capivari de Baixo and left my companion to take care of our ward.  I felt that probably he wouldnt be able to count all of the investigators in church because he doesnt know them all, but oh well.  When I got to the branch in Capivari with irmao Dilney, I recieved three references and a request to visit a less active family who wants to baptize their ten year old son.  When I got back, Elder Brandao said that three people went to church who said that they want to be baptized, people that I had never even met before.  After I broke my fast, I kind of got some kind of determination to follow through with people to help them keep their commitments to be baptized.  The first time I trained, we had ridiculously high numbers and I thought we were having success, but in retrospect, we just managed to teach a bunch of people while only baptizing four in two transfers.  Now, when I mark baptisms, I have a sincere desire and a determiniation to help the people get baptized.  Upon conversing with my companion, weve decided to mark baptisms in two weeks to help us and our investigators focus.  Alot of the time we just mark baptisms for numbers, knowing that probably the people wont really get baptized on the appointed date.  But now I want to help people gain a testimony and act on it getting baptized.  All in all the fast helped me out.        My companion is doing well and yesterday I let him take some of the harder parts of teaching the first lesson and I must say, he did an excellent job.  He is opening up little by little, and is starting to give input on how we can improve, or especially me, but thats OK, because I can see that he is willing to open up a little.  He seems to be doing all right with the rules, and never asks questions, so I just have to guess what he might need help with.  He'll loosen up one of these days.         Our area is doing well and the members trust us and like to help us out when they can.  Capivari is doing alot better now with a new person responsible for the branch.  Irmao Dilney is an outstanding leader and is helping to tie up loose ends and get all the people reactivated.  His wife is also a returned missionary so she is quite capable to help out in the branch as well.  I think there would be no problem in sending a couple of missionaries there.  The members are giving references and the people there are good people.        That sounds pretty funny about wearing mis-matching shoes.  I suppose it would be even worse if one were wing tipped and the other capped.  I dont know if there was any dancing at the reception, but if someone cracked a joke, at least you could say you dont have two left feet...          There was only one day in the last two weeks that we saw the sun; it just rained, and rained, and rained, and rained,and rained, and rained, and rained,and rained, and rained, and rained,and rained, and rained, and rained....  We had our interviews with President Queiroz this week and it went well.  I suppose theres not really a whole lot to tell about this week.        Im glad to hear that Paul Paul is going on a mission to South America, we'll be more or less close for five months...        I love you all and hope you have a sumamente otimo semana, ate que voces tenham alegria infinita por causa de comer tanto doce!              Love Joseph

## Subject: Fw: Helloooooo!!!
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:36:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Helloooooo!!!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 13 Oct 2008 19:31:25 +0000Dear Family  We are having interresting experiences as we continue to work in Capivari de Baixo (the área that was closed and is now part of our área) and we are learning how to be better at the work which we do.  We went up to Capivari this Wednesday and found several people which were willing to be baptized.  We ate lunch at the relief society presidents house and she gave us some referrals, one of which we didnt succeed in getting into that day, but we went to the other one who góes to Assembly of God, who hás lost several of her children over the years (she is in her sixties) and we asked her if she wanted to be with her family again forever.  She Said yes.  So we asked her if she had faith in Jesus Christ.  She Said yes.  So we gave her a blesing and she felt the spirit and was even crying afterward and then we asked if she would give her tv to have her family again forever, to which she responded afirmativly as well as the questions if she would give her car, or house etc.  So we told her that Jesus Christ wants none of that, but that He wants her to be baptized.  She Said to us that she was already baptized to which we Said that we would explain later, but we wanted to know if she would follow the feelings she was feeling by the spirit.  And she accepted.  We also found an alcoholic woman who apparently had recieved the elders a long Time ago but never decided to change.  We gave her a blessing and gave her the invitation to act upon her feeling of the Holy Ghost and be baptized giving up her drinking and she Said she would and that it was time to change.  We could see the sincerity of what she Said in her eyes and marked the baptism for Sunday.  When we got back on Saturday, she had completly given up drinking even though her ex-husband gave her 40R$ for alcohol.  We found out that irmã Lucia, the president of the relief society who was with us when we gave the blessing and baptismal invitation had visited her four times over the weekend and that Meri, the investigator was excited and looking forward to her baptism.  Now she also hás to stop smoking, but she is progressing.  It was good to see that the members want ot help out.  After we got out of the house and blessing, irmã Lucia started asking how we could baptize her husband and this person or that and she was REALLY enthusiastic about the way we do our work.  I think taking the missionaries out of Capivari was a good thing and is helping the members value the missionary work and being a member as well.  Here in a couple of weeks it should be reopening again.  Elder Silva and I have enjoyed this transfer as we both have learned and grown together.  Im going to get to train again while continuing as a zone leader.  President Queiroz is doing some drastic changes and hás decided the age of every body training is over so only the good missionaries will train, and more than once tôo.  He also Said that if the zone leaders dont start baptizing, he’ll get the new missionaries and rent a hotel and train them till they can be his leaders.  No pressure there...  we’re all sweating bullets.  My new companion is from Bahia up north of Brazil.   Elder Silva is exciterd to go to a new área and get some baptisms as well.  I am rather daunted with the responsibility of training again, but with the Lords help, I can succeed.    Our área is going well and yesterday in our comp. study E. Silva and I decided that we have a new extremely high level of teaching and finding, but we need to be have a higher level of follow up with investigators.  Ive been studying the stories of Alma the Older, Peter and his 3000 converts, King Benjamins people and of those who Jesus taught and blessed in Bountiful.  There are several key points that Ive percieved;  1st)  They were taught in large groups.  2nd) none of them fell away.  3rd) they always took a special covenant to serve those who converted with them and have all things in common.  And 4th) they all had a mighty change of heart.  I find it interresting that they were all taught in large groups, be it in each others homes, forests, temples etc.  I am thinking of doing something like that here with my new companion and see if we can use our own investigators to do follow up and use each other to progress and “never fall away”.  Thats open to commentary.  With only seven months left, Im getting frantic to do the best I can and make the most of the second half of my mission.  The last six months really flew by.  I foud out that the family whose son was killed and over whom I worked so hard that I was teaching in Florianópolis got baptized this Saturday.  I cried out for joy and Im glad the elders there are working well with the people I taught. I know the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter Day Saints the true church of God and His Son, built on Prophets seers and revelators who speak with and know Christ.  The power of  the Priesthood is real.  I know that Jesus Christ lives and is our savior.  I love to serve Him and hope that I can become a better servant to Him.  I love you, pray for you and hope that all contiues well at home.  I dont know what things are like up there, but all the banks here are on strike for some reason or other.  I havnt the slightest Idea on what all this economic crisis is, but it sure seems serious.                    Love, Joseph

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: an epsitle unto the illustrious family Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:36:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: an epsitle unto the illustrious family AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 20 Oct 2008 16:39:03 +0000 Dear Family,  This week hás been interresting as I’ve begun training again.  My new companion, Elder Brandão is pretty cool, he’s from a state on the majority of the east coast called Bahia.  Most brazilians say that people from there are kind of lazy, or at least really slow, but my companion is doing a good job, though he dosnt seem all that talkative.  Im working on that one.  Usually when missionaries leave the MTC, they are pretty serious and boring, and we have to give them an Idea of how we can still have fun and work at the same time.  For instance;  singing in the midst of an everlasting warm front at the top of your lungs, walking through the puddles of water because its probably more dry when youre walking in the water,  barking at stray dogs to watch them freak out and start running from the invisible dog, etc.  I have to teach him the new techniques as well, so its kind of like teaching a missionary who didnt even pass through the MTC at all, and I think hes kind of doubtfull as to their inspiredness, so we’ve still got some work to do.  I like him though and Im sure he’ll be a great missionary.    So I’m a zone leader together with E. DeWitt from Gilbert AZ, but we’re not companions, we just live in the same house and are both training.  Its alot of fun.  Its the first time in my mission that Ive lived in the same house with an american.  Ive gotten to pull my english off the shelf and use and hear some words I havnt heard in forever. I decided to buy a new suit for 50$ to replace my one of my wool ones.  My suits were ridiculously hot last Summer and I dont want to die.  I gave a talk yesterday at church, for which Ihad a week to prepare, and I prepared, only I forgot my notes and stuff that I had carefully translated over the week, so as we were in Sunday school (its before sacrament meeting here), I got an Idea to talk about unity and the importance to go to church and feel the spirit in groups.  I have been studying very carefully about the effects of people being taught and converted in groups as shown in acts 2, mosiah 18 and alma 5, mosiah 2-5, and the story of the nephites taught in boutniful by the savior.  Every result was complete conversion until the end and “they had all things in common”.  President Eyring spoke about being united and giving fast offerings and other offerings to the poor and needy, and Said that it is directly affects how much of the gifts, and fruit of the Spirit we recieve.  Our mission president once Said that when talking about Zion, and how there was no poor among them, it doesnt mean that they all recieved the same amount of money.  For example, If I give $1000 to three people and come back in a week, one might have $3000, another, might have nothing, and another might actually owe me $1000.  So the question we need to ask is not “well, if we were all rich...”, but “how do I manage myself and how can I care for others in a way that they will not go hungry?”  Looking further, we see that when we feel the spirit, or especially when we feel the spirit as a result of remission of sin(Moroni 8:25-26), we feel Charity towards our peers.  When this happens in a group, all may feel this and may be converted and care one for another.  Is it any wonder that we need to begin worship in a closely knit such as the family?  When the family prays, and especially as Pres. Eyring described a family who even a Young child prayed for each and every one in the circle in such a way that the spirit descended and blessed all present; when they pray together and progress, they form a mini-Zion, and can be blessed accordingly.  I am working on a plan to keep up retention and follow ups with investigators based on the program in Mosiah 18 using ward missionaries in the place of priests.  I ll write more about that next week after I present the plan to the bishop.   I love you all, and this last week I remembered and naturally missed my nieces and nephews.  I hope they are well.  I pray for you and hope you are all doing well.  I got the letter from Gma Woodbury and Im happy to know she is well.  I had been thinking about her and Said a prayer for her earlier this week.  Im glad to hve blessed with such a wonderful family.                          Love, Joseph

So I put a list together of people that have potencial to be baptized or that were set to be baptized during the transfer. Now, when I mark baptisms, I have a sincere desire and a determiniation to help the people get baptized.  Upon conversing with my companion, weve decided to mark baptisms in two weeks to help us and our investigators focus.  Alot of the time we just mark baptisms for numbers, knowing that probably the people wont really get baptized on the appointed date.  But now I want to help people gain a testimony and act on it getting baptized.  All in all the fast helped me out.        My companion is doing well and yesterday I let him take some of the harder parts of teaching the first lesson and I must say, he did an excellent job.  He is opening up little by little, and is starting to give input on how we can improve, or especially me, but thats OK, because I can see that he is willing to open up a little.  He seems to be doing all right with the rules, and never asks questions, so I just have to guess what he might need help with.  He'll loosen up one of these days.         Our area is doing well and the members trust us and like to help us out when they can.  Capivari is doing alot better now with a new person responsible for the branch.  Irmao Dilney is an outstanding leader and is helping to tie up loose ends and get all the people reactivated. ## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Agronomica
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:37:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronomicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 29 Sep 2008 17:41:10 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SilvaSão JoãoZona TubarãoDear President Queiroz,    Elder Silva and I have been trying to get the new tecniques worked out since zone conference and we are liking them. We also noticed that the things Elder Americo showed us about making an invitation to be baptized in the first visit when we give a blessing makes it easier to find people to be baptized and saves us roughly 50% of wasted time on follow up visits and teaching people who wont really get baptized.  We still have some people who are marked for baptism, but who in all reality wont be baptized on those days.  We decided to exclude them in our numbers of people marked for baptism and try to get a an actual number of people with solid dates for baptism.  Naturally, our numbers for marked baptisms falls.  We also noted that if we apply the stuff Elder Americo introduced, new investigators will fall in numbers, because new investigators are those who are taught a lesson and accept a marked day for another visit.  If they don’t accept baptism, we don’t mark another visit.  Elder Silva and I agree that this could really increase the number of baptisms if we have more faith, really have the spirit as we give a blessing and have developed personal power.  We talked about the new things going on in the mission in the correlation meeting with the bishop here on Sunday, and he likes the idea and wants to start pumping up the ward mission and prepare for retention with a whole lot of new converts.  He seems excited.  I’m glad he supports us and isn’t worried about how he might handle a situation of having a lot of new members to take care of.  Some would just complain and say that we don’t care about retention and how we’re just making a problem for the bishop, but he sees it as a chance to get to work.  I like the ward here.   Elder Silva is doing well and I really am enjoying serving with someone so willing to try out new things and always improve together.  He seems to always know what to do.  On Saturday, we went on a couple of visits and gave blessings.  We used the new stuff we learned on Friday in conference and it felt kind of like a crash course or a 1000 meter dash blindfolded in a dark forest with low branches, but we pulled it off after calling Elder Americo four or five times in an hour and a half, looking for a little advice and working out the kinks here and there.  It turned out well.  We blessed a woman who lost her leg a few weeks ago to diabetes and who has four children living and five that passed away as children for various reasons and who also smokes.  I had no idea what to do or how to give the invitation to baptism, or whatnot, so I asked to use the restroom and I knelt down and prayed for guidance.  I don’t even remember what all I said, but I said a bunch of things about the plan for our families and gave a blessing.  Now that I think about it, I think I could have worded everything better, but we gave a blessing that she would be able to stop smoking.  It was a powerful blessing and the spirit was strong.  They, or especially the husband, said no to baptism.  Then we went to another person who had an issue with smoking and was depressed.  So we asked her, “if Jesus Christ cures you and takes away your desire to smoke, will you follow him and be baptized on the twenty fifth of October?”  She and her husband said yes.  We gave them blessings and the next day when we went to visit them, she said that she has no desire to smoke, that even the smell has lost it’s favor.  It almost seems easier to ask people to be baptized this way.  They exercise faith, making a commitment, based on their belief, and in the same hour, they receive a confirmation of their faith, and it’s easier for them to just do it and be baptized.  We want our whole zone to start doing this as well, and surely it will be the main focus in our zone meetings.  We have other experiences to tell, but it suffices to just say that we are, really, the representatives of Jesus Christ and we hold His priesthood and I am ever happy to be His servant. Our numbers this week are as follows;Bat/conf…………………………………………….….0/0          Goal for coming week……………………2/2Batismos marcados…………………………………….6/2    Goal for coming week………………….10/4Pesquisadores na igreja………………………………...6 Goal for coming week..........................10Lições com membro........................................................15 Goal for coming week..........................15Novos pesquisadores........................................................30   Goal for coming week..........................20Endereços.........................................................................10    Goal for coming week…………………..28Lembre se disto………………………………………….100%Qualificar pelo espirito………………………………….100%  Have a good week and we hope to have some baptisms this weekend.

Upon seeing a heavenly manifestation, their attitudes changed, and upon more heavenly manifestations, they looked to one who understood their origin and made the same supplication as those who were touched by the spirit in peters discourse, in king benjamins discourse, and in response to the teaching of Aaron, the brother of ammon;  what shall we do? ## Subject: Fw: Another fine week here in Brazil...
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:37:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Another fine week here in Brazil...From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 29 Sep 2008 18:03:24 +0000Dear family,            This week was zone conference and we learned a whole lot.  Our assistente viajante (traveling assistant to the president), Elder Americo, gave us a training on how to give a blessing and invite someone to be baptized all in one visit.  I had an interview with the president during the training so I missed most of it and I’m kind of just learning with my companion and what he tells me about it.  Elder Silva and I have been trying to get the new tecniques worked out since zone conference and we are liking them. We also noticed that the things Elder Americo showed us about making an invitation to be baptized in the first visit when we give a blessing makes it easier to find people to be baptized and saves us roughly 50% of wasted time on follow up visits and teaching people who wont really get baptized.  We still have some people who are marked for baptism, but who in all reality wont be baptized on those days.  We decided to exclude them in our numbers of people marked for baptism and try to get a an actual number of people with solid dates for baptism.  Naturally, our numbers for marked baptisms falls.  We also noted that if we apply the stuff Elder Americo introduced, new investigators will fall in numbers, because new investigators are those who are taught a lesson and accept a marked day for another visit.  If they don’t accept baptism, we don’t mark another visit.  Elder Silva and I agree that this could really increase the number of baptisms if we have more faith, really have the spirit as we give a blessing and have developed personal power.    We talked about the new things going on in the mission in the correlation meeting with the bishop here on Sunday, and he likes the idea and wants to start pumping up the ward mission and prepare for retention with a whole lot of new converts.  He seems excited.  I’m glad he supports us and isn’t worried about how he might handle a situation of having a lot of new members to take care of.  Some would just complain and say that we don’t care about retention and how we’re just making a problem for the bishop, but he sees it as a chance to get to work.  I like the ward here.   Elder Silva is doing well and I really am enjoying serving with someone so willing to try out new things and always improve together.  He seems to always know what to do.  On Saturday, we went on a couple of visits and gave blessings.  We used the new stuff we learned on Friday in conference and it felt kind of like a crash course or a 1000 meter dash blindfolded in a dark forest with low branches, but we pulled it off after calling Elder Americo four or five times in an hour and a half, looking for a little advice and working out the kinks here and there.  It turned out well.  We blessed a woman who lost her leg a few weeks ago to diabetes and who has four children living and five that passed away as children for various reasons and who also smokes.  I had no idea what to do or how to give the invitation to baptism, or whatnot, so I asked to use the restroom and I knelt down and prayed for guidance.  I don’t even remember what all I said, but I said a bunch of things about the plan for our families and gave a blessing.  Now that I think about it, I think I could have worded everything better, but we gave a blessing that she would be able to stop smoking.  It was a powerful blessing and the spirit was strong.  They, or especially the husband, said no to baptism.  Then we went to another person who had an issue with smoking and was depressed.  So we asked her, “if Jesus Christ cures you and takes away your desire to smoke, will you follow him and be baptized on the twenty fifth of October?”  She and her husband said yes.  We gave them blessings and the next day when we went to visit them, she said that she has no desire to smoke, that even the smell has lost it’s favor.  It almost seems easier to ask people to be baptized this way.  They exercise faith, making a commitment, based on their belief, and in the same hour, they receive a confirmation of their faith, and it’s easier for them to just do it and be baptized.  We want our whole zone to start doing this as well, and surely it will be the main focus in our zone meetings.  We have other experiences to tell, but it suffices to just say that we are, really, the representatives of Jesus Christ and we hold His priesthood and I am ever happy to be His servant. This week I got a letter from the first presidency (no it wasn’t personalized to me) about elections and how if I can I should vote using the absentee ballot if at all possible.  I havnt heard practically anything about the republican party since Ive been down here, but I think that John McCain is running for president.  It seems that there is a media filter located on the borders of the US that filters anything out that has to do with the republican party.  Everyone down here seems to be in love with Obama, but if you ask why, they never know.  Its kind of funny, especially when you ask them what they know about him, of even about the republican competitor, and they just get a blank look on their face…  then you ask them what they think of abortion, gay marriage, taxes etc, and tell them “welcome to the republican party”.  I love you all and remember you in my prayer and I hope that all goes well up in the northern hemisphere.  By the way, what’s all this talk about a bail out?  Who’s in jail?  ;-)             Love Joseph

## Subject: Fw: Epistola do maravilhoso Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:38:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Epistola do maravilhoso Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 22 Sep 2008 14:06:16 +0000Dear Family, This week was alright, I got to do two divisions with other areas(Imbituba and the other side of Tubarão.) and I must say that I was glad to work with my companion afterwards.  Ive noticed that a lot of missionaries have a fairly easy time developing spiritual knowledge and less ease with developing spiritual power.  Spiritual knowledge helps you get perspective, but dosnt usually help out so much in your actual work.  The power really depends on your own personal worthiness and what your relationship with the Savior amounts to.  Also, spiritual knowledge usually helps you get proud, and power is a source of and a result of humility.  Very interesting.   I got a letter from Charles a couple of weeks ago, and it was fun to see what was going on in his life.  If at all possible, I’d like to get copies of his emails and communications or whatever.  I’m glad to hear that Dad’s recovering well from his surgery.  I still have no idea what it was all about, just that he got surgery on his eye.  Usually I would say that could be rather painfull…     Here in Tubarão(which by way of interpretation is “Shark”) we are having good weather with lots of rain and consequent mud.  My shoes have begun the descent to destruction at last, though I think they’ve still got another two or three months left in them.  Ive never even had to resole them.  Most of my ties are in faded colors, but if I turn them around they seem brand new…  This morning I had a struggle over which of my shirts I would use.  Do I want to use the white one with pin stripes, or the white one with buttons in the collar?  Do I want to use the white one with no buttons in the collar, or the white ones one with button holes in the collar but has no more buttons?  Do I want to use the white one with mitered cuffs, or the white one with traditional cuffs?  Do I want to use the really white one or the kind of yellowish white one?  Boy what a day.  I think I spent a whole fifteen seconds deciding what I would wear today.  That was tough…     Well, my times already up and my companion is getting antsy.  We’re fasting and as soon as I’m done, we’ll break our fast and fill our barrigas with food.  I cant wait.  I hope you all have a wonderful week and know that I love you and pray for you.  Thank you for your prayers and support.           Love, Elder Joseph  

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Dear family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:39:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear familyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 1 Sep 2008 21:15:16 +0000Dear family,    Sorry for not writing a letter last week.  This weeks letter is rather comprehensive, so I hope it makes up for it.  This week I got called to be a zone leader in Tubarão down south.  I’ll be 45 minutes away from my first area and can do divisions there when I want to.  President Queiroz interviewed me and asked me to help the zone apply the new techniques for teaching and get the baptisms up.  The whole zone had one baptism this last transfer.  I’m not sure why he chose me, this hasn’t been the time to be most proud of seeing as my areas not doing so well.  Oh well, I’ll just do my best.  I got to go to the leadership counsel on Friday with all the assistants and zone leaders and discuss rules, requirements etc.  We changed the way we record contacts and I think it will save the church some money and improve the effectivness of the missionaries.     We are still continuing to have good and very positive experiences with the new program and we are getting into more homes and teaching families together and not just one spouse or a few children, but their whole families.  I feel that I have a great tool in my hands that will help me have a great deal more of success on the mission.  I talked to E. Tessaro who is one of the assistants and will be going home two weeks later than most to go on divisions in the weaker zones and help integrate the new programs and asked if he was going to do a division with us in Tubarão, and he said yes.  Thats rather relieving, because I still have a few questions and Im sure he’ll give us a hand.  I’m eager to learn more and be more effective.   Agronômica is not the strongest ward I’ve ever seen, but I’m sure if we can succeed in getting more help from the members in the new program, they’ll come out of the lessons with the same response as Elder McKonkie when he saw the way that Pres. Queiroz’s father did missionary work in his mission some thirty years ago;  “POWER!!”  Something that I’ve noticed is that when we go to people’s homes to bless them, I prefer that the members have a dress shirt and tie if at all possible, so we don’t invite as many members as we used to.  It used to be that we always asked one of the young men to go along with us in and he would go with us in a t-shirt and sandals, but we want to have the appearances of a representative of Jesus Christ as we give a blessing.  If we can manage to get the help of the melchizedek priesthood quorums a little bit more, we might be able to have a little more success.  I’ve made alot of friends here, and I’m sad to go, but E. Carvalho says I’ve made a difference here, even if it dosn’t show so much in numbers.  I hope my testimony has helped those we’ve taught, be they investigator or not, to have more hope, more faith and have more desire to follow the Savior.     Yesterday we went to bless the family of an investigator that had moved and was hard to find.  Her husband was always rather against our visits as he is very catholic, so he never listened and sometimes wouldnt let us in, but we gave a blessing with his permission and after the blessing we said we had a message that could bless him and his family with the feelings of peace he was feeling right then and he accepted the offer.  He invited us to come and go in his home whenever we had a desire to visit.  WOW.  The program works.  At least two people there should be getting marked for baptism this week when we pass by again.  Then we went to another investigators home whose baptismal date had fallen and we were wanting to invite her fifteen year old son to be baptized as well, but we had already taught them the first lesson last week.  I remembered what our president  had said in the leadership counsel about the spirit being strongest during the first lesson after the first vision, and that being the time to invite to baptism, so I thought “how am I supposed to teach the first lesson again?”  So I decided to read a little from 3Ne 17 and say a prayer and then teach the restoration again with the figure aids starting at Joseph Smith.  It worked.  We marked Salete and Wilian for baptism and even got to explain to Salete why her baptism with Igreja Universal was invalid and she accepted to get baptized.  Now she just needs to start going to church.I’m thankful for the opportunity to serve as a zone leader, and throughout the past week I’ve been thinking about how I can help the other elders to have success.  I thought of why it is that the church in general can grow or cease to grow under the influence of righteous men such as prophets and apostles.  In the end, practically none of us will ever meet them, and even though we only hear from them every six months, they have an influence through their words.  They are not with us always, yet they have influence and can know how to help us.  Every time I hear E. Eyring give a talk, I feel the powerful testifying and strength of the spirit and I know what he says is there to help me and it does.  Every time.  So, the reason for this is that he lives his testimony, and his words are validated by his unseen actions.  I’ve never seen him study the scriptures, heard him pray, or make visits, yet the spirit testifies.  Everything we do makes a difference, be it waking up on time, making so many contacts, brushing your teeth and taking a shower at the designated time, companionship study, personal prayer, your attitude as a representative of Jesus Christ etc.  As Preach my Gospel says, “Your investigator’s comprehension will be directly effected by your personal worthiness.”  The Powers of the devil are great in influencing people to destruction, but the influence of the Holy Ghost and of Righteousness are greater in their power.  The Lord calls us in our weakness, but He is said to qualify us.  I’ll get to put that one to the test now.  I will go with my trust in the Lord.  I love each of you all and hope that you all have a good week.  Keep praying for me when you get a chance.  I think I’m really going to need it in my new area.  Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Sao Joao
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:39:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Sao JoaoFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 8 Sep 2008 18:07:19 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SilvaSao JoaoZona TubaraoDear President Queiroz,    This week was filled with good experiences and as I work with Elder Silva, I appreciate having a good companion who is comfortable with the new program.  Its funny that when I started serving last year in Criciúma last year, I did a division with the zone leaders here in Tubarao and I didn’t like the apartment and I thought the city was horribly ugly.  I passed the last year thinking that of all the places where I would like to serve, Tubarão would be last on my list.  Oh, the irony…  After arriving here, I find that I find the city aesthetically pleasing and the people here are gente finíssima.  I like it here.  The apartment is nicer than I seem to remember it being.  I miss serving in the country.  Its pretty and the people are a lot nicer here as well.  It reminds me of when I was serving in criciuma when I began serving my mission.  That’s good because I had a good amount of success and baptisms there.   Elder Silva is a good missionary and I enjoy teaching with him.  He speaks very good English too, and when we are in the house, we speak English.  Its been a while.  He seems very pleased with the new program and we are having a good amount of success with bringing and feeling the spirit in people’s houses.  He says that he is starting to gain a testimony of the priesthood and our power and authority.  It feels good to be with a companion who has spiritual power and to be on an equal level with each other on everything.  The area seems to be going well, and from what I’m seeing with the records with numbers, the new program’s effects are starting to kick in.  I’m sure that Elder Malheiros’ and Tessaro’s help has something to do with it.  I had a few questions about a few things and I think that it was a good experience to have their help.  Elder Silva got a few answers about the invitation to baptism answered with E Tessaro.  It was good to get to know E Tessaro a little better too.  I was always afraid of him, seeing as he always gave a serious impression.  They are helping out plenty in our zone and I think it will be good for Imbituba to have them help out for a couple of days.  The service project by Mãos que Ajudam was a success and the bishop said in sacrament meeting that the people in the neighborhood by the school we worked on see us differently now.  We already got a reference there and we will do a lot of contacting in that neighborhood on Friday.  We did the fast and saw some quick effects.  We entered someone’s house and they seemed like the kind of person that if you let them, they will talk your ears off.  So after listening to the life story of this woman, Niumfa, I asked her to imagine that Jesus Christ didn’t live two thousand years ago, but right now, and that if he were passing by her street, with a hundred people round about and healing and blessing people, he stopped in front of her house, clapped his hands and asked to bless her, what would she say?  So she said a few things about what she wanted for her family and her broken life.  As she had been talking in the beginning, I thought there was little chance that she would accept the gospel;  she just needed someone to complain to.  But then, after listening to her lament over her broken family, I felt compassion and we gave her a blessing to recover from her health problems and blessed her, her home and family.  When we finished and got up, she didn’t know what to say, just to smile and thank us.  When we bless the people, we bring the spirit and if the missionary feels charity, it is manifest.  The Lord said;  “this new commandment I give unto you, that ye love one another.  By this shall men know ye are my disciples; if ye have love one to another.”  When we show the love of the savior dwelling in our hearts, they recognize the servants of the Lord, and they are more disposed to follow.     On Wednesday when I arrived in Tubarao, we went to bless someone and when E Silva said that we could bless the sick or afflicted, and asked if there was anyone sick in the house, the wife, Elielda, started to cry and raised her hand.  She was going to go have a surgery for a problem in the uterus, and asked for a blessing.  We gave a blessing that she would be cured and then we prayed for them.  I felt happy to ask the patriarch of the house if we could come back and leave a message that could bless his family for ever and even happier to hear him say yes.  We went back and taught the first lesson to the family.  As I taught the first vision, I told them that they would feel the Holy Ghost as I taught.  Elielda started to cry as we told of the appearance of the Father and the Son and I was practically crying as well.  They all accepted to be baptized.  Elder Silva was ecstatic.  I was too.  This morning we discussed things we can do to augment our teaching pool and maintain it at a large size.  I’ve been thinking on what I read about Alma sr. in Mosiah 18 and how he taught and baptized two hundred and four people while teaching “in secret”.  We are thinking of doing a second lesson with the large visual aids in the chapel every Tuesday night, because if the investigators get to know other investigators, they will not feel alone in going to church on Sundays and being baptized, but that they and their families are doing the same as other normal people.  We’ll be working on perfect the idea and the details this week.  I enjoy companionship study with E Silva.    Thank you for all you are doing and for your faith and vision which makes its way down the chain to us.  I’ll try my best to pass it on the of the missionaries.  Have a good week.&gt;        Our numbers this week are as follows;&gt;&gt; Bat/conf..............................0/0&gt; Bat marc.............................12/6&gt; Pesq na igr...........................1&gt; Liç c memb.........................15&gt; Novos..................................44&gt; Endereços............................28&gt; Lemb se disto......................96%&gt; Qualificar............................100%

## Subject: Fw: message from Brazil
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:39:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: message from BrazilFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: pwoodbu@mstar.netDate: Mon, 8 Sep 2008 18:45:37 +0000Dear Uncle Paul, Thank you for your email, sorry for not responding sooner.  I always appreciate getting emails from you and your family.  I enjoy serving as a missionary and our new program.  We offer to bless the people, then we teach them.  Peter, in the book of ST Luke, didn’t necessarily become a disciple or apostle of Jesus Christ until after the Savior had healed his mother, and the next few days later gave him financial success in his fishing.  When a blind person walked by and pleaded for the Lord to help him, He didn’t offer a message, nor money, but he cured him.  When a lame man asked Peter and John for money, Peter said that he had naught wherewith to give, but what he had he gave; wholeness.  As a result, five thousand people believed.  In 1corinthians, Paul the Apostle said that the Kingdom of God is in Power, and not in words.  We enter their homes, read Luke 10:5+9 and promise that the Holy Ghost will be present, that they will feel the peace, faith, kindness etc that is listed in Galations 5:22, and then we ask them what they would ask the Savior if he appeared.  Then we bless them and their families.  Immediately thereafter, we offer to give a message later which if they listen, will bless their families forever.  When we come back, we teach the first lesson promising that they will feel the same spirit as they did during the blessing.    The power of the priesthood is real, and I am glad to have the opportunity to exercise it.  I hope that you and your family are doing well.  Thank you for the example you set for us, I admire and look up to you and the rest of the Woodbury clan.  The church is true.  I know it and I feel it.              Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: E Ai, tudo bem?
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:39:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: E Ai, tudo bem?From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 8 Sep 2008 18:24:51 +0000Dear Family,    This week was filled with good experiences and as I work with my new companion, Elder Silva, I appreciate having a good companion who is comfortable with the new program.  Its funny that when I started serving in Criciúma last year, I did a division with the zone leaders here in Tubarao and I didn’t like the apartment and I thought the city was horribly ugly.  I passed the last year thinking that of all the places where I would like to serve, Tubarão would be last on my list.  Oh, the irony…  After arriving here, I find that I find the city aesthetically pleasing and the people here are great.  I like it here.  The apartment is nicer than I seem to remember it being.  I miss serving in the country.  Its pretty and the people are a lot nicer here as well.  It reminds me of when I was serving in criciuma when I began serving my mission.  That’s good because I had a good amount of success and baptisms there.     Elder Silva is a good missionary and I enjoy teaching with him.  He speaks very good English too, and when we are in the house, we speak English.  It’s been a while.  He seems very pleased with the new program and we are having a good amount of success with bringing and feeling the spirit in people’s houses.  He says that he is starting to gain a testimony of the priesthood and our power and authority.  It feels good to be with a companion who has spiritual power and to be on an equal level with each other on everything.     The area seems to be going well, and from what I’m seeing with the records with numbers, the new program’s effects are starting to kick in.  I’m sure that Elder Malheiros’ and Tessaro’s help has something to do with it.  They are two missionaries who are finishing their missions together just going through our zone and helping train us on the new program.  I had a few questions about a few things and I think that it was a good experience to have their help.  Elder Silva got a few answers about the invitation to baptism answered with E Tessaro.  It was good to get to know E Tessaro a little better too.  I was always afraid of him, seeing as he always gave a serious impression.  We did a service project on Saturday painting in a public school.  The service project Mãos que Ajudam(helping hands) was a success and the bishop said in sacrament meeting that the people in the neighborhood by the school we worked on see us differently now.  We already got a reference there and we will do a lot of contacting in that neighborhood on Friday.  We did the fast and saw some quick effects.  We entered someone’s house and they seemed like the kind of person that if you let them, they will talk your ears off.  So after listening to the life story of this woman, Niumfa, I asked her to imagine that Jesus Christ didn’t live two thousand years ago, but right now, and that if he were passing by her street, with a hundred people round about and healing and blessing people, he stopped in front of her house, clapped his hands and asked to bless her, what would she say?  So she said a few things about what she wanted for her family and her broken life.  As she had been talking in the beginning, I thought there was little chance that she would accept the gospel;  she just needed someone to complain to.  But then, after listening to her lament over her broken family, I felt compassion and we gave her a blessing to recover from her health problems and blessed her, her home and family.  When we finished and got up, she didn’t know what to say, just to smile and thank us.  When we bless the people, we bring the spirit and if the missionary feels charity, it is manifest.  The Lord said;  “this new commandment I give unto you, that ye love one another.  By this shall men know ye are my disciples; if ye have love one to another.”  When we show the love of the savior dwelling in our hearts, they recognize the servants of the Lord, and they are more disposed to follow.  On Wednesday when I arrived in Tubarao, we went to bless someone and when E Silva said that we could bless the sick or afflicted, and asked if there was anyone sick in the house, the wife, Elielda, started to cry and raised her hand.  She was going to go have a surgery for a problem in the uterus, and asked for a blessing.  We gave a blessing that she would be cured and then we prayed for them.  I felt happy to ask the patriarch of the house if we could come back and leave a message that could bless his family for ever and even happier to hear him say yes.  We went back and taught the first lesson to the family.  As I taught the first vision, I told them that they would feel the Holy Ghost as I taught.  Elielda started to cry as we told of the appearance of the Father and the Son and I was practically crying as well.  Elder Silva invited them to be baptized and yhey all accepted  Elder Silva was ecstatic.  I was too.  This morning we discussed things we can do to augment our teaching pool and maintain it at a large size.  I’ve been thinking on what I read about Alma sr. in Mosiah 18 and how he taught and baptized two hundred and four people while teaching “in secret”.  We are thinking of doing a second lesson(the plan of salvation) with some large visual aids emphasizing the purpose of life and the questions “where are we from?, why are we here?, and where are we going?” in the chapel every Tuesday night, because if the investigators get to know other investigators, they will not feel alone in going to church on Sundays and being baptized, but that they and their families are doing the same as other normal people.  We’ll be working on perfect the idea and the details this week.  I enjoy companionship study with E Silva.  I love you all and hope you are all doing well.  Sounds like when I get home the house will be completely different.  Crazy.  I want you all to know that I have a testimony of the fact that the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter Day Saints is the only church with power and authority to act in the name of the Lord on the earth.  Other churches can dispute that they’ve seen visions and angels, but there are men who can speak with God face to face, and feel, physically, the prints in the hands and feet of the Savior, and they are all members of the restored church.  I’ve met one.  That is something no one can counterfeit.  We have the authority, and I take courage knowing that we’re on the winner’s side.  I love you all.                     Love, Joseph

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronomicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 1 Sep 2008 20:53:48 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CarvalhoAgronômicaZona FlorianópolisDear President Queiroz,   We are still continuing to have good and very positive experiences with the new program and we are getting into more homes and teaching families together and not just one spouse or a few children, but their whole families.  I feel that I have a great tool in my hands that will help me have a great deal more of success on the mission.  I talked to E. Tessaro today and asked if he was going to do a division with us in Tubarão, and he said yes.  Thats rather relieving, because I still have a few questions and Im sure he’ll give us a hand.  I’m eager to learn more and be more effective.  Elder Carvalho has grown alot since he arrived in agronômica and I’m sure he’ll be fine and work well with E. Haws.  We’ve enjoyed the last two transfers and have had a good companionship.  He has a few problems doing the new contacts and giving prayers and blessings, but he is always getting better.   Agronômica is not the strongest ward I’ve ever seen, but I’m sure if we can succeed in getting more help from the members in the new program, they’ll come out of the lessons with the same response as Elder McKonkie;  “POWER!!”  Something that I’ve noticed is that when we go to people’s homes to bless them, I prefer that the members have a dress shirt and tie if at all possible, so we don’t invite as many members as we used to. I remembered what you had said in the conselho de liderança, about the spirit being strongest during the first lesson after the first vision, and that being the time to invite to baptism, so I thought “how am I supposed to teach the first lesson again?”  So I decided to read a little from 3Ne 17 and say a prayer and then teach the restoration again with the figure aids starting at Joseph Smith. They are not with us always, yet they have influence and can know how to help us.  Every time I hear E. Eyring give a talk, I feel the powerful testifying and strength of the spirit and I know what he says is there to help me and it does.  Every time.  So, the reason for this is that he lives his testimony, and his words are validated by his unseen actions. ## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Agronomica
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:40:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronomicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 20:05:05 +0000Elder AndrewsElder carvalhoAgronomicaDear President Quieroz,         Sorry for the short letter, the network at the lan house broke down and erased what I had already written.  This week passed well and we have been finding new people to teach due to the new program.  I have been focusing with Elder Carvalho on the new teaching techniques and we are ever improving.           Elder Carvalho is doing well and is liking our new contacts and teaching ways and is always becoming a stronger missionary.  We get along just fine.          Our area is doing well and due to the amount of new people we are encountering, we should be marking a few more baptisms this week, especially if our investigators make it to the baptism we will be having on saturday.  We will be baptising an investigator that we encountered the first day I was here in agronomica knocking doors.  Shes cool and is prepared to be a contributing member of the church.  we also found some new people to prepare for baptism in the next two weeks or so.  We FINALLY got some new people to go to church and they liked it.  Every week we go up the hill to wake people up and go to church but this is the first week that weve come down the hill with anything to show for our efforts.  This is generally referred to as a "blessing".  This was also the highest number of investigators that  weve been able to achieve in church since I arrived.  After doing contacts the new way, it seems cheap to do it the old way.  We are eager to give up passing out cards and talking to people and offering to go to their homes to bless them.          Our numbers this week are as follows;Bat. conf...........................0/0bat marc...........................7/4liç c memb.........................8pesq na igr.........................5Novos...............................21contatos.............................140Lem s dis..........................95%qualificar...........................100%

## Subject: Fw: Hey fammy, heres a letter for ya
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:41:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Hey fammy, heres a letter for yaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 18 Aug 2008 20:55:16 +0000Dear Family,       Our new mission president is amazing and is implementing a number of changes in our mission.  He said that we need to focus more on blessing the people than teaching them a message.  He said that when the Lord saw a blind man in the street, He didnt say he could come by some time and teach him a message.  He cured him.  We are doing contacts differently now.  It used to be that we just stopped someone in the street and asked if we could give them a present- a pass along card- and then say a little speel about the restoration or something and tell them to call the number on the card to get the movie or book for free and a message about the restoration.  Now, we just stop people in the street and tell them that were representatives of Jesus Christ and we want to go to there house and kneel down and pray and bless them, their families and their homes and if necessary give a blessing of health to those who are sick and its free and only ten minutes.  We also have a message that if they listen, can bless their family for eternity.  Then we ask if we can come by on a specific day.  It works pretty well.  Then we teach the first lesson very quickly and immediatly after teaching about the first vision and restoration of authority, and prayer, we ask them to be baptized and if they say yes, we give them a premarked book of mormon and say, this is a proof that this is all true.  read this and pray about it and then we leave.  It works.       This week was tough, all but three appointments monday through saturday fell through and consequently we did alot of walking, knocking on doors and after getting misdirected from someone, we discovered that the Morro Horacio has an outlet up top into one of the richest neighborhoods in the city.  You have the favella and the rich next door to each other.  I switched my contacts over from giving out pass along cards to the new approach, and I must say, it was tough and nerve racking just stopping someone in the road with out offering a "present", but it paid off on sunday when we blessed the homes of the people we set up appointments with and they felt the spirit.  Elder Carvalho was somewhat nervous about doing the contacts the new way, so our contacts suffered a little bit, but this week we'll be practicing the contacts together in our companionship study, so the contacts should be picking up.  I was shocked by the amount of houses weve gotten into with the new way and the difference in how people feel the spirit.  At the end of the day on Sunday, E. Carvalho said he wanted to give Irmão Queiroz a kiss on the forehead and thank him for his help!  Ive been feeling a little discouraged in how to do the work since Ive been here in Florianopolis, but now Im feeling how I did when I first arrived on the mission;  Pumped and ready to go.  Every time I come out of a house we give a blessing in, I feel the same way I did in the beginning.           Ive thought alot over time about blessings given, and how blessings given are different depending on who gives them, especially in how much detail is given, how it is expressed etc., and I think its closely tied to the gift of prophecy and how well we are in tune with the spirit and how much charity we have.  Irmao Rodrigo is one of the people who has a gift for blessing, and we took him along with us, and my, what a spirit he brought with him.  After giving a blessing of health to one of our investigators, she asked us to bless each of her children, so we took turns blessing.  I feel priveledged to have been a holder of the melchizedek Priesthood for almost three years before going on a mission and discovering the marvelous opportunity to give blessings, and speak on behalf of our Lord.  I love to bless people, and I am happy to be doing it more plainly now.  Last night we went to an investigators house who always listens alone while his wife and daughter go to another room.  Weve invited her several times to listen and you can tell that Evertom, our investigator, wants her to take part too, but she never comes, so we planned to just bless their family, their house and their lives and leave, so that she could feel the spirit and start taking part.  If she does start participating, they will both most certainly be baptized.  I read 3Ne 17, and then we prayed for them.  The results are beyond expression.  What member would want to miss something like this?  to go to peoples homes, to bless them, to feel the power of the priesthood in action, to see what the apostles saw?  Its all true, and my testimony increases and my love for Agronômica grows despite my seemingly fruitless work here.  One of our investigators weve been teaching and had a problem with smoking stopped smoking and I asked her if she had any objections to being baptized this saturday.  She was already marked for some time in august, but it was just kind of a hollow goal, so I asked her more seriously.  She asked if we thought she was ready, so I told her absolutly.  She had only just finished telling her about how she didnt have any doubts, so The answer has to be yes.  Shes excited.           I love you family and I pray for you all.  have a good week and remember that I love you all.                      Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You have the favella and the rich next door to each other. He dosnt seem to think he should do the blessings, but I will help him to take confidence in himself.  He is a good man, and I will help him to grow as much as I can as long as I can.         Just like you and Elder Tessaro said, as we try out the new way of doing things, everything would fall through.  Every thing, consequently, fell.  On sunday we had two lessons with a member present, and six new investigators.  Elder Carvalho was getting nervous, but we managed to walk as fast as we could, do as many contacts as possible and irmao Rodrigo went out with us to visit and bless.  Ive thought alot over time about blessings given, and how blessings given are different depending on who gives them, especially in how much detail is given, how it is expressed etc., and I think its closely tied to the gift of prophecy and how well we are in tune with the spirit and how much charity we have. ## Subject: Fw: letter
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:47:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: letterFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 4 Aug 2008 18:31:18 +0000Dear family,        I have been learning alot this week and gaining a greater desire to help out the people in this ward which is so divided by class and coldness that it seems to only stagnate the members spirituality.  Here in Floripa there is an interresting phenomenon;  You have the insanely rich and the poor of the world as next door neighbors.  As many have observed in the past,the rich are generally set on the things of this world(this being a general statement, and not implying to people individually;  I know many rich people who are the salt of the earth) It is easiest to work with success in the poorer areas, where the people in general are more meek and genuine, hence we find ourselves working ing the favella and helping people improve their lives, but when the majority of the active membership of the ward is composed of the rich, they have a fear of entering into the ghetto to help us teach or, if the said member is a returned missionary, his wife dosnt like him to go there, even if he is accustomed to it, or loves to relive his own mission memories and help the poor in spirit come unto Christ.  My companion calls the Island ''A ilha das amazonas'' (the island of the amazon women).  All the men are a little controlled by their wives.  The class division is rather hindering to our number of lessons with member present.  This last week we asked a family if we could bring an investigator from the Morro Horacio (the ghetto) to an FHE, but the wifes response was negative enough that I got really depressed for the differences in classes among the people and our ward in particular.  I was very very gratefull for having achieved the standard of excellence in lessons with members present this week, but we had to sacrifice some appointments in other neighborhoods to stick around in an area where a priest helps us out.  We still found people to teach and marked a few baptisms that we were not expecting to continue teaching and the week ended on a spiritual high, so Im not necessarily complaining.         Elder Carvalho is always improving and I have been quite impressed with his progress in teaching and focus.  If he continues to improve in this manner, he will certainly be a fine missionary.  We have a good relationship and I am enjoying working with him.  I always like my third and fourth transfers in an area, because I get to know the investigators better and I can see our progress.         I love you all and hope that you have a great week.          Love Joseph

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Agronomica
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:47:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronomicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 11 Aug 2008 17:57:38 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CarvalhoAgronomicaZona FlorianopolisDear President Queiroz,        This week passed by too fast.  If we could have had one more day I wouldnt compain.  Sometimes it seems that nothing happens until the weekend with our numbers with member present, but we always seem to pull through.  Alot of things didnt work out despite our best efforts, such as people in church and lessons with member present ect, but the week finished on a high note for me.  It was sunday night, and we needed two more new investigators, and two more lessons with a member present, so I thought it would be a good idea to pass by a members house whose sister in law was staying with them and sing a hymn and leave a message extremely fast, so we went there last of all.  We got there and I sang O Pai Celeste (Father in Heaven).  The sister in law didnt really pay much attention, but when I finished singing, I noticed that the irmão was crying.  He asked us to give him a blessing, so we gave.  He was getting ready for a job interview and was feeling sick and probably had a few other concerns too.  I have always loved to give blessings.  He said that it was perfect that we came and that he was needing it.  This brother was in need of spiritual help, and we were able to give it.  Another member that was there with him offered to go out to do visits with us any morning that we needed and it served to build a stronger relationship with some of the members here in Agronomica.  To think about it, if we hadnt been so pushed for numbers, we wouldnt have gone or even thought of going there.  When you have faith and do your best, even the bad situations can strengthen you and edify your testimony.  I can assure you that this dosnt mean we'll be slacking off to get more experiences like that again.  We'll get our numbers right this week and trabalhar até o pó.         Elder Carvalho is doing well and is learning english little by litte.  Its kind of fun to discover how english grammar works and teach it to someone.  Every one thinks english is easy because the verbs are all conjugated the same way in relation to I speak, you speak, we speak, they speak, you(all) speak, he/she/it speaks. etc, but there is no pattern for how to say things in past tense, other than putting an "ed" on the end, but its not always that easy.  Elder Carvalho now hates the words irregular verb.  He is teaching well, but I want to help him teach a little more from the heart and less what he knows is in a given principle of the lessons.        Our area is doing well, we have about five or six people that are progressing well and show a strong possibility of being baptized when we can get them going to church regularly and married along with a few other complications.  We went to go get our investigators and bring them to church two times on sunday, but no one came.  That hurt a little, but next week should be better.  Someone dropped by during church to ask us to visit her and inviter her to go to church, so we'll be contacting her this week.  We also have plans to get the members visiting and helping out with our investigators, though it may still be dificult to get someone to go up to the Morro Horacio with us.  The farther you go up the hill, the uglier it gets, and fortunately, we arent working too far up the hill.          This week I was riding the bus, thinking of how I should do better with doing contacts, when I decided "Im already on a mission, Im on a bus filled with a bunch of bored people, why not make use of time?"  So I did contacts on the bus and also in the bus station.  I dont know exactly why, but doing contacts always makes me feel better about myself even though I have such a timid nature about doing contacts.  If I ever feel depressed, I should do contacts.         Our numbers this week are as follows;Bat/conf....................................0/0Bat marcado...............................8/4pesq na igr.................................0Liç c memb................................14novos.......................................14contatos....................................142Lemb s dis..................................90%Qualificar p esp............................100%

## Subject: Fw: My testimony

## Subject: Fw: Dear family.
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:48:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear family.From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 21 Jul 2008 20:11:09 +0000Dear family            This week was good and passed by rather fast.  I’ve been studying the healing power of the Atonement of Jesus Christ, as stated in Alma 7, and Matthew 11:28-30.  I read also the talk given by Elder Scott in the april 2008 general conference about overcoming the negative results of abuse(or having a loved one killed by the hands of your enemies).  As I read, I really felt the truth of the power of the atonement.  I also read the references he gave to other talks in the end of his talk.  What Dallin H Oaks said in his talk ‘He heals the heavy laden’ was especially helpful and I slowly began to remember the comfort I have received in my own trying experiences. Elder Carvalho is doing well, though to tell the truth, I am somewhat concerned about his effectiveness as a missionary especially for when he becomes senior.  He does fine right now, but when he is on his own, he could have a hard time working. He has a hard time focusing on what were doing, but I’m going to try to include him a little more in decision making and teach him how to work his tail off.  It might be good for me too.  He’s a good missionary and I hope to help him in any way possible.  I think praying out loud for your companion and his family helps him out a lot and makes your companionship stronger.  It’s a habit I plan to carry with me into my family and pray for every person and their needs and concerns in family prayer and in the future, prayer with my spouse.One of our investigators´ sons was killed last week and when we showed up a day later I had no idea for what to say, so we gave a few thoughts and afterward a blessing.  When we returned a couple of days later, she was doing better and we retaught the plan of salvation really fast and tried to see if there was anything we could do to help her.  I feel that one of the reasons I was sent here in agronomica was to help her as she goes through this experience and help her to understand the power of the atonement to heal us and give us that profound peace that comes despite our indescribable pain.  I felt that a few years ago in regard to my Mothers death, and I feel that I can help our investigator, Salete, feel the same through the Gospel of Jesus Christ.  Ever since we started teaching her two months ago, I felt impressed to focus on the doctrines in Alma chapter 7 in regards to how the Savior suffered all our pains so that He could know how to succor us in our need.   I met up with the last person on earth that I would be expecting to meet when doing contacts on Monday night;  the bishop of Itajai.  Boy was it good to see a familiar face.  I was glad to hear about our baptisms that are still active and how the ward there is still growing.  I know they are being blessed for their assistance to the missionary work there, be it in the past or present. 

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

AgronomicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 21 Jul 2008 20:08:05 +0000Elder AndrewsElder carvalhoAgronomicaZona FloripaDear President Quieroz,         This week was good and passed by rather fast. I read also the talk given by Elder Scott in the april 2008 general conference about overcoming the negative results of abuse(or having a loved one killed by the hands of your enemies).
