Elder Carvalho is doing well, though to tell the truth, I am somewhat concerned about his effectiveness as a missionary especially for when he becomes senior.  He does fine right now, but when he is on his own, he could have a hard time working. He has a hard time focusing on what were doing, but I’m going to try to include him a little more in decision making and teach him how to work his tail off.  It might be good for me too.  He’s a good missionary and I hope to help him in any way possible.  I think praying out loud for your companion and his family helps him out a lot and makes your companionship stronger.  It’s a habit I plan to carry with me into my family and pray for every person and their needs and concerns in family prayer and in the future, prayer with my spouse.One of our investigators´ sons was killed last week and when we showed up a day later I had no idea for what to say, so we gave a few thoughts and afterward a blessing.  When we returned a couple of days later, she was doing better and we retaught the plan of salvation really fast and tried to see if there was anything we could do to help her.  I feel that one of the reasons I was sent here in agronomica was to help her as she goes through this experience and help her to understand the power of the atonement to heal us and give us that profound peace that comes despite our indescribable pain.  I felt that a few years ago in regard to my Mothers death, and I feel that I can help our investigator, Salete, feel the same through the Gospel of Jesus Christ.  Ever since we started teaching her two months ago, I felt impressed to focus on the doctrines in Alma chapter 7 in regards to how the Savior suffered all our pains so that He could know how to succor us in our need.  Thank you for letting me stay here to let me still help her and our other investigators. I met up with the last person on earth that I would be expecting to meet when doing contacts on Monday night;  the bishop of Itajai.  Boy was it good to see a familiar face.  I was glad to hear about our baptisms that are still active and how the ward there is still growing.  I know they are being blessed for their assistance to the missionary work there, be it in the past or present.  Thank you for all you do for us and I hope you have a good week.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/conf………………….0/0Bapt marc…………………9/3Pesq na igr………………...4Liç c memb.........................15Novos..................................21Contatos..............................141Leb se disto.........................90%Qualificar............................86%Unfortunatly we did not qualify for the spirit on Friday because of being late getting home from an investigators house.  We’ll be doing better this week.   Boa semana,         Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: My testimony
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:48:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: My testimonyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: uhreelyah@hotmail.comDate: Mon, 4 Aug 2008 18:05:09 +0000Dear Woya,        This is my testimony of Jesus Christ which I wrote out for my mission president as he was leaving to go home to Provo.  You can keep a copy if you like and if you think it appropriate you can give it to Brother Sherwood.Jesus Christ was chosen before this earth was created to be our savior and redeemer. He is the god of the old testament and the great I AM; Jehovah. All things exist by the grace of His glory. He is the Light and the Life of the world, a light that is endless, that never can be darkened, a light that gives life to all creatures in existance. He took upon Himself flesh and blood and walked among us, even the light which ilumines our lives, yet he was rejected, for men loved darkness and reject the light. He walked among us and grew grace for every grace, light upon light until He recieved a fulness of the Glory of the Father, and was and is One with the Father. He was pure, clean from all sin, and was worthy to fulfill His mission and bring to pass the eternal life and imortality of mankind by means of making atonement with His bretheren, and our very Eternal Father.It was He who created the earth and filled it with light. He was chosen from the beginning to overcome the natural effects of the fall and allow us, His bretheren, to be redeemed from physical death through resurrection and spiritual death on conditions of following His Gospel of Faith on His name, Repentance, Baptism, Baptism by the reciept of the gift of the Holy Ghost and abiding in accordance with all other ordinances of His Gospel. He is the God of the Old Testament, the Hope of Israel, the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel.He was born to Mary, a virgin, and is the very Son of God in the flesh. He was born of humble circumstances and gave the perfect example of service and righteousness, walking before His Father with a broken heart and a contrite spirit, suffering pains and afflictions and temptations of every kind, yet He never ceded to sin. Being thus pure He qualified Himself to make Himself an offering for sin. In the Garden of Gethsemane, He suffered for our sins, making possible a remission of our sins. He took upon Him the pains and hurt of all men that have ever lived and have yet to live, that He might know how to succor them in their need, and bind up the broken hearted. These things I know, for I myself have felt His power to purify of sin, His matchless peace that comes to those who suffer, and I testify that this power is very, very real. After suffering in Gethsemane, He was imprisoned, judged unlawfully and delivered up to be given an ignominious and horrible death. Crucifiction, the death consigned to thieves and assasins was decreed on the only human being to walk blamelessly on this earth, even the creator of this world, and there, on Calvary, he poured out His whole soul unto death. His great heart litteraly broke for sorrow of the sins of His people. ‘Behold the wounds in His hands His feet, the Blood and tears both mingled down. Did e’re such love and sorrow meet, or thorns compose so rich a crown?’After three days in the sepulchre, Jesus Christ, the Annointed One ressurrected to life and immortality. I testify, with the energy of my living soul, that He does, indeed, live. And by so living, all men shall live again, raised from corruption to incorruption, from death to endless life, then to be judged by the very being that suffered their cause. As a ressurrected being, He still lives, He still loves and He still speaks. After the long darkness of apostasy and absence of His holy Priesthood and men called after His holy order, He and our Eternal Father appeared to Joseph Smith and called him to be an Elias or restorer of the fulness of the Gospel. Jesus Christ has spoken again and sent forth angels to teach men the Plan of Salvation and ordain men to His Holy Order to teach these things to the rest of the children of men. I have been called to this Order, and having recieved an holy calling and ordinance, I testify, in the very name of Jesus Christ, that Jesus Christ lives. All men can grow in His holy light through repentance and holy works, and see that light grow brighter and brighter until the perfect day. As I ponder His amazing sacrifice, I am want to sing the words; ‘Love so amazing, so divine demands my heart, my life, my all.’  That all that read may find the grace of this Jesus and reach His peace and salvation is my prayer, in the sacred name of Jesus Christ.                                    AMENJoseph Levi Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Agronomica
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:48:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronomicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 28 Jul 2008 14:40:04 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CarvalhoAgronomicaZona FlorianopolisDear President Queiroz,             This week passed by very fast.  We are getting better at contacting references and finding new people.  We  have also been blessed with people who are attending church regularly.  This week I decided to read Acts in portuguese.  The Bible hás always been hard for me to understand in portuguese, but to my surprise, I’m getting better.  As I passed through chapters fifteen to the end, I was impressed with how much Paul loved the people of the cities where he passed and even had a farewell to bear testimony one last time to his friends and the leaders of the church in their respective places.  He knew that he wouldn’t see them again in mortality and that there would be apostasy soon after his leaving, so he bore his testimony and prayed for them.  It never occurred to me how much Paul loved the people he met in his missions. Elder Carvalho and I discussed the progress of our area this morning and decided to make some goals for the area and how we will improve our work as well.  Our ward seems very stagnate.  There are no youth, the majority of the ward is composed of students or young couples and almost all the men are already high priests.  Yet the people here seem to do nothing but go to church, and consequently they are prone to weakening testimony.  We’ve decided to help them out and pass by peoples houses that dont know us and leave messages and invitations for service.  One of the members here hás started to help us out alot as a result of our visiting him a few times.  He is a member of the bishopric and seems a very strong member, but he says that he was feeling weak and spiritually stagnate, and even talked to the bishop about it.  But after our passing by a coulple of times and after going with us to teach, he feels remarkably better.  In the quiet heart is hidden sorrow that the eye cant see.  If the members start helping out, the spirituality of the ward will grow, according to what President Benson says in the end of PMG chapter 1.  We want to start helping out the members and then they should start going with us to teach.Elder Carvalho is doing well and I am seeing a difference in his attitude as he thinks more about the work and less about other things that dont matter.  He is progressing well.This week our numbers were less than pleasing, seeing that an entire family that was marked  for baptism moved away and we put off our contacts until when there was no time left to do them.  We will do much better this week.  Our numbers this week are as follows;Bapt/conf..................................0/0Bapt marc.................................7/3Pesq na igr................................4Liç c membro...........................15Novos pesq...............................15Contatos....................................88Lemb s dis.................................90%Qualificar p espírito..................100%Have a good week.     Love Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Agronômica
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:49:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronômicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 7 Jul 2008 13:58:02 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CarvalhoAgronômicaZona FlorianópolisDear President Quieroz,        It was good to meet you on wednesday and it was a good experience.  This week was a good week for me, even though it isnt particularly shown in our numbers.  My testimony of the divine help we recieve as missionaries was strengthened through this weeks experiences.        Elder Carvalho is doing well.  After conference on Wed. I noticed a marked difference in the way he teaches and focuses in the missionary work.  Before, he seemed to have alot of lightheartedness, and at times lightindedness, and didnt really think about what it was that we were doing, but now he seems to focus on and think about our investigators and how he can help them.  He teaches differently and has begun to give up saying the same things over and over, and to just bear testimony about what he says, pricipally because he studies those things, and they therefore are treasured up in his heart.  I dont know what you said to him, but I think it made a great difference.  He is an excellent missionary, and his good traits are coming out and his potential is being realized.        After zone conference, alot of time was wasted in getting back to our areas due to the strike, and we got home at eight o clock, which left us only one hour to work and all our appointments, which were all late of course as we had planned to be back and working at 16:00.  So it was impossibe to get to any of our marked appointments in Saco Grande due to the strike-its a two hour walk to the other side of the bay where our appointments were- we were going to have to work in our own neighborhood and we dont have any investigators here in Trindade, so I was pretty much at loss for what to do.  So I prayed.  I asked for us to be able to find someone that was needing our message and that we could be led to.  I felt like we should go to a neighborhood on the other side of Morro da Cruz, (Serrinha) so we started walking there and after fifteen minutes, I stopped, because there was still another fifteen minutes to walk and by the time we got there we would have only ten minutes to teach and then another half an hour walk to get home again.  So I said another prayer and decided to go up the street to our right, and it seemed familiar, so I kept going, felt like we should go left, then left again, and found a house of an investigator whose daughter is a member and had asked us not to come by any more when I first got here in May, due to problems with her husband, and consequently after serving with my last companion who showed me the area for only one transfer, I had no idea where it was that she lived.  So I explained the situation to my companion and asked him if we should knock.  He said it was up to me, but he didtnt think it was a particularly great idea, so we walked to the street corner and stopped to talk about what to do from there, but I really didnt know if we ought to not pass by that house, so we passed in front again, but kept going, and stopped at the other street corner, and decided to pass by one more time, and again.  At last I decided that if the Lord guided us there in the first place, even if that wasnt the intended destination in my mind, we should knock.  So we knocked.  Her husband wasnt there, so she came out and we sang a hymn for her and asked if we could start passing by again, and she said yes.  She said she would also come to church on sunday with her daughter and we marked an FHE in the bishops house on monday.  She said she was  needing the visit and it was meant for us to come that night.  I left feeling happy and gratefull that the Lord guides His servants and that our day was not wasted.  The Lord lives, and as I tell many of the people we teach, because He lives, He has a mouth, and therefore still speaks.  I am greatful to have the truth and to have the influence of the Holy Ghost to give me peace, guidance and knowledge that I need.         We also had four investigators in church, which is the best we have yet achieved here.  When I was in itajai, we managed to get ninteen people in church several times, and after doubling and tripling numbers, we felt sanctified and that our sacrifice was accepted, and here in Florianoplolis, after wearing out our whole souls, we get only four people in church and just barely get our minium standards, yet I feel the same thing as in Itajai.  Some places are harder, but the Lord sees your efforts and blesses you.         Our numbers this week are as follows;Bat/Conf..................0/0Bat marcado..............14/4Pesq na Igreja............4Liç c membro.............12Novos Pesqisadores......17Contatos...................144Lembe-se disto............95%Qualificar p Esp............100%Thank you for all you are doing for us.  We appreciate it and your enthusiasm for helping us succeed.  May the Lord bless you and Sister Queiroz for your sacrifices.  Have a good week.           Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Alo Familia
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:49:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Alo FamiliaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 14 Jul 2008 19:13:49 +0000Dear Family,   This letter will be somewhat short, because usually I write to the president first and save experiences and relevant things and piece them into your emails, but today I wrote the president in English, and I don’t think you would appreciate that as much.  This week as I was preparing training for district meeting (needless to say it was the night before the meeting) I was studying about people who had great successes in their work in the scriptures, for example, Aaron, the son of Mosiah helped in convert thousands of lamanites, including their king, Peter converted and baptized three thousand persons, and king Benjamin succeeded in converting an entire people.  Result of my study;  The three of them used the process of teaching and prophesying (bearing pure testimony), and inviting to action with the promise of specific blessings.  This is of course already stated as a process in the manual Preach My Gospel, but what I discovered is this;  when people feel the absolute yearning for that connection with the unknown deity, for the knowledge of the almighty, when they feel that they are striking on the keys of something familiar that is true, and when they feel the altogether indescribable prick of the spirit in their hearts, they desire to do something.  That only comes after you teach by the power of the spirit, and that power of speech usually follows your train of thought based on what you have studied and is the current focus of your thoughts in regard to things spiritual.  When people feel that you can see it in their eyes and sometimes even ask what it is that they can do.  We can tell them what they can do to achieve that unknown desire and even discover what it is that they are desiring unknowingly.  Its fun to learn things by the spirit.   I’m still alive and doing well and our area is improving slowly but surely as people are FINALLY starting to come to church regularly.     I hope you all have a good week and remember that I love you and pray for you.  You’re all the best.            Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Agronômica
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:49:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronômicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: presidentequeiroz@gmail.comDate: Mon, 14 Jul 2008 18:45:55 +0000Elder AndrewsElder CarvalhoAgronômicaZona FlorianópolisQuerido Presidente Queiroz, Tem sido uma boa semana, vendo que em fim alguns de nossos pesquisadores começaram a progredir e ir para igreja.  Esta vai ser a primeira vez que escrevo em português então desculpe os erros.  Nesta semana eu tenho pensado muito sobre o que eu posso fazer para melhorar em nossos números e crescer o nosso grupo de ensino.  Nossos números com lições com membro presente nunca parecem bem, e de fato sempre são baixos, então pensei no que posso fazer para melhorar.  Parece que se eu tiver um bom planejamento semanal no dia fixo,(sexta-feira) eu vou poder convidar membros um bom tempo antes.  Foi interessante algo que um membro explicou no quorum dos elderes no domingo sobre planejar e preparar antes para pular um obstáculo;  se você ver um obstáculo como um “hurdle” em seu caminho, vai ter que preparar soltar, crescendo em velocidade, porque ao pular mais que 0.25 metros, é necessário que tenha velocidade –que é speed e direção combinado-.  Se esperar pular e preparar até chegar perto do obstáculo, não conseguirá passar sem voltar e adquirir a velocidade exigida.  Que pena a volta.  Acho que vou aplicar isso mais em minha missão, começando com melhor planejamento.  Preparação para reunião de distrito foi muito interessante.  Pensei no que você disse na entrevista sobre como Pedro conseguiu batizar três mil pessoas.  Ao olhar no capítulo 11 de Pregar Meu Evangelho, percebi um padrão no que Pedro, o filho de Mosias Arão, e Rei Benjamin fizeram com prestar testemunho puro, o princípio do que quando pessoas sentiram aquele sede que vem do toque do Espírito Santo, querem, desejam, de todo coração fazer algo.  Nós, como os representantes de Cristo, temos a responsibilidade convidar as pessoas fazer esse “algo”, qual seja, ser batizado, se arrepender, ir à igreja etc., e no processo, prometer as bênçãos da ação dita.  Gosto de ser ensinado pelo espírito.  Se sente muito bem. Elder Carvalho está bem.  Ele tem dificuldades acordar e se levantar de manhã mas está melhorando.  Nós estamos bem com amizade e somos amigos.    Nossa área vai bem.  Sempre é uma luta levar pesquisadores para igreja, mas em fim estamos conseguindo com dois pesquisadores.  Mais um vai começar nesta semana.  Uma metade de nossos pesquisadores com data marcada estão se mudando para outros lugares esta mês, então, este numero vai cair um pouco, mas estamos sendo abençoados com novos pessoas e referencias também.  Os membros estão nos dando referencias agora e o futuro está sorrindo brilhantemente diante nós.  Obrigado por tudo que faz, e esperamos que tudo vai bem com vocês.  Favor, agradeça á Sister Queiroz pelo bolo hoje.  Nossos números são a seguinte;Batismos/Conf.................................0/0Batismos marcados.........................11/4Pesquisadores na igr........................3Lições c membro.............................11Novos Pesquisadores.......................16Contatos...........................................140Lembre-se Disto................................90%Qualificar pelo Espírito.....................100%Boa semana,                c/  amor,      Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews sends you greetings
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:49:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews sends you greetingsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 7 Jul 2008 13:30:20 +0000Dear family,       Im glad you all had a good week, I really enjoyed your letter.  Its fun to hear how Morgan is working with Dad.  Working with Dad was an interresting experience for me, and looking back, I think I could have been a little more proactive when I was working.  I should have asked questions and know what was going on rather than just wait to be told what to do.  But I learned to work.  I got to work in several different environments and what I discovered is that it is fun to put your heart into what you do and feel good about it afterward.  Boy does that sound like an old irish proverb...        We have a member here that we call HomemAranha(SpiderMan), because two weeks ago we were building a house (which by the way is ridiculously more simple than building a house in Lenexa) and he was up in the rafters putting up the roof when he fell from four meters, and broke through the floor.  We call him spiderman because he got up with out a scratch somehow.  He fell some four feet away from me, so when I looked down, I thought he must have died, but to our surprise and relief, he lives on, unbruised.         You shouldnt tell me about what kind of cake you made for Charles birthday, just thinking about it made me drool with homesickness...  Just kidding.  They have some pretty good kinds of food down here, especially when they make stroganov and rice.  Rice and beans grows on you too.  If you go for a day without it, you actually start to crave it.  There are ALOT of italians in the south of Brazil, so there is alot of italian food, and a decent amount of german pastries due to the high german population too.  They dont have peanut butter or maple syrup, and avocados are for making sweets, not guacamole.  But the food is good.        Thats sad that someone in the ward is not in a good situation, especially if I know them.  I hope the situation turns out for the best.  Its good to hear international finance and politics and stuff.  Its interresting.        This week we had zone conference and interviews with our new mission president.  Hes cool and we all like him.  Hes young too; 48 or something.  The bus system was on strike that day, so we rented a van to take us all back to our reaspective areas on the Island, and it was during rush hour, so we all talked and convered and everything for a long time.  It was fun but it also makes you a little homesick for social life, but we survive.  We got home at eight o clock, which left us only one hour to work and all our appointments, which were late of course, were impossibe to get to due to the strike-its a two hour walk to the other side of the bay where our appointments were- we were going to have to work in our own neighborhood and  we dont have any investigators here, so I was pretty much at loss for what to do.  So I prayed.  I asked for us to be able to find someone that was needing our message and that we could be led to.  I felt like we should go to a neighborhood on the other side of Morro da Cruz, so we started walking there and after fifteen minutes, I stopped, because there was still another fifteen minutes to walk and by the time we got there we would have only ten minutes to teach and then another half an hour walk to get home again.  So I said another prayer and decided to go up the street to our right, and it seemed familiar, so I kept going, felt like we should go left, then left again, and found a house of an investigator whose daughter is a member and had asked us not to come by any more when I first got here in May, due to problems with her husband, so I explained the situation to my companion and asked him if we should knock.  He said it was up to me, but he didtnt think it was a particularly great idea, so we walked to the street corner and stopped to talk about what to do from there, but I really didnt know if we ought to not pass by that house, so we passed in front again, but kept going, and stopped at the other street corner, and decided to pass by one more time, and again.  At last I decided that if the Lord guided us there in the first place, even if that wasnt the intended destination in my mind, we should knock.  Her husband wasnt there, so she came out and we sang a hymn for her and asked if we could start passing by again, and she said yes.  She said she would also come to church on sunday with her daughter and we marked an FHE in the bishops house on monday.  She said she was  needing the visit and it was meant for us to come that night.  I left feeling happy and gratefull that the Lord guides His servants and that our day was not wasted.  The Lord lives, and as I tell many of the people we teach, because He lives, He has a mouth, and therefore still speaks.  I am greatful to have the truth and to have the influence of the Holy Ghost to give me peace, guidance and knowledge that I need.         We also had four investigators in church, which is the best we have yet achieved here.  When I was in itajai, we managed to get ninteen people in church several times, and after doubling and tripling numbers, we felt sanctified and that our sacrifice was accepted, and here in Florianoplolis, after wearing out our whole souls, we get only four people in church and just barely get our minium standards, we feel the same thing as in Itajai.  Some places are harder, but the Lord sees your efforts and blesses you.  I love you all and hope you have a good week.            Love Elder Andrews        

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Elder Carvalho is a good missionary and I am trying to help him be a little more independant on how to teach.  I think he thinks that the senionr companion does everything. We now have several investigators that look somewhat possible to be baptize so were happy.        From time to time I get down about our numbers, especially after our successes in Itajai.  At times I wonder what I could do better, and there is always an answer, but I still feel good as I serve people and help them gain hope in and through the atonement of Christ.  Our ward looks perfect when you go to church, but in the quiet heart is hidden sorrow that the eye cant see.  Things are improving and I have a hope that they will continue to improve.      Thank you for all you have done for us, it is much appreciated, and I hope that you finish well.  The fruits of your labors do not end with your last few weeks' numbers, nor your last week or the weeks that follow.  The seeds youve sown will continue to bear fruit long after the tree is gone.  Thank you for the impact and service youve given us, our investigators and to the Lord. ## Subject: Fw: To the Andrews family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:51:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: To the Andrews familyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 9 Jun 2008 18:22:11 +0000Dear family,        It sounds like youre all getting alot of rain up there.  I dont think I have ever seen the creek get up over the bridge on 151st before.  It seems that Charles'  new bike is pretty fancy.  Perhaps a little better than the one he used on his mission.  I met a guy from paraguay last night.  If all goes well, we should be teaching him in the next few weeks.  Elder Eliakim didnt believe me when I told him how you say I go and I fall in Guarani, so I asked the guy how you say it.  ''Ha ha, aha ha-ah ha'' or something like that.          This morning we went to the mission home to play soccer, Florianopolis zone against Sao Jose zone.  We won of course.  My companion can play against three people and always score a goal.  I played goalie and did well enough that they wanted me to stay there for another three hours.  I had fun and got kicked a few times when I jumped on the ball, but it was fun.  I like being in Florianopolis, because on p day we can see people from the other areas close by, especially old companions and friends from the MTC.         Elder Eliakim is still being as great a missionary as he ever was, so that makes it so I have nothing to worry about there.  I think he is ready to be a senior companion as well.  He is a great missionary.  From time to time he gets a little down about people not recieving us any more, or people not keeping commitments, but I think if he has a happy companion he should always be fine.  We get along great.          Our area is on the verge of a breakout in missionary work.  The members are telling us about a number of people they are preparing to recieve the lessons from us.  The members are excited to give us lunches, so thats a blessing to us as well.  I think it helps out a great deal to be in such frequent contact with the missionaries.  It helps with referrals.  Its really hard to get people to go to church.  This week Im going to ask for help from several members to pick up investigators.  I find that when members go with us to teach, it does more than prepare for better retention, it also helps with people getting to church.  We have a number of investigators that are getting more and more ready for baptism, they just need to get started going to church.       I love you all and hope you all have a good summer.  Im enjoying the fall and winter down here.  Heat is not pleasant with leather shoes long pants and a tie.  I prefer the cold.  Have a good week.              Love Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Olaaaaa
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:51:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: OlaaaaaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 16 Jun 2008 14:17:02 +0000Dear family,       This week I tried to be more proactive and apply some of the things we have been taught but never seem to use.  It seems like people suck up information like active charcoal but applying it is something that takes enormous effort.  We started to use what President Cardon from the CTM calls Faith of Power to achieve the goal of baptizing someone that seems not to want to be baptized and sees no need for it while every relative he has is baptized or is getting baptized.  So we put together some goals for us and a few other things and asked the Lord for help.  Result; Wanderley -our investigator-went to church even though there was a soccer game to watch and his wife (who is a less active member) was sick.  I think there is a connection there.  Something I want to apply more is a system of goal making based off of the baptismal questions involving what we need to do, what the Lord needs to do and what the investiagators need to do in order to achieve conversion.  It just takes alot of time to set up and alot of paper, but it should give us a little of balast to get our teaching organized better for the benefit of the investigator.       Elder Eliakim will be transferred this week and E. Carvalho will take his place.  E. Carvalho is also brazilian so I can still practice my portuguese.  I have greatly enjoyed being companions with E. Eliakim.  He is a good missionary.  Everyone here in the agronomica ward will miss him including me.  I am always a little bit nervous with showing an area to another companion, but I am sure I will survive.        Our area is going well, we have alot more investigators and one of them, Everton, came to church on his own (this being a miracle) with his whole family.  Everton seemed to be along the lines of a philosophy major when we met him more than a month ago, but has slowly been changing, recieving a softer heart.  He lost one of his children a few years ago a week after being born and lost faith in God.  Before that, he had been courageous in standing up for God, but lost faith in losing a child.  At times, I feel a strong impression that I really am sent to teach these specific people, so that my personal experiences can bless their lives as I relate what has happened in my own life.  As I began my mission, I kept my own mothers death as a secret, afraid of making others uncomfortable, but the experiences that I passed through following her passing are of great value in helping others forgive and accept the will of the Lord.  When my own mother died, I knew there was a reason and something that I was supposed to learn from the experience, but I had to wait for three years to get an answer, and if it had not happened, I could not have gained my testimony of the Living Christ, nor His indescribable capacity to bind up the broken hearted, and thus be empowered to bear greater testimony of Him as I serve a mission.  Everton came to church.        Paraguay beat Brazil in soccer yesterday.  Que vergonha.  I hope you all have a good week and remember that I love you all.           Boa semanaElder Andrews

With the dedication and celebration in Curitiba it was a little difficult to get lessons with members present, but we managed to get by. ## Subject: Fw: Dear Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:52:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 2 Jun 2008 14:08:44 +0000Dear Family,       This week was a little rough, especially in getting people to church and teaching with members.  There was a temple dedication and celebration on saturday and sunday, so almost all the members were up north in Curitiba for the week end, which is prime teaching time, so we suffered a little this week with lessons with members present, but this week should be alot better.  Sacrament was immediately after the temple dedication broadcasted in downtown Florianopolis, so we didnt get any investigators to watch it with us.  There was an american there who was on business selling surveillance systems who dosnt speak portuguese, so I offered to translate for him.  Translating is portuguese to english is hard.  Luckilly most of the presentation was translated from english to portuguese, so I survived the dedication, but testimony meeting was a little different.        We ate lunch with one of the members yesterday who is a professional cook and maid, so she really knows how to make good food.  She made a carrot cake for me since it was my birthday, so it was a good day.  Sounds like the young men had a good time on the high adventure.  Im glad they did something different this year.  This week in zone conference a sister and I will sing I believe in Christ, so weve been trying to put something special together, I wanted to do a key change on the last verse, but it didnt work out unless we went up a halfstep to e flat major.  It sounds good, but singing tenor gets hard when you hit the peak of your singing range.  I think itll turn out well though.        People in Florianopolis are a little harder to teach, so Im having a hard time deciding whether to keep with some of our investigators that arent progressing or not.  Its a hard decision to make sometimes.  It was good to hear the prophet yesterday.  Im glad we have a prophet who can speak to the Lord on our behalf and I am glad to have a testimony.  I hope you all have a good week and pray for you.           Love Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: My testimony
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:52:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: My testimonyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: ruthzahller@earthlink.netDate: Mon, 26 May 2008 18:20:42 +0000Dear Grandma,         This week was our last interview with Pres Dansie.  He asked us to write our testimony of Jesus Christ for him.  I figured it dosnt hurt to send it to family either, so Ill share it with you.  I think it is appropriate that you hear/read the testimony of your posterity and know that your efforts have an effect in my life.  Thank you for all you have done to help me in adqiring a personal testimony.  I love you and pray for you too.         Jesus Christ was chosen before this earth was created to be our savior and redeemer. He is the god of the old testament and the great I AM; Jehovah. All things exist by the grace of His glory. He is the Light and the Life of the world, a light that is endless, that never can be darkened, a light that gives life to all creatures in existance. He took upon Himself flesh and blood and walked among us, even the light which ilumines our lives, yet he was rejected, for men loved darkness and reject the light. He walked among us and grew grace for every grace, light upon light until He recieved a fulness of the Glory of the Father, and was and is One with the Father. He was pure, clean from all sin, and was worthy to fulfill His mission and bring to pass the eternal life and imortality of mankind by means of making atonement with His bretheren, and our very Eternal Father.It was He who created the earth and filled it with light. He was chosen from the beginning to overcome the natural effects of the fall and allow us, His bretheren, to be redeemed from physical death through resurrection and spiritual death on conditions of following His Gospel of Faith on His name, Repentance, Baptism, Baptism by the reciept of the gift of the Holy Ghost and abiding in accordance with all other ordinances of His Gospel. He is the God of the Old Testament, the Hope of Israel, the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel.He was born to Mary, a virgin, and is the very Son of God in the flesh. He was born of humble circumstances and gave the perfect example of service and righteousness, walking before His Father with a broken heart and a contrite spirit, suffering pains and afflictions and temptations of every kind, yet He never ceded to sin. Being thus pure He qualified Himself to make Himself an offering for sin. In the Garden of Gethsemane, He suffered for our sins, making possible a remission of our sins. He took upon Him the pains and hurt of all men that have ever lived and have yet to live, that He might know how to succor them in their need, and bind up the broken hearted. These things I know, for I myself have felt His power to purify of sin, His matchless peace that comes to those who suffer, and I testify that this power is very, very real. After suffering in Gethsemane, He was imprisoned, judged unlawfully and delivered up to be given an ignominious and horrible death. Crucifiction, the death consigned to thieves and assasins was decreed on the only human being to walk blamelessly on this earth, even the creator of this world, and there, on Calvary, he poured out His whole soul unto death. His great heart litteraly broke for sorrow of the sins of His people. ‘Behold the wounds in His hands His feet, the Blood and tears both mingled down. Did e’re such love and sorrow meet, or thorns compose so rich a crown?’After three days in the sepulchre, Jesus Christ, the Annointed One ressurrected to life and immortality. I testify, with the energy of my living soul, that He does, indeed, live. And by so living, all men shall live again, raised from corruption to incorruption, from death to endless life, then to be judged by the very being that suffered their cause. As a ressurrected being, He still lives, He still loves and He still speaks. After the long darkness of apostasy and absence of His holy Priesthood and men called after His holy order, He and our Eternal Father appeared to Joseph Smith and called him to be an Elias or restorer of the fulness of the Gospel. Jesus Christ has spoken again and sent forth angels to teach men the Plan of Salvation and ordain men to His Holy Order to teach these things to the rest of the children of men. I have been called to this Order, and having recieved an holy calling and ordinance, I testify, in the very name of Jesus Christ, that Jesus Christ lives. All men can grow in His holy light through repentance and holy works, and see that light grow brighter and brighter until the perfect day. As I ponder His amazing sacrifice, I am want to sing the words; ‘Love so amazing, so divine demands my heart, my life, my all.’ This is my testimony, and from henceforth let no man trouble me; for I bear in my body the marks of the Lord Jesus. That all that read may find the grace of this Jesus and reach His peace and salvation is my prayer, in the sacred name of Jesus Christ.                                                   AMENJoseph Levi Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: An email from Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:52:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: An email from Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 26 May 2008 18:10:33 +0000Dear family,       This week was good, we ate lunch with the bishop and I got to know him a bit better and I like him.  The members here have a good spirit about them and I feel alot of charity and care for them.  I particularly like going to sacrament meeting here.  I am trying to incorporate more testemony into my teaching and use what I study in what I teach.  It dosnt allow for alot of study on deep doctrines, so Im glad.  The bishop here says that nintey percent of apostasia(false doctrine) comes from serving missions.  Some missionaries after studying PMG(preach my gospel) and the Book of Mormon so many times start to think they know it all already and look for other things to study about.  That dosnt really help out with your testimony, and can lead to false doctrine.  Ever since I arrived on the mission it has been stressed in my mind the doctrines of the Gospel of Jesus Christ, its necessity for salvation and exaltation, and its connections with basic principles.  I love to think and ponder about the connections and interrelations of the Gospel ordinances and the rest of the plan of salvation.         Elder Eliakim is an excellent missionary and I enjoy hearing his testimony every day.  We get along well and teach well together.  The members seem to like him very much.        We are in the stage of finding people in our area.  Sometimes I dont quite know when it is appropriate to stop teaching people.  Some people dont progress.  I think I will use as a measure the willingness they have to go to church and their willingness to make and keep commitments.  We continue to find good people to teach, but I feel that I should pray a little harder -or alot harder- to find the elect of the Lord who are prepared.  A 22 year-old young man stopped us in the street the other day and asked us what he needs to do to become a member of our church.  Needless to say we got his adress and went to visit him two days later.  He and his mother are now marked for baptism, though I have suspicions about the word of wisdom.  I think I am going to apply the proverb 'pedi e recebereis' this week and see if we cant get a few more lessons with members who can help us out in getting people to church.  It worked in Itajai so it should work to some degree here as well.  It turns out that the elders quorum president here is one of Chris Challis´ companions from when he served in Belo Horizonte.  I remember Chris telling me about Rafael Coelho and his visit to florianopolis about two months before I came down here.  Small world.        Yesterday in church I looked around and saw alot of good members of the church and felt grateful for them and their love for each other.  I love to feel the pure love of Christ enter my heart and feel to some degree for others the way He does.      I hope you all have a good week.  I love you all.          Love Joseph

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw:
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:52:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject:From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: fern.woodbury@gmail.comDate: Mon, 26 May 2008 18:20:00 +0000Dear Grandma,         This week was our last interview with Pres Dansie.  He asked us to write our testimony of Jesus Christ for him.  I figured it dosnt hurt to send it to family either, so Ill share it with you.  I think it is appropriate that you hear/read the testimony of your posterity and know that your efforts have an effect in my life.  Thank you for all you have done to help me in adqiring a personal testimony.  I love you and pray for you too.         Jesus Christ was chosen before this earth was created to be our savior and redeemer. He is the god of the old testament and the great I AM; Jehovah. All things exist by the grace of His glory. He is the Light and the Life of the world, a light that is endless, that never can be darkened, a light that gives life to all creatures in existance. He took upon Himself flesh and blood and walked among us, even the light which ilumines our lives, yet he was rejected, for men loved darkness and reject the light. He walked among us and grew grace for every grace, light upon light until He recieved a fulness of the Glory of the Father, and was and is One with the Father. He was pure, clean from all sin, and was worthy to fulfill His mission and bring to pass the eternal life and imortality of mankind by means of making atonement with His bretheren, and our very Eternal Father.It was He who created the earth and filled it with light. He was chosen from the beginning to overcome the natural effects of the fall and allow us, His bretheren, to be redeemed from physical death through resurrection and spiritual death on conditions of following His Gospel of Faith on His name, Repentance, Baptism, Baptism by the reciept of the gift of the Holy Ghost and abiding in accordance with all other ordinances of His Gospel. He is the God of the Old Testament, the Hope of Israel, the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel.He was born to Mary, a virgin, and is the very Son of God in the flesh. He was born of humble circumstances and gave the perfect example of service and righteousness, walking before His Father with a broken heart and a contrite spirit, suffering pains and afflictions and temptations of every kind, yet He never ceded to sin. Being thus pure He qualified Himself to make Himself an offering for sin. In the Garden of Gethsemane, He suffered for our sins, making possible a remission of our sins. He took upon Him the pains and hurt of all men that have ever lived and have yet to live, that He might know how to succor them in their need, and bind up the broken hearted. These things I know, for I myself have felt His power to purify of sin, His matchless peace that comes to those who suffer, and I testify that this power is very, very real. After suffering in Gethsemane, He was imprisoned, judged unlawfully and delivered up to be given an ignominious and horrible death. Crucifiction, the death consigned to thieves and assasins was decreed on the only human being to walk blamelessly on this earth, even the creator of this world, and there, on Calvary, he poured out His whole soul unto death. His great heart litteraly broke for sorrow of the sins of His people. ‘Behold the wounds in His hands His feet, the Blood and tears both mingled down. Did e’re such love and sorrow meet, or thorns compose so rich a crown?’After three days in the sepulchre, Jesus Christ, the Annointed One ressurrected to life and immortality. I testify, with the energy of my living soul, that He does, indeed, live. And by so living, all men shall live again, raised from corruption to incorruption, from death to endless life, then to be judged by the very being that suffered their cause. As a ressurrected being, He still lives, He still loves and He still speaks. After the long darkness of apostasy and absence of His holy Priesthood and men called after His holy order, He and our Eternal Father appeared to Joseph Smith and called him to be an Elias or restorer of the fulness of the Gospel. Jesus Christ has spoken again and sent forth angels to teach men the Plan of Salvation and ordain men to His Holy Order to teach these things to the rest of the children of men. I have been called to this Order, and having recieved an holy calling and ordinance, I testify, in the very name of Jesus Christ, that Jesus Christ lives. All men can grow in His holy light through repentance and holy works, and see that light grow brighter and brighter until the perfect day. As I ponder His amazing sacrifice, I am want to sing the words; ‘Love so amazing, so divine demands my heart, my life, my all.’ This is my testimony, and from henceforth let no man trouble me; for I bear in my body the marks of the Lord Jesus. That all that read may find the grace of this Jesus and reach His peace and salvation is my prayer, in the sacred name of Jesus Christ.                                                   AMENJoseph Levi Andrews

I am grateful for my parents willingness to give up worldly things and goods to bring up children in righteousness. I know Jesus Christ lives. [jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, AgronômicaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: mp8-dansiel@ldsmail.netDate: Mon, 26 May 2008 18:03:14 +0000Elder AndrewsElder EliakimAgronômicaZona FlorianópolisDear President Dansie,        I enjoyed speaking with you at interviews.  This week was good, we ate lunch with the bishop and I got to know him a bit better and I like him.  The members here have a good spirit about them and I feel alot of charity and care for them.  I particularly like going to sacrament meeting here.  I am trying to incorporate more testemony into my teaching and use what I study in what I teach.  It dosnt allow for alot of study on deep doctrines, so Im glad.  The bishop here says that nintey percent of apostasia(false doctrine) comes from serving missions.  Some missionaries after studying PMG and the Book of Mormon so many times start to think they know it all already and look for other things to study about.  That dosnt really help out with your testimony, and can lead to false doctrine.  Ever since I arrived on the mission it has been stressed in my mind the doctrines of the Gospel of Jesus Christ, its necessity for salvation and exaltation, and its connections with basic principles.  I love to think and ponder about the connections and interrelations of the Gospel ordinances and the rest of the plan of salvation.         Elder Eliakim is an excellent missionary and I enjoy hearing his testimony every day.  We get along well and teach well together.  The members seem to like him very much.        We are in the stage of finding people in our area.  Sometimes I dont quite know when it is appropriate to stop teaching people.  Some people dont progress.  I think I will use as a measure the willingness they have to go to church and their willingness to make and keep commitments.  We continue to find good people to teach, but I feel that I should pray a little harder -or alot harder- to find the elect of the Lord who are prepared.  A 22 year-old young man stopped us in the street the other day and asked us what he needs to do to become a member of our church.  Needless to say we got his adress and went to visit him two days later.  He and his mother are now marked for baptism, though I have suspicions about the word of wisdom.  I think I am going to apply the proverb 'pedi e recebereis' this week and see if we cant get a few more lessons with members who can help us out in getting people to church.  It worked in Itajaí so it should work to some degree here as well.        Yesterday in church I looked around and saw alot of good members of the church and felt grateful for them and their love for each other.  I love to feel the pure love of Christ enter my heart and feel to some degree for others the way He does.        I hope you have a good week and the spirit is close to you.  Thank you for all you do to help us in our work.  We love you and appreciate you, and will miss you when youre gone. ## Subject: Fw: Hellooooo!
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:54:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Hellooooo!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 28 Apr 2008 15:43:20 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai 2Zona ItajaiDear Family,       This week passed by very fast.  My companion and I were rushed to contact our investigators with zone conference and d-day all in the same week, but I think we managed to get along pretty well and teach with a powerfull spirit to our investigators.  I feel a little more receptive to the spirit and easier to feel charity for people and it helps significantly with what I do.  This week I made the goal to have a doctrine of the day on which to ponder and teach if I have to give a short message.  It also helps to keep your mind on the saviour.  On thursday I studied Baptism in Preach my Gospel, and I didnt make it past the phrase ''baptism is the first ordinance of the Gospel of Jesus Christ.  An ordinance is a ceremony or rite that shows we make a covenant with Heavenly Father.''  I started to think about what a ceremony is.  The three common characteristics of ceremonies are as folows; someone in authority realizes the ceremony and oversees the covenants, the parties involved and witnesses.  This is true in regard to weddings, change of command in the military, award ceremonies etc.  The Change of command in a rifle company in the US ARMY is notably interresting.  While an officer may recieve a certain rank, such as Captain, this does not necessarily mean he is in a given command, but must recieve command over a body of men.  When this happens, there is a ceremony in front of the group recieveing a new commander, showing that from the moment the flag of the rifle company is passed from one Captain to another, the new captain is in command.  While paper work has to be filled out to authorize the change, the change is in effect from the ceremony on.  When we read section 128 of the Doctrine and covenants, we see quite plainly that we are judged according to men in the flesh (here we could say that the ceremony of baptism is to show to the witnesses or congregation and to God that we enter into the covenants of baptism) and according to God in the spirit, by what is written.  The ordinances of the Temple could be seen like a captain, who already possesing AUTHORITY, recieves an Oath and a Covenant in the presence of the supreme command and is endowed with POWER from on high.  Ordinances are absolutley necessary in our knowing God the Eternal Father and His son, Jesus Christ.       A few days ago we visited a family we are teaching who are going through financial problems and are struggleing with smoking and have been a little depressed with a slow down in their progress, so we visited them to help them.  I dint feel particularly inspired to teach on a given doctrine so I just asked them if they had any questions.  They didnt say any thing so I just waited.  And waited.  I noticed that the wife had tears in her Eyes.  So I waited some more and Roberto started to tell me how htey were passing through difficulties and how we hear alot about people being called or chosen and how they didnt know if they were among the chosen.  They said alot of other things as well, but I dont remember them.  I told them how I had passed through many problems, heartaches and times of hopelessness myself and I read them a scripture that helped me meny times in D+C 121.  I felt many things and spoke alot of things from my heart and told them that we are the ones that choose if we are chosen.  Some hear and turn away from the voice of the spirit, but others choose to embrace it.  The Lord, it seems, does not care so much about achievment so mush as he does about what we are doing.  Then we gave each of them a blessing and I prayed for them.  I love to pray for others and feel charity fill my heart as I act in the name of the Savior and speak his will and love for others.        On saturday night we got back from D-day in Balneario and We passed by a members house to ask if they could teach with us, but he was a bit sick and they offered a snack which we accepted.  I think there was some high tention in the home, and their 20 year old son yelled at his mom.  I felt a little saddened at this as well as Elder Pimentel.  We both sat down on the couch to see where we could go to teach, and our plans seemed futile, so we prayed for inspiration on what to do.  I didnt have any ideas and Elder Pimentel was still praying. Then he stopped and asked if we could leave a message with the family.  Half of what follows is what E. pimentel told me afterwards, so, while he was praying to know where we should go, he felt that we shluld stay just where we were.  So following the spirit, he took the hymn book and grabbed Rafael(the son who yelled at his mom) and asked him to sing I Am A Child of God with him.  so the two of them sang and then the two of them kneeled and prayed, and after that E Pimentel told Rafael to give his Mother a hug and ask forgivness and never disrepect her again.  As my companino did all this, he did it with a profound humility and perfect love, which not even a 20 yearold young man could deny and I did not see Elder Pimentel speaking, But Jesus Christ.  After that, Elder pimentel spoke to the the family and asked them to love each other and never let that happen again in their home.  He spoke of his won family and how he showed love to them every day and eles acobraram quando ele nao mostrou seu amor para eles.  He said that this family was sealed and they should honor and cherish that blessing.  He said none of his family but him is a member so he dosnt know the blessing of having an eternal family, and he pointed to me and said that I do and I have a great blessing in my life.  I felt powerfully a deep sorrow and an even deeper desire to help E Pimentels family recieve this blessing.  I also bore testimony of how we should cultivate love in the home, and how if we dont, we may drive those we love from us, especially through judgment and sarcarsm.  I asked if I could pray at the end, and I prayed for each of the people in the family present and E. Pimentels family as well.  We have acted in the name of Jesus Christ this week and we feel the sanctifying power of representing him as best we can through Faith Hope and Charity.  Humility is the key, and as it says in Hel 3:35 We deliver our hearts to Him through Prayer.  Every thing begins with prayer.  It is my testimony that we may be sanctifyied through our prayer, humility, Faith hope and especially Charity, and that we are qualified for hte work when we wholly take upon us the Holy name of Christ.       I love you

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Itajai 2, Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:54:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Itajai 2, Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: mp8-dansiel@ldsmail.netDate: Mon, 5 May 2008 18:59:53 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai 2Zona ItajaiDear President Dansie,      This week was rough, due to alot of rain and investigators not being home, but after working hard, calling lots of members etc, we actually made it through all right.  These last two weeks have been a little rough, espiecially in the way of getting our investigators to church, and our numbers had fallen a good deal too, so I was a little worried that we might finish the transfer badly, so we worked a little harder, walked a little faster and in the end we were blessed with good numbers.  I have taken note that when your investigators dont go to church for a few weeks, they weaken and you have to start a few things over again.  I have been studying the Oath and Covenant of the Priesthood and its relation with the temple ceremonies with a result of a more keen awareness of what it means to be called as a missionary, what my authority and obligations are etc.  I feel more empowered in knowing that I am endued with power from on high.       Transfers are interresting things as you feel sorrow in parting with friends, but I never feel a real loss of hope for the future.  Its kind of like getting a mission call all over again.  Your heart aches at leaving, but when you hear where youre going, the spirit give you a confirmation that that is where youre needed and you desire to go there.  I thank you for letting Elder Pimentel and I serve together for two transfers, I have learned and grown much with him.  I also thank you for not putting him with a great fubecca.  Elder Bateman is a good missionary, or at least was in the CTM.  Im sure they will do great here.  I will miss our bishop here.  We didnt spend a whole lot of time wiht him, but alot of the members are kind of scared to be social with him since hes on the swat team.       The area here is doing well, we still have a few people that have to quit smoking and others that are waiting for the paper work for marraige.  During the next two transfers there should be some eight or nine baptisms if we all keep working as hard as possible.  We are processing the paper work for seven marraiges.  That will be fun.  I have seen miracles here, and have found many of hte Honest in Heart.        My uncle wrote a song a few years back wanting to portray Joseph Smiths vision of zion;          I see our Zion, with hills surrounded          Where evry family will dwell in peace          A place of beauty and pure devotion          Where praise to Him will never cease          There are no poor or hurt among us          The meek and weary will there have rest          And every heart that has been broken          Is surely healed in righteousness          Oh can you see the place Im seeing ?          Oh can you hear Him call you there?          Oh can you feel His arms around you          And His pure love find everywhere?          We shall fall down and kiss His feet,          Be crowned with glory, pure light well find          And heavenly angels will throng the temples          And join with us to save mankind          Oh can you see the place Im seeing?          Oh can you hear Him call you there?          Oh can you feel His arms around you          And His pure love find evrywhere?            Oh can you see the place Im seeing?          What we see now is just the start,          Go share this news with evry people          And gather in the pure in heart.       I wish the members here could feel the vision of Zion, of being one in Heart and Mind, having no poor among us.  Some people just think that the church exists to help us financially as an organization, and their testimony rests on this, but through the Ordinances of the melkisedek priesthood, or through the temple, we have the opportunity to know God.      ''...Eis que [Deus] viu que era conviniente que os homens soubessem das coisas que decretara para eles.  Enviou, portanto, anjos para conversarem com eles, os quais fizeram com que os homens contemplassem sua gloria.  E dali em diante começaram a invocar seu nome; portanto Deus conversou com os homens e revelou lhes o plano de redenção... (Alma 12:28-30)     ''E ... desaria chamar vossa atenção para a epoca em que o Senhor transmitiu estes mandamentos a seus filhos; e quisera que lembrasseis de que o Senhor Deus ordenou sacerdotes segundo a sua santa ordem, que era segundo a ordem de seu Filho, para que ensinassem estas coisas ao povo.'' (Alma 13:1)      We have recieved an endowment with power from on high with a responsibility to teach these things -the plan of salvation and the Gospel of Jesus Christ, which has been restored in these latter days- to all people, and we have been called with a holy calling and ordained with a holy ordinance, taking upon us the name of Christ.  My responsibility is very, very great, but if I can have faith, hope and charity, which charity and hope can come through a remission of sins, I can do His work effectivley.  So seeing this, Whenever I read the scriptures, it seems like all im reading are the words- repent. repent. repent. repent. etc.  I am grateful for the glorious opportunity to have the Gospel in my life, and the even greater opportunity to be a missionary and diciple of Jesus Christ the Son of God, being called of him to declare his word among his people, that they may have everlasting life.      Our numbers this week were;Bapt/conf............0/0bapt marc............21/9pesq na igr...........13liç c memb...........34novos pesq...........26contatos..............142qualificar.............100%lem se disto..........90%Have a great week.  Thank you for what you do to help us every day.

## Subject: Fw: This is a letter to y'all
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:54:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: This is a letter to y'allFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 12 May 2008 18:57:17 +0000Dear family,      it was good to tald to you all yesterday, it sounds as though every body is doing well.       Transfers are always an interresting experience if not absolutly humbling.  Its interresting to show up in a given area and not have a clue whats going on and still work.  There arent a whole lot of people in the teaching pool here, but were looking for people and I am trying to find new ways to find and teach the honest in heart.        Elder Eliakim is a great missionary and I like to hear him bear his testimony.  He has a purity that is undisputable.  I am always glad and grateful to have a companion that works and teaches with testimony.  It was good to talk with our families, and as he was talking with his family, it was apparent that he loves his parents.  He told me afterwards that during sacrament meeting he felt strongly what was being said about mothers, but his thoughts were drawn more toward me and my own Mother.  So he gave me a hug and told me he felt that surely my Mother must be proud of and happy with me.  That meant alot to me.  I am glad to have a good companion all over again.  We both have eyebrows para caramba, so we make quite the team.        This area is a little richer than Itajaí II, and today after playing soccer with the rest of the zone, we found a music shop with a cello, so I stopped in and asked if I could play.  When I asked for a bow they gave me a violin bow.  I like it here.  Places that are richer generally are a little harder so Im feeling that there should be a few more struggles for me here, but with the help of the LORD combined with improved and strengthened faith, it should give fruit.  There arent really a whole lot of people showing good prospects for baptism or even being marked for baptism, but we found a woman this week who should be perfect.  She lives alone, has no addictions, already knew members a few years back and loves to recieve our message.  We also found a moça who was baptized in Porto Alegre, but moved out to the middle of no-where, where the church still didnt exist and then moved here, but never found the church.  She still reads the Book of Mormon every other night and as far as I can tell is still worthy.  What a blessing.  It seems like every person that goes inactive ends up moving in with someone and starts smoking and has to go through a whole lot of repentance to come back to church.  Also, one of our investigators who had been somewhat reluctant to change-from what E Eliakim tells me- decided to get married, stop smoking and get baptized, along with renew his broken family ties as well.  In short, even though there is alot of work to be done here in regards to marked baptisms and people going to church, the Lord provides a way and if we sanctify our hearts through charity, our covenants of the Priesthood and pure testimony.       I know Jesus Christ lives.  I have a sacred promise made to Him to fulfill and I will always seek to improve my methods of service, that through Him, I might fill the world with light.  I love him.                      Love, Joseph

## Subject: Fw: To the family Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:55:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: To the family AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 21 Apr 2008 15:57:00 +0000Dear Family,      This week was tough, but I survived.  We had trouble getting the members to make visits this week and when they did go with us it seemed that nobody was home anyways.  We did a service project that ate up a bunch of our time, but we managed to rip out a trunk/root of an avacado tree.  It takes alot of digging and axeifying, and leaves you with alot of sore muscles if youre out of the habit of physical labor.  We now have six marraiges planned to take place in late may and all of june, so our bishop will know how to marry people verry well by the end of summer.  One of our investigators managed to convince her ''husband'' to marry her and made him get down on his knees and propose to her.  She called us afterwards to tell us that he said yes.  I congratulated her for being a bride, or for ficar noiva.  Its funny that even after living together for twenty years and having four children, there is still doubt over whether they will say yes or no, and that the doubt is actually valid!        I think I will be transferred before mothers day, its pretty rare for people to stay in an area for more than six months.  Im pretty sure I can call you guys or you can call me using skype these days.  Its alot cheaper so I hear.  I will look into that as it may be better for me to call you guys on mothers day.      I think Ive forgotten what the national convention is and what it does.  Did Dad put his name in for election or did someone else?  That would be really interresting for him to make it in as a delegate.  When I did the whole model UN thing a few years back I enjoyed the chaos of being on a committee, making resolutions and enemies etc.  It can be alot of fun.        Yesterday we had a stunning two investigators in church, and only because we chased them down in the rain and brang them to church.  If not, we would have had zip.  Rain is bad news for missnionaries on sundays.  Last week we had ten times as many investigators in church.  We call this the peak and trough effect found in waves, which means -hopefully- this week will be better.  Itajai is a city built on the plain, in fact, it is the flattest place ive ever seen in my life, and I grew up in kansas, so it floods extremely easily.  We gave up walking for swimming yesterday...        Well I hope youre all having a great time up there, Im enjoying the cold again while youre getting into the warm part of the year.  Here in six months well all want to trade places again.  Have a good week, and remember to pray, read the scriptures and take the sacrament every week.  Its all true.  I guarantee it.            Love, Elder Andrews

Most of our plans fell through and progress in general was slowed.  I fear for alot of our investigators' faith and we have to work to keep them strong, but this week we had a really hard time getting a hold of them.  I am reading the Book of Mormon and am in the book of Helaman.  I never had that much interest in the sermon by Samuel the Lamanite, but I payed attention this time.  I found some interesting doctrine about spiritual death and second death in chapter 14 verses 15-18.  I think alot on the plan of salvation, and what part I play, and how all parts in the plan interact perfectly.  It is not a plan created by mortal man but by Gods.        My companion and I get along well, and I think one of hte things that helps is obedience and a mutual desire to be obedient.  If every missionary was just obedient, his life and mission would be easy and he wouldnt have as many serious problems with his companions. Yesterday we chased all of our investigators down to take them to church, but only two came.  If we just sat in the chapel waiting, we wouldnt have had even one.  Rain on sundays dosnt usally help the missionaries it seems. This week ought to be better.        Our numbers this week were low despite our efforts.
