## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Itajai 2
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:55:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Itajai 2From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: mp8-dansiel@ldsmail.netDate: Mon, 28 Apr 2008 15:37:20 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai 2Zona ItajaiDear President Dansie,       This week passed by very fast.  My companion and I were rushed to contact our investigators with zone conference and d-day all in the same week, but I think we managed to get along pretty well and teach with a powerfull spirit to our investigators.  I feel a little more receptive to the spirit and easier to feel charity for people and it helps significantly with what I do.  This week I made the goal to have a doctrine of the day on which to ponder and teach if I have to give a short message.  It also helps to keep your mind on the saviour.  On thursday I studied Baptism in Preach my Gospel, and I didnt make it past the phrase ''baptism is the first ordinance of the Gospel of Jesus Christ.  An ordinance is a ceremony or rite that shows we make a covenant with Heavenly Father.''  I started to think about what a ceremony is.  The three common characteristics of ceremonies are as folows; someone in authority realizes the ceremony and oversees the covenants, the parties involved and witnesses.  This is true in regard to weddings, change of command in the military, award ceremonies etc.  The Change of command in a rifle company in the US ARMY is notably interresting.  While an officer may recieve a certain rank, such as Captain, this does not necessarily mean he is in a given command, but must recieve command over a body of men.  When this happens, there is a ceremony in front of the group recieveing a new commander, showing that from the moment the flag of the rifle company is passed from one Captain to another, the new captain is in command.  While paper work has to be filled out to authorize the change, the change is in effect from the ceremony on.  When we read section 128 of the Doctrine and covenants, we see quite plainly that we are judged according to men in the flesh (here we could say that the ceremony of baptism is to show to the witnesses or congregation and to God that we enter into the covenants of baptism) and according to God in the spirit, by what is written.  The ordinances of the Temple could be seen like a captain, who already possesing AUTHORITY, recieves an Oath and a Covenant in the presence of the supreme command and is endowed with POWER from on high.  Ordinances are absolutley necessary in our knowing God the Eternal Father and His son, Jesus Christ.       I like serving with Elder Pimentel, he has a special spirit when he teaches.  I know that I have been here for a while, but I would like to request one more transfer with him here.  If we are needed elsewhere, I understand, and accept the call to another area, but we would like to serve together as long as possible.  We love serving one next to the other.  I feel as if were ready to train and everything.  He is perfect and I am humbled to seve with him.       We now have six or seven people ready for baptism as soon as their paper work for marraige goes through.  We have to work hard for them to keep them strong.  The members continue to help, though not as much as before.  But we only have reasons to be grateful for them.       A few days ago we visited a family we are teaching who are going through financial problems and are struggleing with smoking and have been a little depressed with a slow down in their progress, so we visited them to help them.  I dint feel particularly inspired to teach on a given doctrine so I just asked them if they had any questions.  They didnt say any thing so I just waited.  And waited.  I noticed that the wife had tears in her Eyes.  So I waited some more and Roberto started to tell me how htey were passing through difficulties and how we hear alot about people being called or chosen and how they didnt know if they were among the chosen.  They said alot of other things as well, but I dont remember them.  I told them how I had passed through many problems, heartaches and times of hopelessness myself and I read them a scripture that helped me meny times in D+C 121.  I felt many things and spoke alot of things from my heart and told them that we are the ones that choose if we are chosen.  Some hear and turn away from the voice of the spirit, but others choose to embrace it.  The Lord, it seems, does not care so much about achievment so mush as he does about what we are doing.  Then we gave each of them a blessing and I prayed for them.  I love to pray for others and feel charity fill my heart as I act in the name of the Savior and speak his will and love for others.        On saturday night we got back from D-day in Balneario and We passed by a members house to ask if they could teach with us, but he was a bit sick and they offered a snack which we accepted.  I think there was some high tention in the home, and their 20 year old son yelled at his mom.  I felt a little saddened at this as well as Elder Pimentel.  We both sat down on the couch to see where we could go to teach, and our plans seemed futile, so we prayed for inspiration on what to do.  I didnt have any ideas and Elder Pimentel was still praying. Then he stopped and asked if we could leave a message with the family.  Half of what follows is what E. pimentel told me afterwards, so, while he was praying to know where we should go, he felt that we shluld stay just where we were.  So following the spirit, he took the hymn book and grabbed Rafael(the son who yelled at his mom) and asked him to sing I Am A Child of God with him.  so the two of them sang and then the two of them kneeled and prayed, and after that E Pimentel told Rafael to give his Mother a hug and ask forgivness and never disrepect her again.  As my companino did all this, he did it with a profound humility and perfect love, which not even a 20 yearold young man could deny and I did not see Elder Pimentel speaking, But Jesus Christ.  After that, Elder pimentel spoke to the the family and asked them to love each other and never let that happen again in their home.  He spoke of his won family and how he showed love to them every day and eles acobraram quando ele nao mostrou seu amor para eles.  He said that this family was sealed and they should honor and cherish that blessing.  He said none of his family but him is a member so he dosnt know the blessing of having an eternal family, and he pointed to me and said that I do and I have a great blessing in my life.  I felt powerfully a deep sorrow and an even deeper desire to help E Pimentels family recieve this blessing.  I also bore testimony of how we should cultivate love in the home, and how if we dont, we may drive those we love from us, as happened in my family after my own mother died.  I asked if I could pray at the end, and I prayed for each of the people in the family present and E. Pimentels family as well.  We have acted in the name of Jesus Christ this week and we feel the sanctifying power of representing him as best we can through Faith Hope and Charity.  Humility is the key, and as it says in Hel 3:35 We deliver our hearts to Him through Prayer.  Every thing begins with prayer.  It is my testimony that we may be sanctifyied through our prayer, humility, Faith hope and especially Charity, and that we are qualified for hte work when we wholly take upon us the Holy name of Christ.       Thank you for all you do for us.  We sustain you and pray for you.       Our numbers this week were as follows;                   meta                   realbapt/conf    0/0.................0/0bapt marc    20/8...............16/7Pesq na ig   15..................3liç c mem     35..................24novos          35..................23contatos      170.................163qualificar     100%...............100%Lem se dis   95%.................90%Total          6/7               Our weeks have gotten harder to achieve our goals, but we will be better this week.  We prayed for the rain to stop on saturday night so that people would come to church and it stopped raining.  When we went to pick up our investigators ate com carro, they didnt come.  Oh well, we did our part.  Hve a great week.

## Subject: Fw: You have a letter from Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:55:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: You have a letter from Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 14 Apr 2008 14:21:22 +0000Dear Family,      This week came and went fastly enough, and I cant believe were starting the fourth week of our transfer already.  I think when Im transferred Ill be a little sad to leave, because this area treats me well.  Last night when I reported our numbers to the zone leaders, I was pretty shocked to see how much weve been blessed.  It is definately not just us working here, because its pretty much impossible to do it on your own.  The members have been helping us like who knows what.        So Aurelia cut her hair short huh?  Youll have to send pictures(you can email digital photos to me via myldsmail.net without any problems).  This week we did a service project at a members house.  I dont think they throw anything away.  I got to chop a tree stump out of the ground with a really dull axe, and the next morning when I woke up all the muscles in my back were more or less ridiculously sore.  Im feeling the consequences of eleven months without physical labor.  I should probably excercise more.  We had another baptism on saturday, but somebody with a nasty sense of humor shut off the water valve to the church, so the big tubs of water that store water above the roof were empty, which means there was no water to fill the font.  So we had the baptism at an inactive members pool.  It was a little different, but seeing as the water was neck-high there were no worries about the investigators knees sticking out of the water or anything.        Im glad to hear Charles is still having good luck with cars.  Loosing wheels is always fun...  Why is Erin having jaw surgery?        I hope you all have a good week.  I took a look at the date the other day and realized that mothers day is coming up.  It seems like yesterday was christmas.  Time really flies!  Eu amo voces e espero que tenham uma boa semana!           Love Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews,Itajai2
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:55:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews,Itajai2From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 7 Apr 2008 17:28:24 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai 2Zona ItajaiDear President Dansie,I had a good time watching conference this week. At the end, one of the elders watching with me comented that President Monson never cited the scriptures once in his three talks. I found that interresting, but it dosnt really make a difference. As Brigham Young said in response to someone saying that the standard works should be the base of all doctrine and how we teach, the written word is from the past, the spoken word from the living oracle of God, is current, is Doctrine, and he would rather have a prophet than all the records ever written cobined. Authority dosnt come from the scriptures as Elder Holland explained so thoroughly. Im grateful to have a Prophet and I sustain President Monson as our President, Prophet, Seer, and revelator.My companion and I get along just fine, though sometimes he talks with perhaps a little excess and dosnt really leave me time to say much, and this week I realized that I was getting a little mad at him for it during one of our lessons, and when the time came around for me to teach I had lost the spirit because I was angry over something so petty. So after really repenting during the lesson, I was able to teach with the spirit. This really taught me that I do need to be more humble, and always have a broken heart and a contrite spirit, remembering Christ, and this will open the way to having the spirit, which brings charity. One of my biggest faults would be pride, and as I have been studying Alma and his prayers and sermons, his chief key to success was humility, a broken heart and contrite spirit, and pure charity. The focus of his talks seems to always point to being humble, being grateful for past deliverance. My attitude toward my companion improves as I humble myself and regard him as an equal.This week we visited an investigator and his brother who is a member who is new here and hasnt come to church in a month. It turns out that he was offended that the church didnt give him any financial help when he arrived and has decided to not go to church. He never spoke to the Bishop about it, just left a message in the voice mail, nor did he give his adress to the Bishop etc. But he was determined that the bishop has been neglecting his responsibilities and has decided not to go to church. So I asked him why he decided to be baptized fifteen years ago. He said he did what he needed to do for his personal salvation, so he was baptized. So I asked him what the Sacrament is to him. He scoffed and said it dosnt really matter because half the time nobody partakes of it with a contrite spirit and a broken heart like were supposed to any way. Ive come to realize that alot of people look at the church as just another church, or think it is the true church just because we help the poor, but the moment they demand help, if it does not come efficiently, they fall, and reject the Lords servants, such as the bishop. Our church is true based on the fact that we have the authority to administer the ordinances of the gospel through the high priesthood, which holds the keys to the know-lede of God, which is eternal life, and without the ordinances (the sacrament for example) ''and the authority of the priesthood, the power of godliness is not manifested to men in the flesh; therefore, without this no man can see the face of God the Father, and live...'' This experience really shook me in regards to how much sand is under the foudations of alot of ''mature'' members of the church in regards to their testimonies of the church, so I am focusing much of my efforts with active, less active and non members to see the importance of having prophets; living apostles who are the oracles of God here upon the earth and that the Gospel of Jesus Christ wit all its ordinances is restored and administered by the same organization of priesthood authority as set forth by Jesus Christ himself two thousand years ago, and even since the before the world existed.We have an investigator who it looks like will be baptized this saturday, and many others who are working on the paper work for marraige. In short, these next two months should be loaded with family baptisms.Our numbers this week are as follows;real..........................meta0/0..........................1/223/8.........................35/152.............................719............................3024............................35140...........................160100%.........................100% Qualify for the spirit90%...........................90% Lemre-se disto6/7Looking at that, I think we have room for improvement in achieving our goals. This week should be better. Thank you for all you do for us, and have a good week.Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Itajai II, Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:56:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Itajai II, Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 7 Apr 2008 16:38:58 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai 2Zona ItajaiDear President Dansie,I had a good time watching conference this week.  At the end, one of the elders watching with me comented that President Monson never cited the scriptures once in his three talks.  I found that interresting, but it dosnt really make a difference.  As Brigham Young said in response to someone saying that the standard works should be the base of all doctrine and how we teach, the written word is from the past, the spoken word from the living oracle of God, is current, is Doctrine, and he would rather have a prophet than all the records ever written cobined.  Authority dosnt come from the scriptures as Elder Holland explained so thoroughly.  Im grateful to have a Prophet and I sustain President Monson as our President, Prophet, Seer, and revelator.        My companion and I get along just fine, though sometimes he talks with perhaps a little excess and dosnt really leave me time to say much, and this week I realized that I was getting a little mad at him for it during one of our lessons, and when the time came around for me to teach I had lost the spirit because I was angry over something so petty.  So after really repenting during the lesson, I was able to teach with the spirit.  This really taught me that I do need to be more humble, and always have a broken heart and a contrite spirit, remembering Christ, and this will open the way to having the spirit, which brings charity.  One of my biggest faults would be pride, and as I have been studying Alma and his prayers and sermons, his chief key to success was humility, a broken heart and contrite spirit, and pure charity.  The focus of his talks seems to always point to being humble, being grateful for past deliverance.  My attitude toward my companion improves as I humble myself and regard him as an equal.        This week we visited an investigator and his brother who is a member who is new here and hasnt come to church in a month.  It turns out that he was offended that the church didnt give him any financial help when he arrived and has decided to not go to church.  He never spoke to the Bishop about it, just left a message in the voice mail, nor did he give his adress to the Bishop etc.  But he was determined that the bishop has been neglecting his responsibilities and has decided not to go to church.  So I asked him why he decided to be baptized fifteen years ago.  He said he did what he needed  to do for his personal salvation, so he was baptized.  So I asked him what the Sacrament is to him.  He scoffed and said it dosnt really matter because half the time nobody partakes of it with a contrite spirit and a broken heart like were supposed to any way.  Ive come to realize that alot of people look at the church as just another church, or think it is the true church just because we help the poor, but the moment they demand help, if it does not come efficiently, they fall, and reject the Lords servants, such as the bishop.  Our church is true based on the fact that we have the authority to administer the ordinances of the gospel through the high priesthood, which holds the keys to the know-lede of God, which is eternal life, and without the ordinances (the sacrament for example) ''and the authority of the priesthood, the power of godliness is not manifested to men in the flesh; therefore, without this no man can see the face of God the Father, and live...''  This experience really shook me in regards to how much sand is under the foudations of alot of ''mature'' members of the church in regards to their testimonies of the church, so I am focusing much of my efforts with active, less active and non members to see the importance of having prophets; living apostles who are the oracles of God here upon the earth and that the Gospel of Jesus Christ wit all its ordinances is restored and administered by the same organization of priesthood authority as set forth by Jesus Christ himself two thousand years ago, and even since the before the world existed.         We have an investigator who it looks like will be baptized this saturday, and many others who are working on the paper work for marraige.  In short, these next two months should be loaded with family baptisms.         Our numbers this week are as follows;real..........................meta0/0..........................1/223/8.........................35/152.............................719............................3024............................35140...........................160100%.........................100%  Qualify for the spirit90%...........................90%   Lemre-se disto                6/7Looking at that, I think we have room for improvement in achieving our goals.  This week should be better.  Thank you for all you do for us, and have a good week.                     Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Greetings from Brasil
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:56:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Greetings from BrasilFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 7 Apr 2008 16:02:41 +0000Dear Family,       Im glad to see that so many people enjoyed conference, because I sure did.  Especially because I got to see the last three sessions of conference in english.  I feel that it is exceedingly better to watch it in your native language.  I enjoyed the strong spirit given especially through the first presidency, as well as their humor.  President Monson caught me a little by surprise with his ears, but he proved a good point with the fact that people watch and follow our examples.  One of the missionaries watching with me commented at the end that in the three talks given by the president, he cited no scriptures.  I almost gave him a lecture to read the chapter in the Joseph Smith manual about prophets and continuing revelation along with D&amp;C 68, but I didnt.  Authority dosnt come from the scriptures as Elder Ballard explained so thoroughly.  I enjoy, and have been enjoying greatly the talks given by President Eyring since his call to the first presidency.  His humility brings on pure doctrine and a spirit that is very remarkable.       Anyway, Ill get along with it and tell you all how Im doing.  This week was bad in comparison to our last month, but when looking at what weve achieved, Id say we are still doing pretty well.  This week were going to do better and be a little humbler.  We visited a member this week who is new here and hasnt come to church in a month.  It turns out that he was offended that the church didnt give him any financial help when he arrived and has decided to not go to church.  He never spoke to the Bishop about it.  So I asked him why he decided to be baptized fifteen years ago.  He said he did what he needed  to do for his personal salvation, so he was baptized.  So I asked him what the Sacrament is to him.  He scoffed and said it dosnt really matter because half the time nobody partakes of it with a contrite spirit and a broken heart like were supposed to any way.  Ive come to realize that alot of people look at the church as just another church, or think it is the true church just because we help the poor, but the moment they demand help, if it does not come efficiently, they fall, and reject the Lords servants, such as the bishop.  Our church is true based on the fact that we have the authority to administer the ordinances of the gospel through the high priesthood, which holds the keys to the know-lede of God, which is eternal life, and without the ordinances(the sacrament for example) ''and the authority of the priesthood, the power of godliness is not manifested to men in the flesh; therefore, without this no man can see the face of God the Father, and live...''        This experience really shook me in regards to how much sand is under alot of ''mature'' members of the church in regards to their testimonies of the church, so I am focusing much of my efforts with active, less active and non members to see the importance of haveing prophets, living apostles who are the oracles of God here upon the earth and that the Gospel of Jesus Christ is restored and administered by the same organization of priesthood authority as set forth by Jesus Christ himself two thousand years ago, and even since the before the world existed.       ''Some people just dont get it.''      During our district meeting on tuesday I switched up the program and spoke on using time effectivley using goals, and how to set effective goals.  I cant resist giving training on effective use of time based on what I did with FranklinCovey.  I think it turned out pretty well for changing the program the moment of.  I really enjoy serving as a missionary, especially when I have an excellent companion who always looks for self improvment.  Thank you all for your financial and prayerful help.  I love you all and Pray for you as well.  May the Lord bless you in all your righteous endeavors.             Love                      Elder Andrews          PS.  Im kind of surprised to see Big Red without a mustache.  Hes been around just about as long as MoTab has sung at conference.  Im glad Aurelia keeps up the tradition of send a txt every time she sees him.  If I could send txts, you all would have recieved one too;  ''BIG RED''!  Tchau.

Last week we had a super pday across the river at the new chapel in Navegantes.  They have a new imported kawai keyboard that playes the hymns by playing one key.  one of the other elders likes to sing, so while every one else was playing soccer, we stayed in the chapel and sang.  It was good to sing out with another person who sings well.  Brazilians dont really sing very well, and if they do, its kind of breathy, and I like to sing with my whole soul, so it was good to sing with some one who has a strong voice.  While we were singing I remembered singing with Paul Alan, Julia, Aurelia and Daniel two thanksgivigns ago ''awake awake''.  To me, there arent really things outside the gospel that give me as much joy as singing with my family.  sometimes I really miss it, but I can remember that one day, ALL of us will sing together in praise of the savior when he returns.        I want to thank you for your support, your example and the legacy you and Grandpa made and continue to make.  I hope our extended family remains close, even when we all get married and have our own families.  I love you and hope your health remains strong enough to help you fulfill your mission in life to the furthest extent possible.              Love,  Joseph

## Subject: Fw: Itajai II Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:57:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Itajai II Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 24 Mar 2008 21:33:28 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai 2Zona ItajaiDear President Dansie,        this week I took a look at the people we have marked for baptism and I saw that alot of them could be progressing much faster than they are, especially those with problems with smoking.  So Elder Pimentel and I decided to make goals for each of them -divided into our part and the part of the investigators- based on the Baptismal interview questions.  Basically what this means aside from helping our investigators progress faster is that each investigator has a page in the area book with six pages of supplementary documents focusing on progress.  Ive begun to use my study jounal a little more liberraly in scripture study in general.  My study journal for study itself is very well organized and I dont like to put things in that could be seen as redundant, but I have recognized a lack of spirit due to this, so Im writing more again.      I love working with Elder Pimentel and I would like to thank you for letting us stay together.  We have plans for the area.  We get along just fine and he is a good missionary.  Being with an obedient missionary makes for less stress.      We are teaching a members wife and a few neices and nephews who should be baptized on saturday.  We have several people who are only waiting to get the paper work done for marraige and they will get baptized.  All in all, the months of april and My should have at least six to eight baptisms.  Some other people have problems with smoking, so were preparing to help make goals and give as much help as possible.  The members are extremely helpful and I feel a great difference in the ward from when I got here.  President Benson said that member missionary work will raise the spirituality of the ward where it is applied and I am seeing this first hand.       This week we did a division and what we had planned didnt seem right, so I scrapped it.  I was feeling like someone in particular was in need, but I couldnt figure out who it was, so we visited a convert who hadnt been to church in a while to see how she was doing, and I think she needed the visit, but I still felt like we needed to find someone, so we prayed and followed our feelings.  Sometimes revelation comes packet at a time to allow us t obecome slowly and fully prepared for what is coming.  After an hour and a half of driving around and not finding anyone at home we finally went ot the other side of our area and visited an investigator.  We taught a good lesson and the spirit was strong.  She is very willing to ask the Lord and recieve revelation.  She then told us that she was needing the visit when we arrived.  She had just finished arguing with her mother about religion and her mother had left for a session of church at Deus e amor (she had a bad experience there when she went) and so she went to her room to sit down and fume, when we arrived.  It was a two sided miracle.  It  was a good thing that the members got to see how miracle like this happen so often, it always lifts them up to the work.  I know that the Lord leads the work and we are on the side that wins.    Our numbers this week were;Bapt /conf...................0/0Bapt marked.................26/8Pesq na igreja...............9lessons with member.......42Novos pesq...................40contatos......................123Lembre se disto.............81%qualificar p esp..............100%We got alot of rides from members which cuts back on our contacts, so our contacts were a little harder to get, but well use our walking time a little better from here on out.  Thanks for all you do for us, and I hope you have a good week.      I hope you all had as good an easter as I had.  The bishop asked us and the ward mission leader to speak in sacrament meeting.  Elder Pimentel gave an excellent talk about being a witness of Christ, the ward mission leader spoke about his conversion and I talked about Lazarus and my testimony of the Savior, then the Bishop asked everyone to sit as a family in their respective families and then invited the missionaries to sit with the ward mother.  After speaking on the family and how the Saviors atonement blesses families, the meeting ended.  The meeting was very powerful, and the whole ward felt different.  One of the families in the ward was sealed in the Porto Alegre temple last week.  The sister used to be kind of sarcastic and a bit pessemistic, but after they went to the temple, Ive seen a marked difference in her way of talking to people.  I really miss going to the temple, and feeling the power of godliness that is so very strongly manifest in the things we do there.       Last week we succeeded in breaking our record again for lessons with members present, something I was thinking was a bit impossible.  Im staying here in Itajai with my ''filho'', thanks to some phone calls from the bishop and a few other people as we found out last night.  Apparently the members and the bishop like us...  We love them too.  Im not too worried about our new mission president, im sure he ll make some changes, but Ive discovered that if youre obedient to your leaders, you love them and life is alot happier.        Im glad that Aurelias recital out at BYU went well.  I didnt really have doubts that she would do well.  Im sorry I forgot to wish Anna and Dad a happy birthday last week, on tuesday I saw the date (the 18th) and just about hit myself.  So happy birthday.  Everybody is getting so old so fast.  I still feel like High school was last year and Im only 19 or something.  Yeah, and my twenty second birthday is coming up in june...       Its good to hear that Charles respects traditions that go back as far as the history of cars goes; breaking tools is pretty much and Andrews family mechanics ritual by now.  So Charles met some people in the singles ward that never have driven a car?  Were they Amish?  I hope you all have a great week, I love you all and keep you in my prayers.        Love Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Itajai 2, Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:57:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Itajai 2, Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 10 Mar 2008 19:04:06 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai IIZona Itajaidear President Dansie,       I am feeling like my spiritual power is growing and my confidence in myself and my standing with the Lord.  This week I had the opportunity to give several blessings.  Before I came here on the mission I loved to give blessings and speak in the name of the Lord and feel the words flow continually to my mind as I spoke, but when you have to do it in another language, things get hard.  As I learn more and speaking in portuguese becomes more natural, I am finding the same experiences as before in giving blessings.  I love to help people, especially when I am acting in the name of our Savior.  I am gratefull for the opportunity to serve as a missionary.       My companion is great, he really has a gift for speaking to people and sharing experiences, Im usually a little more reserved about sharing experiences as many times they are personal, so as he shares everone loves him.  He loves to help people and I am learning to be less shy in helping others through his example.  I respect any decision made in transfers, but I would like to express my desire to serve atleast one more transfer with him here in Itajai.        After Interviews, I put in some thought on what exactly you would like to hear in regards to our area, so I will tell you about some of our investigators:  We see many miracles in regards to encountering people to teach and people who gain testimonies over the most unikely things in the world.  We are teaching the wife of one of the irmaos in the young men presidency who was a strong catholic and didnt see any purpose in being baptized or anything special in our church.  After some time she began to think about the tithing her husband was paying and why.  After recieving a response about the church being true over tithing, she decided she wanted to be baptized and requested to start recieving the lessons.  You should have seen the look on the Bishops face when we told him.  Deer in the headlights.  She was the last person he thought would want to join the church.  We also are teaching a single woman named Luciane who we encountered in the rain four weeks ago as we were without umbrellas and hiding from the sudden rain under a soffet.  She asked us if we wanted to come in and the rest is history.  We have been visiting her and teaching her as she puts in comments like; why did the bible end?  shouldnt there be more?  etc.  four years ago she saw the missionaries and wanted to see what it was they taught, so she followed them and made a circle around the block to pass by them to see if they would talk to her.  They walked past her without saying anything.  She did the same thing and passed by them FIVE times and in the end gave up.  So Four years later WHen the missionaries showed up in the rain, she thought to herself, they came to ME!  she is accepting every thing and even burned the Jehovas witnesses that passed by and said we didnt believe in God for talking trash on other religions and lying about what we believe when she heard from our own mouths the truth.  She, like many others we teach, just needs to give up smoking.  Sometimes my heart sickens because of the vices with which satan holds the majority.  Our task sometimes seems impossible, but I remember the quote that Sister Dansie gave us a while back; We going to win.  The Lord will help us.  I will do all that is necessary to represent Christ and let his light shine through the darkness in the lives of others.        This week was ridiculously good numbers wise, but at the end of the week, my companion and I felt like we were blessed and just slacked the rest of the time.  Although this isnt true, we felt like we could have done better.  Friday through sunday I felt somthing weighing me down, like we needed to help someone in particular, but I couldnt figure out who it was, but at eight forty five last night we decided to visit a sister in the ward who signed a divorce this week.  One of the member families that we visit alot(or by way of interpretation, we pass by, talk and get a ride from him and teach lessons with him), has been telling us we need to visit this sister, but we put it off until yesterday.  We both agree that she was the one in need of a visit.  I brought my guitar(I got sick of life without music, so I bought a guitar three weeks ago and have been teaching my self in my free time.  Its fun to sing primary songs with it.) and sang two songs; Ele eviou seu filho and that one about a seed in spring which relates to the resurrection and resoration-em um dia primaveril. Then we gave her a blessing.  I think we helped her alot, shes been pretty depressed and she lives alone too.  It was good to use my talents to help someone again.  My companion has the gift of the gab, and much of what I have to say is lost in translation, so sometimes I feel like a third wheel, so again, it felt good to use my talents.  I love to live the gospel of Jesus Christ and help others on their way.  It leaves me feeling good and it really does bring ''verdade e paz, que satisfaz, o evangelho é luz''.      Our numbers this week are;Bapt/conf...........0/0bapt. marcado.....10/5pesq.s na igreja...10liç. com memb.....25novos...............28contatos............208Lembre se disto...18/22qualificar p esp....4/7All of our baptisms will probably be performed march 29 due to scheduling with the buildings and stake activities.  Elder Pimentel is on fire with contacts, he has a gift for talking to people, and we arrived a few minutes late a few nights this week.  Have a good week and we look forward to zone conference tomorrow.  Thank you for all you do to help us, it is much apreciated.            Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw:
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:57:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject:From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 17 Mar 2008 20:12:37 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai IIZona Itajai Dear President Dansie,        Our area really took off this week.  I feel like I would like to slow down time in a given day, but I cant, so we just have to be velozes.  We are focusing on helping every last one of our investigators progress, to be baptized and stay active.  Ive decided that this requires that we focus on how family worship is conducted and on how well our investigators under stand the repentace process after Baptism, and that they will make mistakes, but when you do, you just pick yourself up and start over again.  I think that the lack of understanding in these areas is one of the primary causes of lessened retention and inactivity among our converts.  Sure we introduce the atonement and get it to work in their lives, but the hard part is to get it to keep working.       My companion is great.  We work very well together and we have a bond like we were brothers.  Once again, I would like to express my VERY strong desires that we both remain here this next transfer.  I feel like we are only just now coming to realize the potential we have as a companionship.  However, if one of us is needed somewhere else, we will understand.  We commented to each other this last week that we have been seeing the hand of the enemy at work here, trying to upset our work by putting a mist of darkness around our investigators and lead them away, but we are on the winning side, and after doing all that was possible, the Lord has blessed us with miracles to answer our prayers.  One of our investigators who dosnt even know how to read, and her husband had been reading to her from the Book of Mormon, has two evangelical neighbors who already rejected us and gave us back all of our materials have been trying to get her to go to church with them.  They never have tried before we came along.  Whenever we pass by her house, her neighbors send their children to get her to come over to their house or to chuch or whatnot. One night two weeks ago one of her neighbors dropped by during one of our lessons and challenged the authority of the Book of Mormon and then left with our investiagator.  Being and evangelical, we were more or less certain that her vizinha would fill her head with doubts.  ELder Pimentel left his Guarda shuva at her house and we have been having dificulty contacting our investigator, Rose.  But this week we passed by to get the umbrella.  Rose was there and so we left a message.  I asked if E. Pimentel had a fovorite chapter in the Book of Mormon to read to her, so he chose Helaman 15.  Good chapter, but it starts off VERY uncomfortably.  So we started to explain a little about hte context and managed to get to the spiritual part and Rose interupted to tell that she had some thing to tell us.  Oh no, here comes the part where she says she dosnt want to here our message any more, we thought.  But we listened.  She said that her mother had gotten lost a few days before and so she was really worried, so her neighbor came by to pray and read a scripture to her.  She read some thing from the Bible about how the lost ones would be found in the waters or something.  Anyway, her mom pegou chuva and through all this she ended up finding her mom.  Heres the real kicker: her other neighbor never leaves the house without a Bible, but this one time she came over without it, and ROse wanted her to also read a scripture(this being after she found her mom), but there wasnt a bible in hte house so she grabbed the Book of Mormon and asked her to try reading something from it instead.  So her neighbor read from the Book of Mormon, and sure enough, it was the same scripture about the lost ones being found in the waters.  It was a small and simple thing, but it showed her that the Book of Mormon is true.  She and her whole family came to church this week.  I thought that we had lost her, that we had failed, and it had been weighing me down for almost two weeks, despite my prayers for her and her family.  That very morning I was feeling depressed about them, and had prayed extensively for them.  In all reality, The Lord does indeed answer our prayers, especially when we do all that is possible.  We have miracles like this one happen all the time, and even like I said that we see the hand of the enemy working, we see the hand of the Lord working harder and more successfully.  We have a ton of people preparing for baptism and many of them will start to be baptized beginninng on the twenty ninth of march.  Thank you for letting me serve here.       We worked very hard this week.  Our numbers are as follows:Baptisms/confirmations...........0/0Baptisms marked...................26/8Pesqisadores in church.............14Lessons with members.............40Novos pesqisadores.................32Contatos..............................203Lembre se disto......................19/22Qualificar p/ espirito................5/7Thank you for all that you do for us, have a good week.

## Subject: Fw: Letter from the illustrious elder Andrews

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Letter from the illustrious elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 24 Mar 2008 20:56:49 +0000Dear Family,      I hope you all had as good an easter as I had.  The bishop asked us and the ward mission leader to speak in sacrament meeting.  Elder Pimentel gave an excellent talk about being a witness of Christ, the ward mission leader spoke about his conversion and I talked about Lazarus and my testimony of the Savior, then the Bishop asked everyone to sit as a family in their respective families and then invited the missionaries to sit with the ward mother.  After speaking on the family and how the Saviors atonement blesses families, the meeting ended.  The meeting was very powerful, and the whole ward felt different.  One of the families in the ward was sealed in the Porto Alegre temple last week.  The sister used to be kind of sarcastic and a bit pessemistic, but after they went to the temple, Ive seen a marked difference in her way of talking to people.  I really miss going to the temple, and feeling the power of godliness that is so very strongly manifest in the things we do there.       Last week we succeeded in breaking our record again for lessons with members present, something I was thinking was a bit impossible.  Im staying here in Itajai with my ''filho'', thanks to some phone calls from the bishop and a few other people as we found out last night.  Apparently the members and the bishop like us...  We love them too.  Im not too worried about our new mission president, im sure he ll make some changes, but Ive discovered that if youre obedient to your leaders, you love them and life is alot happier.        Im glad that Aurelias recital out at BYU went well.  I didnt really have doubts that she would do well.  Im sorry I forgot to wish Anna and Dad a happy birthday last week, on tuesday I saw the date (the 18th) and just about hit myself.  So happy birthday.  Everybody is getting so old so fast.  I still feel like High school was last year and Im only 19 or something.  Yeah, and my twenty second birthday is coming up in june...       Its good to hear that Charles respects traditions that go back as far as the history of cars goes; breaking tools is pretty much and Andrews family mechanics ritual by now.  So Charles met some people in the singles ward that never have driven a car?  Were they Amish?  I hope you all have a great week, I love you all and keep you in my prayers.        Love Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Itajai II
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:58:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Itajai IIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 3 Mar 2008 21:58:42 +0000Elder AndrewsElder PimentelItajai2ItajaiDear President Dansie,        This week was more or less outstanding.  We are working hard and are trying everything to help our investigators and be effective as possible.  I feel myself growing every day and look forward to studying and sharing what Ive learned with Elder Pimentel.  I love to feel the spirit as we teach those who are eager to hear the message of the restoration.  Ive been trying to read and study the messages I find in the Book of Mormon and share these things with the people we teach, leaving passages that are fresh in my mind with them and helping them understand.  There is a scripture in 1nefi ten, verse 17 that says a few interresting things; e aconteceu que eu nefi, depois de ouvir {as palavras de meu pai que disse PELO ESPIRITO que ele recebeu PELA FE que ele teve no Filho de Deus, desejei ver e saber estas coisas, que podem ser dadas para qualquer homem que procura diligentemente.}  This time as I read the Book of Mormon, Im seeing very apparently the power and importance of faith, both for us and for our investigators.  First, We need to have faith so as to speak with the power of the spirit, which will then help the investigator have a desire to know, even to the extent that they are willing to act in faith, reading hte Book of Mormon for themselves and praying to know the same things that we know.  How true it is that we cannot convert anyone beyond our own conversion!  It is like it is said in Romans 10:17; So then faith cometh by hearing and hearing by the Word of God.       My companion is great, we love to work together.  I would like to express strong desires to remain companions as long as possible, but I am willing to accept whatever assignment you think necessary.  He is progressing very well, and we work together more or less ridiculously effectivly.       Our area is absolutly perfect in every way.  We are recieving refferals de++++, and are being kept on our toes keeping in contact and helping our investigators effectively, but it feels good to be busy.  Our bishop is eager to help us out and we always have miracle contacts, practically every day.  The other day I was feeling a little down and so I started doing contacts.  I would like to share my testimony that one or the keys to having a good day as a missnionary is found in doing lots of contacts.  I dont know how it works, but it lifts your spirits and things begin to happen when you do all you contacts and maybe a little more every day.  I know it makes a difference.      Yesterday after church a man came into the building who had just been released from prison on friday and had nowhere to go and had been resisting going back to his old lifestyle of stealing cars and had been eating out of trash cans, hadnt bathed in days etc., and was sicerely wanting a new life.  So we taught him about the power of the savior to change our lives and gave him a book of mormon as well as a blessing of strength.  After making arrangements to buy a busride to Brusque (a city forty minutes from here) we took him to one of the sisters houses to get some new clothes, food and a shower.  When I first walked into the relief society room, he was sitting in a chair, his head bowed down, hardly thinking himself worthy to be called human, or worthy of recieving help, but when we left him that afternoon at the sisters house with new clothes, food, a means of obtaining a future as an honest man, he was a man, with hope in his eyes; hope of repentance, of obtaining the human dignity which he had lost, and the light of the gospel of Jesus Christ -helping the fatherless and the widowed- shining in his eyes.  I dont know if I will ever see him again, whether he will find the missionaries in Brusque or what the future holds, but I am humbled by the opportunity given to help him, and I will never forget the experience of seeing a man gain his self respect again.  Afterward I told my companion about the beginning of my favorite book, Les Miserables, how a bishop helped a man doomed to social rejection gain hope, and change his life forever by looking at the condemned and giving him the candlesticks, sacrificing to save him who had only just been caught robbing him.  My Mothers name was Cosette, and was named that because my grand parents were reading Les Miserables when my Grandma was pregnant with My Mom.  I never forget hearing my mother tell me the story of Les Miserables on the front proch of the house.  what the story meant to her, and how we should all try to be the same.       I hope you have a great week and I look forward to seeing you and Sister Dansie tomorrow.  Our numbers this week are;baptisms/conf........0/0Bapt marcados........10/5pesq na igreja........12liç. com membro.....26novos pesq............36contatos...............145/6padroes................8/9Lemre se disto........19/22qual. pelo espirito....6/7 (we got home a little late one day.  well be improving this.)   Have a great week                          Elder Andrews

As I read the Book of Mormon, I see more and more about faith and the power that it has.  Alma counseled his son Helaman to teach the people to resist evey temptation from the devil with their faith in the Lord Jesus Christ, Jacob says that their faith was gained and strengthened in studying the Prophets revelation and the spirit of prophecy, and Mormon says that all good things come from Christ and we lay hold upon every good thing by faith.  Elder Richard G Scott said that as we grow in character, our capacity for excercising faith grows and vice versa.  This gave me a few Ideas about how we grow grace for grace as well as grace to grace.  As we excercise faith we build character, or experience in the past in which we can see evidence of things not seen which are true; we know the Lord helped us before, and he can certainly help us again.  It is all very fascinating, and I am learning the power of praying in faith as well.      Elder Pimentel is working and learning perfectly. Well Im out of time, so I go ahead and finish up.  I love you all and hope this week is as good for you as mine was.  Boa semana para voces.         Love,                 Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Hello familia
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:58:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Hello familiaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 10 Mar 2008 18:20:58 +0000Dear Family,       I am glad you got my letters, it sounds like you got them fairly quick, usually it takes more than two weeks for letters to get from here to there.  Looks like we got lucky.  This week was ridiculously good numbers wise, but at the end of the week, my companion and I felt like we were blessed and just slacked the rest of the time.  Although this isnt true, we felt like we could have done better.  Friday through sunday I felt somthing weighing me down, like we needed to help someone in particular, but I couldnt figure out who it was, but at eight forty five last night we decided to visit a sister in the ward who signed a divorce this week.  One of the member families that we visit alot(or by way of interpretation, we pass by, talk and get a ride from the brother and teach lessons with him), has been telling us we need to visit this sister, but we put it off until yesterday.  We both agree that she was the one in need of a visit.  I brought my guitar(I got sick of life without music, so I bought a guitar three weeks ago and have been teaching my self in my free time.  Its fun to sing primary songs with it.) and sang two songs; How could the father tell the world of love and tenderness; and that one about a seed in spring which relates to the resurrection and resoration- I like that one because of the chord progressions and diminished minor chords.  Then we gave her a blessing.  I think we helped her alot, shes been pretty depressed.  It was good to use my talents to help someone again.  My companion has the gift of the gab, and much of what I have to say is lost in translation, so sometimes I feel like a third wheel, so again, it felt good to use my talents.       We went on what might be called a wild goose chase on saturday to find a reference a member gave us way out in the country.  All we know is the referrals name is Paulo and he drives a black mercedes.  So basically we looked for the biggest and gawdiest houses and walked upwards of ten miles in five hours, but we made progress in finding the road to the house we all think this paulo lives in.  We ll see next we go out that way.  We had already accumulated our numbers for our goals so we felt alright burning a little time.  It was good excercise too.        Something I feel in regards to Isaiah is that it is more or less the same as revelations.  Joseph Smith said that revelations is one of the most easiest to understand and plainest books in the bible.  Basically the message is this; Were going to win.  I feel the sme way about Isaiah.  If you look at the big picture, its easy to understand, especially if you read it together with Kings.  It tells the promises to Israel and the message is this; Israel is the people of the Lord, and he will remember them.  They will win.  One might suppose that the jews, looking way beyond the point and into the miniscule details, were given things like Isaiah, which are plain, and yet difficult to understand at the same time.  Sometimes you have to back up from the tree so you can see the forest.  Thats the way I look at anything written by Paul as well.  You have to read it all to understand anything.  And now Im rambling.  By the way, I really thought brother Geurnseys commentary in the mob letter about the center of the galaxy was extremely interresting.       Thank you all for the help you give and have aready given me to be on a mission.  I pray for you and hope the family remains strong.  Every things hot and steamy still down on this side of the planet.  Were probably all dreaming about trading places by now.  I cant wait for the cool again.             Love                      Elder Andrews

Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:59:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Itajai IIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 11 Feb 2008 16:14:51 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SchioserItajai IIZona ItajaiDear President Dansie,        Ive been reading more of Book of Mormon lately, and I have been seeing alot more things about faith and seeing the need we have for faith in everything that we do as missionaries.  In Alma thirty one, it says that Alma was granted the answers to his prayer, ''because he prayed in faith''.  I hvae started to notice how our converts need to devolop habits of prayer, not just personally, but as a family.  The same could very easily be said about scripture study and family home evening.  These things stuck out to me, very clearly in what PResident Monson said in the leadership meeting last week as well.  It also says this in the beginning of the planners we use.  I am fast discovering how sweet it is to pray for other people, especially as we visit them.  As I do so, I recieve more charity for them and I pray more for each of them in my personal prayers as well.  Elder Bednar said in his article in the september Ensign, that if feed a man a fish, you feed him for a meal.  If you teach a man to fish however, you feed him for a life time.  Last week I went on divisions with a member of the bishopric, and he pointed out houses of inactive members in almost every street.  I felt to wonder, How would the missionaries who taught them feel if they new these converts were inactive?  What would they do better to insure activity in their converts as they taught if they could see the future?  I will try to teach people to carry the aspects of religion into their personal lives as best I can.       Elder Schioser is dissapointed in being moved, but I always remain puzzled at his reasons for liking the area.  It never has to do with the ward, or the investigators.  Alot of missionaries say they are making a sacrifice of their lives for two years of their lives, when it really isnt much of a sacrifice if you think of the glory of coming home having learned a new language, gone to do the Lords work and returning home as a hero etc.  Its a freeby really, because noone in your home ward was there to see if you slacked off your whole mission or something, but if you give up your whole soul to God, and waste yourself away doing his work, come rain or shine, conveniences of laundry or just having a bucket etc, you have really sacrificed the only thing that is truly yours; your will of action and heart.  Of all things that I would wish to see in the hearts of the missionaries around me is charity.  Many preach, seek baptisms, and tell people the way, but I have seen few who get on their knees and pray with the investigators with the energy of soul with which Alma prayed.  The Book of Mormon is a record of answered prayers of the prophets and even a manifestation of the Lords responses to prayers of faith.  I love the Gospel, I love the restoration, and I love my brothers and sisters here on the Earth.       Our area is doing well, though we ought to get back to work on finding new investigators and marking baptisms, those numbers have been fallin a little for us lately.  The members are the greatest, and I thank you for letting me stay here a little longer.  Yesterday it was hot enough to compete with a volcano.  I was sure to use alot of sunscreen and leave the umbrella in the apartment, and sure enough it rained... HARD.  We had three of the deacons in our ward with us, and it was really surprisingly fun to run like wild through the rain from soffet to soffet, until we stopped and heard a voice ask voces querem entrar?  A woman let us into her small entry to escape from the rain and lightning, and though we were entirely soaked, we talked to her about the gospel and set up a very promising appointment for thursday to come over and teach her about the restoration.  Others might get a little down about getting wet and all, but it lets you know youre alive and its good to get a good laugh in every once in a while as you run without an umbrella in the rain.  It seems like the Lord blesses me with miracles most when it rains.  Ou numbers this week are;Bapt/conf0/0marked baptisms9/3(as I said, I am going to try to work on that one)Investigators in sac. meeting7lessons with members15other lessons20progressing invest.s6referrals0/4new investigators32new members12remember this;77%qualify for the spirit 5 days THank you for all you do and have a good week.   Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: querido familia
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 03:59:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: querido familiaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 18 Feb 2008 21:33:13 +0000Dear Family,      This week was more or less the best.  We all went down to transfers conference in Florianopolis on wednesday and I got to see some faces I havnt seen for a while, so I loved it.  My new companion is Elder Pimentel, straight out of the MTC.  As far as training him goes, all I have to do is sit back and enjoy the ride.  Hes better than half the zone leaders and experienced missionaries and then some!  It feels kind of like a breath of fresh air after six months of stagnation.  I am starting to realize how the effectiveness of our contacts in the street effect our enthusiasm when we do them as we should.  I am enjoying being a senior companion as well, it gives me alot more capacity to follow the spirit as I work and teach.  Today we mounted that which previously has been thought of as just an impossible dream;  we cleaned our apartment.  The origianal plan was to start at ten and end at four in the afternoon, but instead we started at seven this morning and had to stop at four in the afternoon.  I like the way brazilian houses are made;  tile and plaster over brick.  To clean, you jsut get buckets of water and scrub everything, so there is no frustration with vacuuming and everything smells like eucaliptus flavored disinfectant afterwards.  I am more or less exsaustified now, so I feel good and will feel even better to come home tonight to the smell of eucaliptus and dream about scrubing stoves that havnt been cleaned since 1992...  B.C.        I still remember singing with Daniel and Paul Woodbury last november and loving it, so I hope Charles had a good time singing with them.  Sounds as if everybody is congregating back at home, so give everybody a big hug for me- if they are still there.  As I said last week, our bishop works in the drug busting department of the police, so we planned a welcome for E Pimentel.  I gave the spare key to our apartment to the bishop and he put an ice box filled with liver in our refridgerator while we were gone and at ten that night we got a knock on the door from the police saying that they had recieved a tip that there was an american ''missionary'' smuggling and selling human organs, so they asked if they could check out our house.  Upon finding the liver in the refidgerator, we were arrested.  My companion stayed calm and cool, but you should have seen his face when the one of the cops introduced himself as our bishop.  I cant think of a better way to meet the bishop of your new area.  Weve been working our tails off and had to ''jog'' to get home on time one night after teaching an amazing lesson.  My companion teaches by the spirit, something my last companions have lacked, and I love to teach with him.         I hope all is well at home and that you are all happy.  Our telephone has a voice memo that can be used for a ringing tone, so every morning as an alarm I now hear ''ver meine spieres spitze, fuertchet, duerschritze das fuer nie!''  (last line in the opera, das walkerie).  Im sure you all miss hearing me belt out opera at the top of my lungs when Im happy...                     Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Dear family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:00:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear familyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 11 Feb 2008 15:36:00 +0000Dear family        Sounds like its been a pretty interresting week in the way of computers.  I dont particularly like messing with them because they cant take care of themselves alot fo the time, but they do make things somewhat more convenient.         Yesterday it was hot enough to compete with a volcano.  I was sure to use alot of sunscreen, and sure enough it rained... HARD.  We had three of the deacons in our ward with us, and it was really surprisingly fun to run like wild through the rain from soffet to soffet, until we stopped and heard a voice ask voces querem entrar?( do you want to come in?).  A woman let us into her small entry to escape from the rain and lightning, and though we were entirely soaked, we talked to her about the gospel and set up a very promising appointment for thursday to come over and teach her about the restoration.  Others might get a little down about getting wet and all, but it lets you know youre alive and its good to get a good laugh in every once in a while as you run without an umbrella in the rain.       My companion, E Schioser, is being transferred, I dont know where because the place he was supposed to go he dosnt like because no one will wash his clothes and he dosnt like the apartment there etc., so he called up the president and told him he wouldnt go there.  I had no idea anyone had the guts to do that.  Oh well, Im pretty sure well know what happens tonight.  I will be training this transfer, and Im more or less RIDICULOUSLY excited.  I want to try to give the best possible to my precious newbie before he gets put with less than obedient companions in the future.  President Dansie generally puts the newest, freshest and most obedient missionaries with the ones that struggles, so I will prepare my new companion for that.  I have some Ideas about how to get the missionary work here to take off in a boom too, so Im looking forward to the next transfer.  This morning we went over to the bishops house to take pictures in his uniforms for work.  He is the commandante of the tactical unit in the police here, so he showed us how to take corners with a pistol, search someone for weapons, etc.  Elder schioser had a hard time fitting in any of the uniforms, but he succeeded in the end.  I am kind of surprised at the kind of guns the police use(.380 auto), which is pretty weak really.  The FBI has to use ten mm, which is pretty powerfull, when doing drugbusts in the states, and there are alot more drugbusts here.  I ll try to send some photos of that later, theyre kind of funny because were up to our chins in gear, yet were wearing haviana sandals...  very chicy      So Charles has started up as a shoe salesman huh?  I always enjoyed retail sales, because unlike other sales, you pretty much only have to worry about customer retention and making other people happy.  Its fun to get people to trust you and make friends too.  I think Charles is good at that, so he should do well.  I love you all and hope you have an excellent week.                       Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Itajai 2, Elder Andrews
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:00:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Itajai 2, Elder AndrewsFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: Mp8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 28 Jan 2008 16:18:27 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SchioserItajai IIZona ItajaiDear President Dansie,       All of my Emails to you have fallen through since I came out to Itajai, so I hope this makes it to you.  This week I have made a concerted effort to read the Book of Mormon PRAYERFULY, as I found a quote from President Hinckley in PMG 108 (english): ''I promise you without hesitation that if you prayerfully read the Book of Mormon, no matter how many times youve already read it, the Spirit of the Lord will will come into your heart.  You will feel a stronger determination t okeep the commandments and a stronger testimony of the living reaity of the Son of God''.  I took it up and I can say it makes a real difference, especially if youre seaching for the blessings promised in that statement.  Needless to say, ive been including this promise in my teachings to members and investigators alike, and it makes a considerable diference.  Music does too.  This week we had our monthly D-day for the zone here.  Its always very efective and its good to go with someone who isnt stuck in the missionary routines.  My assigned area was in the shopping district of the city, so we found (that means we had to serch for them) maybe fifty houses, almost all of which were empty (the beach is a two minute walk from there) and anyone that we encountered was a determined catholic, so I decided to change things up and instead of asking if we could leave a message, I started asking if I could come in and sing a hymn for them.  That worked so well that I think that is going to be one of my primary aproaches to knocking doors from this time henceforth.      This week Elder Schisoer had problems getting up and didnt want to accept help, so I called the zone leaders.  I dont particularly care for telling on people, so I just got it over with and tried to show an increase of love for him.  He wasnt too pleased for my calling, but as far as outward appearances go, I dont think hes holding it against me.         Our area is doing much better now and things are finally starting to pick up with the work, especially with the members giving references and taking friends to church.  We have a baptism this week -a thirteen year old named Evandro- who was a referral who wanted to get baptized from the beginning.  Im grateful that the Lord is answering my prayers for the area and the for the fire of the work in the hearts of the members.         This week as I was reading in Alma 7 verses 15-17 I decide to take the words of Alma seriously and I decided I believed the testimony he left of the Savior and decided to ''lay aside every sin which taketh you so easily'' and make a covenant to serve the Lord, by taking the sacrament.  I love the Book of mormon and know it is true.  I love to testify of its miraculous power in drawing us nearer to Christ.    our numbers this week are0/012/514303060/10409142needless to say I feel good about last week.

## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews, Itajai II
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:00:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews, Itajai IIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 4 Feb 2008 15:18:30 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SchioserItajai IIZona ItajaiDear President Dansie,       This week was great.  It was hard to get all our numbers, due to inclement weather and other things as well including meetings, but we managed to get alot done.  This week I learned that If it rains hard for four days, it floods.  My feet got more or less drenched, but in the end, the work that we got done was very satisfactory.  During conference on friday you said something that sparked my interest.  You said that perhaps one of the greatest reasons we sin is in a lack of faith in the promised blessings for keeping the commandments.  In the last two general conferences, Elder Scott and Elder Hales have said somethings about character and faith; how when we excercise faith, we build character, and the more character we have, the more capacity we have for excercising faith.  I have often pondered why we dont always feel those spiritual highs which seem so infrequent, when we feel the power of the love of God and feel as if we could do anything in his power if it were necessary.  These experiences seem to be the powerful manifestations, or a taste of what is promised, should we remain faithful, that can give us the faith and strength to continue and endure t othe end.  I see the twelve diciples in 3Nefi 19, when their garments were purified, they were in the presence of the savior, I imagine that they looked back many times with nostalgia on that experience and wished they could be there again.  Our remarkable experiences can serve to strengthen, bear and lift us up out of our problems and even temptation.       Elder Schioser is doing well, sometimes his sarcasm stings a little, but I think he might have come from a backround where you develop tough skin against that so I just learn to brush it aside.  He has been entering some websites to play games while waiting for downloads of fotos from his family.  He still has trouble waking up in the morning, he usually wakes up for a few seconds and sleeps again.  When you were calling him in the mornings, he would get up to talk to you and then go to the bathroom and sleep on the toilet.  I try to help him though.  Hes started to take showers later and begins to study at 8:00, and continue in the morning schedule until ten, when he takes a shower.  I tell him that he is a good missionary and that I love him, and I think it makes a difference in how he treats me and even how he thinks of himself.  Its just hard sometimes to help people to be obedient, but I try to do my best.  I very much dislike telling about others disobedience, and I hope you understand that I have absolutley no desire to make myself seem better than him.  He is my brother and I am his.  Thank you for clarifying to us during conference that if our companion is having problems it is OK to tell you, and that it is our duty.  It helps me feel less bad.        Our area is Great.  Things in general are improving a great deal.  We have begun to eat in more members houses and members are giveing some referrals now and bringing people to church.  Several have family or friends that want to be baptized.  We have a family we are teaching, and the wife cannot read, so her husband reads the Book of Mormon to her.  When she told me that, I think it melted my heart.  I dont know what to say other than it just touches me that they read together, that he has enough love to read to her.  We marked her for baptism this week and yesterday I wanted to ask him to be baptized as well, but he was drunk, so infelizmente, nao deu.  I love our members and this ward.  If possible, Id like to stay here for a while, however, if thats not possible, I understand that the Lord sends us where we need to be.       Yesterday we confirmed a new member and as we stood in the circle to bless him, we all put our right hands on his head and our left hand on the shoulder of the person to our left.  I put my hand on the left shouder and someone stood up and and put my had on the right shoulder of my neighbor before we started.  That made me see a relation to other things and I find I am beginning to understand and treasure the very eternal truths we have in the Temple.  I know that we have prophets today, and that the church of God in its absolute fullness graces the earth today.  Jesus Christ lives, He is our Lord, King and salvation.       Thank you for your help to all of us and I hope you have a good week.Our numbers this week are:1/19/41017753/41510140Remeber this- 68% -we have some work to do thereQualify for the spirit- 6/7
