## Subject: Fw: Foi uma boa semana
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:00:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Foi uma boa semanaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 4 Feb 2008 14:28:33 +0000Dear Family,       One of the things I greatly enjoyed about the MTC was not having to deal with cell phones, or any kind of phone for that matter.  I didnt have to worry about the unreliable means of communication they present.  Generally I like to speak to people face to face and use the sincerity of charisma to solve problems and express feelings.  Text messaging is the worst when communicating about important things.  I liked to use text messaging to send jokes or quotes though.  As far as women and communication goes, I agree with you that it really is one of the great differences between men and women in the need to communicate on a constant basis.  Some one pointed out to me that when we drive, women pay attention to what is in a closer proximity than men and men watch further ahead and let the closer things take care of themselves, because what once was the future will be your present sooner or later depending on your speed.  Hence I think that in a fast moving world like we have today, all the communication materials we have ought to be a benefit to women in general and perhaps something of a curse to men.  After all, one of the reasons men look further ahead is to see what really matters-or is only absolutly essential to be done- and do what is in relation that, leaving everything else to neglect, because in the end, it dosnt really matter.  Id say thats open for comments as Im not really sure its true...        The weather here was awful this week.  It rained cats and dogs, and the drainage systems in Brazil are less than ideal, so we did alot of wading and people dont let you in their houses on rainy days, generally speaking, so I discovered why the Lord decided to bless us by doubling our numbers last week- to make up for this week.  We also had alot of meetings and events to go to and seeing as the city bus system in Itajai is o pior do mundo (translation: bad), we generally waited for an hour for a bus to a neighbor hood across the city.  We had our Zone conference on friday in Joinville, a city an hour north of us, but do to accidents, it being the weekend of carnival, flooding and fallen bridges, it took us four hours to get there and another four hours getting back.  There are alot of missionaries who have been taking advantage of the trust which president Dansie gives us and have been breaking rules, so we all got burned.  I love our president because even though hes chastening you, you can still feel his love and how much he means it when he calls us ''the great and noble ones''.  It was a good conference.  We also had a baptism on friday, which we missed due to slow travel time on the way back from conference, but we are happy to see the results of our work.       I hope you all have a great week, I pray for you and hope you are all well.       Love, Elder AndrewsPs- Anna, Ill send a letter to you before your birthday.  I miss you too.PPs- congrats to Woya for breaking a string.  What was she playing this time?  Last time it was Worthy is the Lamb by Handel I think.  Big A major chord if Im not mistaken.

## Subject: Fw: Querido Familia
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:01:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Querido FamiliaFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.com; skipandrews@att.netDate: Mon, 28 Jan 2008 15:48:55 +0000Dear Family,       sounds like its been an interresting week for you all, and yes, I am a little jealous of the comfortable weather, but I can survive the inferno because I just bought a sun repellant alluminium foil tie that reflects the sun AND the heat...  Not really, because that would be something of a ripoff and I flatter myself that Im not that stupid.  This week we had our monthly D-day for the zone here-when we get all the missionaries in our zone together and work in one area doing divisions with the members and just find people for six hours.  Its always very efective and its good to go with someone who isnt stuck in the missionary routines.  My assigned area was in the shopping district of the city, so we found (that means we had to serch for them) maybe fifty houses, almost all of which were empty (the beach is a two minute walk from there) and anyone that we encountered was a determined catholic, so I decided to change things up and instead of asking if we could leave a message, I started asking if I could come in and sing a hymn for them.  That worked so well that I think that is going to be my primary aproach to knocking doors from this time henceforth.       Im glad that Dad got the opportunity to go out with the missionaries and speak spanish again.  This week we ate lunch with a sister from Uruguay, and I think half of the time she was really speaking spanish.  Its funny how they roll the Rs so much and the Ss in between vowels make a sssss sound instead of the zzzz sound we use in portuguese( casa or house would be and cassa in espnl, and caza in port. ).  It kind of sounds like a lisp.  I think Ill try to learn spanish when I get back and be made fun of for my protuguese accent.       The missionary work here in Itajai has finally started to take off.  Ive been praying alot for it, not just for us, but for everyone in the ward.  We will be having a baptism this week and another in a couple more weeks.  If you could see my face, all you would be able to see is a smile.       Congrats on the DSL, the family will finally be on the internet fast track and you wont have to wait for an eternity for downloads.  Hopefully this letter will make it into your acount, if not im sending it to the old adress as well.  I hope Morgans glasses are somewhat stylish, if not he could always try out my old pink ones...(just kidding).  The members here get a kick out of my telling them that I have pink glasses, and think Im joking.  What I would do for some pictures of me with long hair and pink glasses.  Speaking of which, is it possible to send me some pictures of the family via email or snailmail?  Brazilians love looking at pictures, its almost like an acient ceremony or somehting here.  People treat you like a real person if theyve seen your pictures.  Its kind of funny.       As far as dating for Dad goes, theres a new member in our ward who is divorced(her husband left her) who since finding out that Dad is single wont leave me alone about it.  I dont know if Ill ever stop regretting mentioning it to her.         We got a call this morning from the ZLs that President Hinckley passed away last night.  Im sad that he is gone and am gratefull to him for the excellent work which he presided over and I know he really was a Prophet, Seer and Revelator, just as his predecessors were.  I love you all and wish you a good week.         Love, Elder Andrews

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

It makes a real diferrence in the way I teach and how people react to it.  So many times it seems that we just leave a VERY short message on a verse of scripture or something that really dosnt help the people in their respective lives, so Im trying to focus on making their lives better any way that I can. ## Subject: Fw: Elder Andrews Itajai 2
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:01:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Elder Andrews Itajai 2From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 14 Jan 2008 13:37:58 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SchioserItajaí IIZona ItajaíDear President Dansie,      This week has gone well enough and I feel like I am starting to help people in gaining testimonies and feeling the spirit.  I really have made a concerted effort to gain more of the spirit as I teach, and to make a stronger effort to pray in faith as it says in PMG chapter 4. I have definately seen a difference in my messages to the members and even in some of our lessons. We represent Christ in peoples homes, so Im trying to live up to that for the benefit of those I serve. Im beginning to learn that while the powers of the enemy are great, the influence of the Holy Ghost and righteousness are greater in their power, especially in creating an environment for keeping the commandments and influencing those we teach to repent and change. As President Eyring put it in conference: ''Our duty, which IS in our power, is to live in such a way that other people will see the fruits of the Holy Ghost in our lives and desire it also, enough to change.''  Or at least thats more or less what he said.  I wouldnt quote me on it but thats the message presented.        My relationship with my companion is alright I suppose.  Sometimes it requires alot of patience but patience has always seemed to pay off, so I trust in the future.  Sometimes he can be very sarcastic and his comments sting, but I can live with it.  Something that I wish could just be buried while we are on the mission is patriotism and politics.  My companion regularly comments on Brazilian supiriority and puts down the US, and while I know that it dosnt really make a difference, it manages to offend and eat up my mind all day, making me angry.  I can get control on my anger, but it takes time, and when provocations are repeated it gets hard to maintain a clean transmission of the spirit.  When people put down my country I feel the same way as if they called my mother something slanderous.  I try to compliment Brazil when asked about it, and I would appreciate a courteous response.  But I can get over it I suppose.  Other things are more important at the present.       Our area is getting better, though its hard to maintain a good standing with the members.  But I love them and want to help them and I hope that they feel it.  I feel things improving as time progresses.  We have a number of good investigators, including José and family, Jose being evangelical based yet skeptical of some of the doctrines in most of the typical churches and very willing to accept the book of mormon.  His wife is catholic and is a little less willing to believe, but I can tell that she feels the spirit when we are there and I think she just needs to have time.  There is also Marcos and Rose, who because Rose dosnt read well are reading the Book of Mormon together.  Our last visit she was excited about what she read about the resurection in 2NE 2.  We also have other excellent investigators, and I enjoy watching people feel the spirit and how it makes them happier.       I was studying in PMG 1 this week and decided to do the activity in the end of the section: The restoration; the foundation of faith.  I said something regarding revelation that I knew was true, and was also more less said by my Três avô when he said in his testimony to his posterity ''I have known all of the presidents of the church except Joseph Smith, and I have seen those that rejected them as prophets fall by the wayside and [perish], while those who sustain the prophets are prospered by the hand of the LORD and are blessed.''  The Church is guided by revelation and those who reject revelation are left behind to stagnate in the empty practices and traditions of men, as were the Jews and all others who rejected the SPOKEN word of God.  I have a testimony that we do in fact have prophets in our days and that they speak with GOD.  GOD lives, and we are his children.  Thats true and I love it.       Our numbers this week are:   0/010/49161860/43711141

## Subject: Fw: itajai II
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:01:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: itajai IIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 28 Jan 2008 16:14:47 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SchioserItajai IIZona ItajaiDear President Dansie,       All of my Emails to you have fallen through since I came out to Itajai, so I hope this makes it to you.  This week I have made a concerted effort to read the Book of Mormon PRAYERFULY, as I found a quote from President Hinckley in PMG 108 (english): ''I promise you without hesitation that if you prayerfully read the Book of Mormon, no matter how many times youve already read it, the Spirit of the Lord will will come into your heart.  You will feel a stronger determination t okeep the commandments and a stronger testimony of the living reaity of the Son of God''.  I took it up and I can say it makes a real difference, especially if youre seaching for the blessings promised in that statement.  Needless to say, ive been including this promise in my teachings to members and investigators alike, and it makes a considerable diference.  Music does too.  This week we had our monthly D-day for the zone here.  Its always very efective and its good to go with someone who isnt stuck in the missionary routines.  My assigned area was in the shopping district of the city, so we found (that means we had to serch for them) maybe fifty houses, almost all of which were empty (the beach is a two minute walk from there) and anyone that we encountered was a determined catholic, so I decided to change things up and instead of asking if we could leave a message, I started asking if I could come in and sing a hymn for them.  That worked so well that I think that is going to be one of my primary aproaches to knocking doors from this time henceforth.      This week Elder Schisoer had problems getting up and didnt want to accept help, so I called the zone leaders.  I dont particularly care for telling on people, so I just got it over with and tried to show an increase of love for him.  He wasnt too pleased for my calling, but as far as outward appearances go, I dont think hes holding it against me.         Our area is doing much better now and things are finally starting to pick up with the work, especially with the members giving references and taking friends to church.  We have a baptism this week -a thirteen year old named Evandro- who was a referral who wanted to get baptized from the beginning.  Im grateful that the Lord is answering my prayers for the area and the for the fire of the work in the hearts of the members.         This week as I was reading in Alma 7 verses 15-17 I decide to take the words of Alma seriously and I decided I believed the testimony he left of the Savior and decided to ''lay aside every sin which taketh you so easily'' and make a covenant to serve the Lord, by taking the sacrament.  I love the Book of mormon and know it is true.  I love to testify of its miraculous power in drawing us nearer to Christ.    our numbers this week are0/012/514303060/10409142needless to say I feel good about last week.

## Subject: Fw: Dear Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:02:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 31 Dec 2007 19:55:15 +0000Dear Family,      I apologize for your not recieving a letter last week, I sent it to Dads earthlink address and it blocked it, so I include last weeks letter at the end of this letter.  This week is transfers and it looks as if no one is moving, much to the disappointment of the members here.  They were hoping that Elder Schioser would be transferred, but hes staying.  They have been complaining to the zone leaders and me about him.  I think he is the reason we havnt eaten in a members house this transfer and while I know that he can be annoying, sarcastic and lacking in social skills, I dont think there is a particular reason to hate him and call him a slacker.  I am kind of disappointed in the members pride and how much it has hindered the missionary work here.  I sometimes feel that there is alot waiting to happen here, but everyone is just waiting for my companion to leave before doing anything and every once in a while I feel like its wasting my short time as a missionary.  Oh well, I guess it dosnt really matter as long as Im doing every thing I can.       Ive been making a strong effort to improve my prayers and have the spirit with me always.  I think its working ever so slowly.  I have also been studying the talk given by President Eyring in Priesthood meeting in october.  It helps me focus on how to be really effective.  Im learning that the greatest powers I can have at my personal disposal are those of personal righteousness and the influence of the Holy Ghost, not just for my personal benefit, but more especially for the benefit of others.  President Dansie had mentioned how when he was a bishop the members always liked to have him around because they felt happy and safe in his presence.  He says the missionaries generally have the same ''aura'', and as I looked over at my companion, I thought to myself: we do??  For a while I just thought that people must imagine this, but as I have made a concerted effort to recognize it, I realize that we do indeed carry a spirit with us, but it depends in strength upon our personal worthiness.  I have been trying to have that spirit in my persona and influence my companion to do better just through example and a little more communication and I think its working more or less.       Sorry to rattle on... this week has been well enough, it was still hot, but oh well, what can one do more than sweat alot?  I finally broke down and bought a liter of Ice cream for six reais, which equates to-way overpriced-, but it was good.  Thats the second time Ive had icecream in the field.  Ive really missed it.       Christmas was fun, we ate lunch at the stake presidents house which was by far the most fancy house Ive yet seen in Brasil; it had wood floors, two stories, a swimming pool, well furnished and real silver ware.  Here in Brasil we would call it -shique demais- or by way of translation, ridiculously fancy.       Other than that, there is not a whole lot to tell about this week, so Ill just wish you all a happy new year and know that I love you all very much.                 Love Elder Andrews  (December 24)I look forward to talking to ya ll tomorrow, its been a while. This week we had our christmas conference with the zones from itajai joinville and joinville north. It was really wonderfull and President Dansie gave a presentation on Joseph Smith (thats been one of our study focusses this transfer) and I got to sing A poor wayfaring man of grief and praise to the man for him. It was really well put together and had a very sweet spirit. then we had a white elephant game. I gave away a multi proposito trocinho para os missionarios(multi purpose dudeamafargin for missionaries[a teeny weirdly shaped pocket knife]) with an instruction manual in english and portuguese. It was pretty funny and one of the assistants got it. I got some REALLY cheap candy and a santa hat. it was still fun to play the game though.I remember when I interviewed with farmers ins. and they gave a ''were sorry but we cant accept you'' letter three and a half months later when I had already gotten another job. I laughed that they felt it was necessary to still send it so late after the fact. Personally I thought it was a joke!Its pretty cool that both Charles and Ben have gotten their degrees! Parabens!well I am running out of time so I have to cut the letter short, but I feel it appropriate to add that .....Im dreaming of a white christmas...today it was over 100 degrees. It just dosnt seem like christmas.Love, Elder AndrewsPS. Hey Charles this is your favorate twenty-one year old brother. merry christmas to you too. ;-D

I really have made a concerted effort to gain more of the spirit as I teach, and to make a stronger effort to pray in faith as it says in PMG chapter 4.  I have definately seen a difference in my messages to the members and even in some of our lessons.  We represent Christ in peoples homes, so Im trying to live up to that for the benefit of those I serve.  Im beginning to learn that while the powers of the enemy are great, the influence of the Holy Ghost and righteousness are greater in their power, especially in creating an environment for keeping the commandments and influencing those we teach to repent and change.  As President Eyring put it in conference: ''Our duty, which IS in our power, is to live in such a way that when we teach, the Holy Ghost will carry our words to the hearts of those we teach and that they will see the fruits of the spirit in our lives and want to change.''  Or at least thats more or less what he said.        Things with my companion could definately be going better.  I try to be encouraging.  Many times I do not understand what he says and ask for an explanation or I miss a key word in a given phrase and he gets mad that Im not listening, but I dont like to ask for explanations because of his sarcastic answers.  Quite frankly it hurts my feelings.  This week we went to a members house who lives forty minutes from our house by foot the night before transfers to teach a lesson to her and her relatives who were visiting.  Elder Schioser wanted to stay and play a video game with her sons.  At more or less nine o clock I asked of we could leave and he asked the irmã if she could give us a ride, but she said she couldnt until later because she hadnt registered her license plate yet, so she would have to wait until there were less police on the street.  So Elder Schioser said that we could wait until nine thirty to leave and sat down to play video games again.  Her family was also making a churrasco which was ready at 9 pm.  So we ate as fast as we could we managed to leave though I felt a little guilty about robbing the guests of their hosts.  Meanwhile there were four elders waiting outside of our apartment since 8 pm and so the zone leaders called which call he decided not to answer.  A few minutes later we got a call from the Assistents.  When we got home at 9:40 ELder schioser walked right past the other elders and hurried to the apartment to get a DVD we had rented to watch for Pday that needed to be returned that night and after apologizing to the other elders and getting one of their bags, I followed him.  He was mad at me for not wanting to return the movie.  so we exchanged a few warm words.  Suffice it to say, I very much dislike it when missionaries want to play video games, and as I am told by the members, they dislike it too.  I wish missionaries would just be obedient to the rules, for their sakes and for the works sake.  The members in my area dont trust my companion and the results of it practically kill the effectivness of the work.  But Im ready to do what I can, after all, the influence of the Holy Ghost and of righteousness are greatest in their power.  Ill find a way with the help of the Lord.     Im sorry to say so much that is negative, and I apologize if it seems that Im complaining, I always look for the best in people so its easier to live with them.  Im grateful for the opportunities Ive been given to grow, I think I needed them.  Our area is good and as I get to know it I love it.  The members are very good and we have some perfect investigators.       I look forward to interviews and hope that you and Sister Dansie are doing well and feel the comfort and strength found in the spirit.  As a mision, we trust you and feel confident in your capacities to lead.  THank you for every thing you do.  OUr numbers this week are:0012/571612737216146

This week passed well, we had interviews with the president, which as a junior companion Ive learned is almost like a tattle tale session.  Sometimes I wish people would just be honest so that I dont have to tell the truth for them.  Whats more is that I wish people would just follow the rules.  But it was good to listen to training from the president and zone leaders.      Our members have put their complaints in the air about problems with the missionaries in the past and so Im going to have to work hard to maintain a trust between us, because my companion thinks every thing is just dandy. He always tells me hes not worried about crossing the busy highway because if one of the semis hits him it would destroy the truck, not him. I chewed her ear off for putting up values and interrests in the air for what would be cool.  A woman for president, because she(my friend) is blatantly feminist; a Black man for president for black rights and a marker against racsism; and a mormon for president because that would be neat.  And what do they have in common? ..........       Enough on politics.  I can get rather heated in my opinions, like most young people.  Brazil is as hot as ever, I dont know about Aphganistan, but I hope Noahs doing alright there.  I hear it gets hot there too.  We have an investigator who is from Iran and he taught me to write my name in persian.  Suffice it to say that it looks cool.        I hope you all have a good week and nothing I write is less than prudent, most of my communication skills are manifest in face to face relations and lost in txt messaging and emails, even occasioinally on the phone, so I apologize if I ever seem to have a big mouth.  I love you and look forward to hearing from you again next week.      Love Elder Andrews

It just gives me good motivation to keep the rules.        For the phone call on Christmas, the number for the phone we will be using is 011-55-48-9624-6872.  We are four hours ahead of you so at six in the morning it is ten o clock am and at noon there it is four here.  You could probably do the math in your head, but I wanted to test my arithmatic.  Not bad, eh?  You can call whenever you want, well have the phone with us all day, so fique vontade, tudo bem?        The members here seem somewhat closed to us and cold, so I called up Elder Giló, my trainer(the phone call is free because he works in the mission office) to ask him what he thought I could do because he is notorious for setting his areas on fire and getting the members to love him.  He gave me a couple of Ideas, but especially the advice that I could sing for the members in their homes.  That has made a more or less ridiculous difference in just one time, let alone the other opportunities that Ive taken to sing.  If I got a nickel for every time someone asks me about the CD Charles, Aurelia and I made, I would be a quintrillionaire.        I recieved my copy of the November Ensign this week.  Im so happy...  Ive been spending every spare moment reading it and I have to say, President Eyring´s talk during the General Priesthood Meeting is very study-worthy material.         Im sorry to hear that we lost a part of the sycamore tree, I love sycamore.  I miss the cold too, this christmas season dosnt seem like christmas at all because of the heat, but thats ok because nothing seems real right now.  A mission is like a two year bubble separated out of measure of time for me.  Time flies, today Ive been out for seven months.  I hope every body travels safely on their way home from school and other places.  Is Nicole (Woodbury) still planing on serving a mission?  Any ways, Merry Christmas and Talk to y'all next tuesday.            Love, Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Re: Merry Christmas
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Re: Merry ChristmasFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: fern.woodbury@gmail.comDate: Mon, 24 Dec 2007 20:15:15 +0000Dear Grandma -and Barbara Rick and family if youre still with them-,       Thank you for the note, I always love hearing from you.  This week the family has been in my thoughts alot, especially Mom.  We got our conference editions of the Ensign, which Ive been reading very ravenously as I didnt understand a word of it when it was broadcasted in portuguese.  I liked the article by Julie Beck about mothers who know.  Mom qualified with flying colors on all subjects and you do too, Grandma.  The following days it was impressed on me that my Mom knew and does know, and I remembered the things I learned from her through example.  I saw her pray in the mornings when she got up, I saw and heard her read scriptures and seek revelation to help her raise her children, and even the last day of her life she was trying to fulfill her responsibilities for the Primary.  Thank you for raising you children so well.        These last two days have been more or less difficult to actually teach lessons or even leave messages with people because of the season, so me and my companion resorted to singing carols to our investigators and converts.  We may not have pumpkin pie to give, but we can always try to bless their lives with the spirit.  My companion is completely tone deaf, but we still manage to bring the spirit of the music, which is by far more important.  It kind of reminds me of that ''activity'' we used to do when every body picks their own key to start in and every body starts singing and tries to keep their own key, no matter how bad it sounds.  I know I can win now...       The members treat us well enough though I was informed by our zone leaders this week that my ward in general dislikes my companion, so there is some coldness there, but Im hoping to change that, and it is already slowly changing.  we will be spending christmas at a new member famliys house who like us, so alls well.  Im glad that Uncle Rick is still humble about his cheesecake ''building'' abilities.  Im sure if the missionaries knew the possibilities of deliciousness found at Barbaras and Ricks, they would spend both christmas AND christmas eve at the Putnams.  Their loss.         I love you all and wish you a merry Christmas.  Let me bear testimony that Jesus Christ is our brother and King.  He certainly did leave a path to follow that we can trust and tread, and while He was and is the Son of God, He was just like us in mortality, and -if we will- we can be just like Him in eternity.  He is our Savior, and we can ''behold the condesension of God'' in his birth.                   Love,   Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Dear Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:04:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Dear FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 3 Dec 2007 17:34:06 +0000Dear Family,       my companion and I are still working on what we will be doing for christmas, especially since christmas eve falls on a p-day, so Im not sure what the plan is for calling, but Im slowly gathering the info needed.  Congratulations to Charles on the graduation and the solo too.  Id sure be interested to know what hes singing.  Im sure he and Aurelia will be more or less atounding to assembled guests, no matter what they sing.  This week has passed relativley fast, and the events of the week were smooth and after looking at the numbers we achieved, I have to say things happen easier even though it requires the same amount of effort make things happen.  My companion works hard to find people and we are teaching well enough.  Its just hard to stay focused on portuguese during lessons and meetings.       I dont know what it is about this place, but cockroaches live in an abundance, despite my efforts to clean our apartment.  I think the problem extends to all inhabitants of the building we live in as well.  I didnt really see a noticeable number in Criciuma, and I lost count last week, so I might have to look into it.  I think PART of the problem could be found in the fact that I may be the first one to ever clean the bathroom in the last eternity.  I swear I must have used half a bottle of toilet cleaner in one scrubbing.  Members always ask me if President Dansie is coming to apartment when they see me buy toilet cleaner, so I think the issue could be found in all missionary apartments, excepting most of the sisters.  I just have a preference of smell when I enter the Bathroom.       Since I was about twelve, I always took notice that my parents never really held a grudge and were generally calm faced in the front of annoyance.  I try to emulate it, though sometimes its hard.  I dont think I can hold a grudge for more than six hours before forgetting it.  And then if someone buggs me again, I really want to lash out at them and tell them of all their previous offences were, but I dont ever remember what they were, even though I know they happened.  So if any one thinks that I dont fight back, its usually just that I have a horrible memory.  I dont worry so much about what kinds of things I might have done to offend mom as much as the things that I do now, when can see all, that might offend her.  Knowing that a person dosnt hold a grudge is a good thing to me as it allows me to always be comfortable around the said person.  If not, I end up walking on glass trying not to trigger memories on past grudges they may be holding.       Any ways, I hope none of that sounds cocky or selfrighteous.  I appreciate your letters, prayers and love, and you can always remember that I love you and pray for you all as well.  Have a good week.             Love                         Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: ItajaiII
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:04:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: ItajaiIIFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: MP8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 26 Nov 2007 20:38:20 +0000Elder AndrewsElder SchioserItajaí IIItajaíDear President Dansie,      this week has been good and I enjoy working with Elder Schioser, he is great.  I had a good Thanksgiving and even though I didn´t get to officially celebrate it, I was able to write in my journal the things that I am most grateful for and feel a spirit of thanksgiving throughout the day.  I have been reading in second Nephi, and on that particular day I read 2NE 4.  I am glad that Nephi was able to follow the spirit in his writing as that particular chapter is a jewel in the Book of Mormon.  I have been enjoying reading the passages in Isaiah as well, even if you can´t understand certain things, or just don´t have the patience to decypher everything, you can still enjoy the spirit of the text and feel the spirit.      Thank you for putting me with Elder Schioser, he does a great job at planning, and though he stuggles getting up in the morning, he is very serious about hte morning schedule, something Elder Fontenele wasn´t so much focused on.  while I am somewhat sad to leave the people in Criciuma, I am very pleased with the opportunity to start anew.  I always enjoy what is said in the trasfer meetings about hope and opportunity.  Its true.  Elder Schioser is either very sincere, or very overtly demonstrative in his prayers and Im inclined to think it is the former.  I look forward to hearing his prayers during the day.  He is a good man.       Our area is good and, much to the satisfaction of my legs, very flat.  The members are open and give us references, two of which have already turned into marked baptisms, Jean and Felipe.  When I told the sister who gave us the referrals, she couldnt believe they were already marked for baptism.  Elder Schioser is also very good at helping the investigators make commitments.       The following paragraph may be included in the group of miracles that Sister Dansie is making:       This past saturday, the Itajaí stake held D-Day, a day when the whole zone gets together in one ward area and does divisions with the members and then- we find people.  I feel it appropriate to say that there is a general comfort zone in the way we as missionaries go about our business and especially in the case of our contacts; most of the time it is just giving a card away, and just that.  The member that I went with, Maurício, has served a mission and was very enthusiastic in talking to people.  We knocked on a few doors with relatively good success and after a few houses, we stopped for a moment, trying what to do next as we had reached the end of the street.  I told Maurício that rather than just leaving a short message, I would rather leave the first lesson in a very short formatting of ten minutes, more or less, so I explained the principles and asked him to be able to share his testimony whenever he wanted during the lessons duration.  Maurício asked to pray.  So we did.  He said the prayer.  He spoke to Heavenly Father of the blessings we had and wanted to find a family, one that was ready.  So we got up and walked down the street until we came to a fork in the road.  One was paved and looked as if it would have a good yield of residents, and the other was a dirt road ascending the hill and looked relativley inhabitantless.  However, I remember one of my most wonderful baptisms was in a similar street, far beyond what seemed likely, so we decided to ascend the hill on via this dusty dirt road.  We came upon a group of four houses hidden in the trees and so we clapped our hands.  For nearly five minutes all that issued from the house was a rather vicious looking dog, but we waited.  A man with one arm and a cast on his leg came out, it looked as though he had walked thirty yards on this cast to get to us and he was calling to the dog.  I couldn´t tell if he was saying ''peggy''  or ''pegue ele''.  But we asked if we could leave a message, even if it had to be outside of the house and so we started with a prayer.  Then we taught the first two principles of the first lesson and Maurício bore his testimony.  The man interrupted and asked if he could come to church as well as his family and also if we could come back and teach his family, all of which occupy the four houses.  Maurício will be taking them to church this comeing sunday and while I do not think that I will ever get the opportunity to return to Blumenau (who knows?), I feel the spirit testify that that Maurício´s humble prayer was answered, and that if he had not been there with the missionaries that day, we would not have found Valdenir.  The Lord guides the work.  Even if we do not baptize the whole world, we can still bring hope to them that sit in darkness, to lift the hands that hang hoplessly down, to love our bretheren and sisters.       Our numbers this week are:0/013/641871061511143/9       Thank you for every thing you do for us.                                   -Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Oi Família!
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:05:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Oi Família!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 29 Oct 2007 15:38:46 +0000Dear family,       This week went well, we had interviews with President Dansie in Tubarão and it was fun to have the elders from Criciúma 1 and Arangua over for the night to prepare for the bus ride.  Its good to talk to other americans.  I figured that since I didn´t get a letter last week you were probably busy or traveling so naturally I didnt freak out.  We got a call from some elders in Boston informing us that they had a new convert coming down to Criciúma (there are alot of brazilians in Boston) so we went to visit her this week and after I asked a few questions about trees in boston she asked if I had ever been to the states.  I replied that I used to live there and she asked for how long.  She thought I was brazilian!  ISSO!  I was more or less ridiculously pleased.      Tip for the week:  The trees are only turning yellow because the first trees to turn colors are ash trees.  Most neighborhoods in Olathe that are older have pin oak-which will just turn brown later in the season and keep the majority of leaves throughout the winter- and Green ash, which turn yellow.  Newer neighborhoods will be turning Purple fisrt because they plant alot of Autumn purple ash, which are more popular than green ash because they are less suceptable to borers and they are male trees so they do not produce fruit.  In mid to late november, youll be seeing all the katrillions of red maples- esp the red sunset variety which everyone and their dogs fleas buy for their front yard- which I, even myself sold last fall by quite literally thousands.  This is because Maples are naturaly from the north and as such are more accustomed to the  cold.  I tend to prefer red oak and legacy sugar maple myself, which are native to the new england area.  I miss american trees.     I sendmy personal congratulations to Bogrid on his excellent academic achievements.  I´m sure Mikail Ivanovitch would be worried to find his enemy following so well in his footsteps.  Sydney´s soccer program saound fun, I bet she is alot better than I am.  I think people suppose that soccer is just kicking a ball back and forth kind of like they think that boxing is just ''two men standing there hitting each other'', but people stop the ball, dance around it and spin it in different directions etc fake people out etc.  There´s a young man in our ward who is more than proficient at this who I call twinkle toes.  I bet you all enjoyed the Bsass Pro Shop in springfield.  when people watch 'Cars' I always explain what a red-neck is to them.  they like to hear about the guys who catch four foot catfish using their fists as bait...     I hope Grandma Z is doing alright, the members out there in bellefontaine are amazing so we can trust that she is in good hands.    Well I love Ya´ll so have a good week and BEEE GOOOOOOOOD....               Love                 Elder Andrews.         PS.  Its hot

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Opa Familia!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 26 Nov 2007 19:51:31 +0000Dear Family,       Sorry I didn´t write last week, my companion didn´t seem to want to use the internet last week and seeing as I cant go anywhere without my companion, I didn´t write.  My compliments to Dad on his perception on transfers.  I am now in the sea port of Itajaí, a few hours north of Florianopolis.  Let me describe my new companion.       Last sunday night after we found out about transfers, my trainer, Elder Giló called to ask if I was excited to be transferred.  I said sure and then I asked if he knew anything about my new companion Elder Schioser.  I wish you could hear Elder Gilos accent- ''Oh ELDER,...  He´s so FAAAT!''  Whenever I told people he would be my companion, they just laughed and gave me the ''look'' as if I were on my way to ...a really bad place.  Elder Schioser snores something terrible.  Apparently my zone leader went on divisions with him one time and couldnt sleep all night.  Lucky for me I am a heavy sleeper.  But I really like Elder Schioser, he does what hes supposed to and it is like a breath of fresh air.  I suppose my only complaint would be that he takes up the whole side walk!  He is my first companion that dosn´t speak any english, so my poertuguese is improving and I find myself quite surprised at how well I speak and understand now.       I hope you all had a happy Thanksgiving, I remembered you and hope that you all know that I love you very much.  We got a fair amount done and I am enjoying my new area though it is really flat and there are no hills to let you know where you are-or if your legs arent strong enough.  I am glad that Charles was able to get back to ID in one piece, sounds like he had some troubles with his car, but he is an andrews, so he´s bound to have car troubles on a road trip.       On Saturday we went to Blumenau to have a D- Day.  Basically the whole zone goes to one ward area and splits with the members, making roughly twenty companionships and we go and find people.  It was VERY effective and I must say that Blumenau (founded by the germans) is something of a gorgeous city.  One of the americans had the nerve to mention pumpkin pie.  All the rest of us walked around for the rest of the day with mouths watering and hearts pining.  Well, I hope all goes well at home and that Morgan and Anna finish the semester well.  I suppose that goes for Charles and Aurelia too.  I´d like to know what time of day will be best to call on Christmas as President Dansie wants us to make all the preparations now.  We´re on daylight savings time right now.  And if you get a chance tell Stephen Harper I am serving in Itajaí and I got to go to Blumenau.  He served more or less in those places.             Love, Elder Andrews      

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Subject: Fw: Hello Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:05:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Hello FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 5 Nov 2007 20:24:00 +0000Dear Family,      this week was well enough, we went to the college again to teach english and a little about the church.  Alot of questions to answer.  I talked to my companion about the state of the area that we´re assigned to cover and we decided to improve some things that needed improving and our comunication, so hopefully our area will progress a little better.      Im really missing the fall right now, especially after what Dad wrote about hot chocolate and cider.  I love the changes in seasons.  The air always seems fresher...  Congratulations to Catherine on the baby!  I really miss all of my neices and nephews, I hope they are all doing well.  Well even if the publishers don´t like Dads book, you can always try to publish it for the family or something for their benefit.  Id be interrrested in reading it when I get back.       I got to give a talk in a missionary fireside yesterday about missionary work.  Surprise, surprise.  I started by talking about the war in heaven, which I dont think was so much a war with swords as much as it was a fight to get others to make the right decisions.  Im sure there were people that were not so sure they could succeed and were thinking of supporting the other plan to insure their success, and we know the enemy is particularly gifted at making us feel lesser than we really are, but there were other stronger people, who said that we could have faith, that no matter the negative consequences, we could hope for salvation through the Savior.  We promised people that we would help them.  Missionary work has existed since before this world, it exists now and exists after this life.  We have the opportunity to serve now, as members of the Church, to fulfill promises and reap the rewards of our earlier missionary work and valiance in this life.       I find it interresting that the only pain or sorrow Heavenly Father feels and can feel is in regards to his childrens unrighteousness and whether they love him or not.  It is not in lost planets or galaxies, but in the loss of his own children.  I feel confident that if it were necessary He would cause whole star systems to evaporate into nothingness to allow us to return to Him.  But instead, He leaves it up to the direction of His Son, and the rest of his hosts children in doing the work before, during and after this life on the earth so that we may grow as a family and return to His presence as His children ready and worthy to inherit the divine stewardship of godhood, having proved ourselves selfless and just, redeemed of the Son.      That was more or less the theme of my talk with a short part about how to turn our faith into action through making goals and commitments.       I hope you all have a good week this week and remember that I love you all.               Love                         Elder Andrews

And when they wanted to put Diego, six foot tall and all arms and legs, in the back with us, everyone consented that it was too much.  the member that gave us a ride told us about his puppy that fell from the deck of his house on a chain and leash.  He says it died, so he performed mouth to mouth recsusitation...  It lives...  The things people do for their Dogs...  Its funny to see an eight year old running in the isles during sacrament meeting during the prayer and trying to run while praying with his eyes closed.  I think you all can use your imagination as to what happens in such cases.  Im just glad I was taught to be reverent in church.  Any how, those are some things that rather tickled me this week, so I hope you all enjoy them too.         I love you all and thank you all for the sacrifices youve made for me and hope all goes well for you.                     Love                                Elder Andrews

I got an email from Paul Paul that I thought was from Uncle Paul until he said he was getting ready to serve a mission and I did a double take.  It was pretty funny.  Ill probably write a reply snail mail next week.  The pouch service is no longer available, people probably sent too many photos or things that you should only send through regular mail.  So if any if you want to send mail, go ahead and send it to the mission adress.      Sorry Aurelia is having such a hard time, Im kindof glad I dont have to worry about cars and money for while yet, its very nice.  A family we baptized a month or so ago ismoving to São Paulo to work, get passports and move to spain.  They invited Elder Gilo and I to go visit them after the mission.  theyre remarkably strong in hard times, because Marco, the father worked in portugal for a long time and saved ALOT of money and moved back here to live.  He lent out about 100,000 reais and helped out some people and had hired a lawer to get him a passport and tickets to spain, but the lawer took off with all six thousand reais and now the family is living in a house the size of my room back home.  But theyre still fine and optomistic.  Theres not really a whole lot else to tell this week so I guess Ill go ahead and finish up. For lack of a better example you mightrecall elder Calhoun and elder VanPelt from the best two years. Theirapproach to dealing with companions was quite different and you wold bebest off if you didn’t take the confrontational approach. Some times wejust have to kind of o with the flow and do the best that we can.The other thing that you should understand is that having a companion ispreparation for having a wife. Once you are married to someone who isimperfect as you will also be it is important to deal with thesituations that arise in a way that will be as constructive as possible.If you approach things in the wrong way you may just make them worse.Learn now so that you will be more prepared for marriage when it does come.We have had weather in the sixties and seventies this week and it hasbeen beautiful weather except Monday and Saturday when it rained. It hasbeen in the forties and fifties at night and kind of nippy in the earlymornings. We really did need the rain so I was happy to have it.This week has been a lousy week for me. I have lacked animation as wellas motivation. Nothing seems to have gone real well and just not funthough nothing great has gone wrong.I think Aurelia has had the same kind of week maybe. I’m not really surehow all here week went. She called earlier this week and bent my ear fora while. She said she hated living with girls. They got a new roommatethat is immature and was unhappy and wanted to change roommates. Wellthey got together and had a talk session in which everyone said all thewrong things. And now everyone hates everyone else’s guts. She went outto her car and it ran out of gas before she got out of the parking lot,which is a lucky thing. However she was going to have to ask one of herroommates to take her to the gas station and she knew that that wouldonly irritate them more. She is also low on funds till she gets her nextpay check. She was on her way to the testing center to take a quiz whenshe called and got to the center before she was any where near done. Shesat on a bench by the doors and finished talking. After the quiz a youngman, a freshman, approached her and said that he had overheard her phoneconversation about her desperate straights and asked if he could takeher to get gas. She accepted and he did. He also put twenty dollarsworth of gas in her car. The young man commutes to school every day fromTaylorsville, Utah. At any rate she was a little shocked and also glad.I told her tho thank the Lord for the young mans kindness when she saidher prayers.Charles called one night this week and said he had participated in arelay of some kind each person ran around the track once and I have noidea as to ow many people were involved but he said that he broke sixtyseconds for his lap. He was pleased to have done so well.Ben and I tore the probe apart this week. There was a problem with thedrivers side front tire. We had to take the lower control arm off and inthe process we had to cut the stabilizer link off. It was a little bitof a hassle but we eventually got it off. One of the bushings was wornout and casing the tire to wear badly. The front end couldn’t be alignedtill we fixed it. We ordered parts but they won’t be here till Tomorrow.Ben also ordered a new tire which we picked up. I got the ball jointreplaced on the arm so we just have to wait for parts.Well that is most of the news from here again.LoveDad

It was pretty fun and I got to teach the entire first lesson (the restoration and the Book of Mormon) to twenty seven people.  We gave out cards to recieve the Book of Mormon to all the students, so I think we might get a few lessons out of that. I had a good time and I think soccer is fun, so as I was watching from the side I got to know one  of the guys who was there to play. Its really fascinating how it works and how fast the pit stop teams are.  The average pit stop is 5.4 seconds.  One of the drivers hit a pit worker as he was coming into the pits.  He had already slowed down so he didn´t do much besides knock him down.  The pit workers make something like 347$ per hour.  I think its interresting that the USA isolates itself from the the rest of the world in sports in that we don´t really care about soccer, we dont really care about formula one but have our own Indy 500 etc.       Well, I hope you are all doing well and love you all.              Love, Elder Andrews

They should arrive in approximately sixteen days, so be patient. I am quasi studying the compilation of the canon and  find the histories quite interresting and the words particularly covering the formation of the masoretic texts intrigue me. ## Subject: Fw: Hello Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:07:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Hello FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 24 Sep 2007 21:53:10 +0000Dear family,       I got a letter from Granma Woodbury today, and I enjoyed reading it.  As I grow older and older(which is still relativley young), I gain more and more appreciation for my pregenitors and more proud of my heritage on all sides of the family.  I´m glad that some of the family will get to go to general conference in salt lake, I really want to hear that choir in person some day.        I think Dad is right that your attitude makes all the difference in your work, because even when you´re not activley doing your assigned labors, you can still be doing the mental parts of the work and influence others in a positive way.  Yesterday we were walking in a thunderstorm on the way back home( our area is reputed for being the largest in the mission and we walked for 9 Kilometers in the pouring rain) but I decided that I couldn´t get any wetter so I started ''singing in the rain'' and singing Isn´t it a lovely day to be caught in the rain.  It kept me in good spirits and my companion laughing.  Thanks Fred Astaire and Don Lockwood.        I like the topic of the book youre writing Dad, I have often commented, quite forcefully at times, the need for balance between ethics and morals and how executive decisions should be more guided by morals than ethics.  Interesting.  Also, especially in relation to the story of Joseph and Potifar´s wife based on the perspective of which guided his actions, ethics or morals?  Also, was it predetermined of premeditated what his actions\reactions would be?  Intriguing...       I have many favorite scriptures, all based on different subjects and perspectives, but universally it would be this: ''Behold a new commandment I give unto you, that ye love one another even as I loved you.  This new commandment I give unto you that ye love one another.  By this shall men know ye are My diciples, that ye love one another.''  I don´t have my scriptures on hand, so that may have some mistakes, but if there be mistakes they are of man not of God... I think the scripture reference is ST John 13:34-35.       I was teaching the first lesson one day and I noticed as we were reading the introduction, it says to read, then ponder on the MESSAGE of the Book of Mormon, and then pray.  What is the message of the Book of Mormon?  Judging by who wrote it( Mormon and Moroni) It seems good to first ask under what circumstances it was written and the style of the writers.  In nearly all places in which we recieve the interjecory narration and commentary from the authors, I see three things that display themselves, other than direct testimony of the Savior, conspicuously: First Hope, second Faith and third the fruits drawn therefrom: Charity.  See the interjections in especially in Helaman 3, Ether 12, Mormon 7 and the final chapters of the book of mormon.  This Hope, the Hope of a better world and of being clean is ''an anchor to the souls of men'' which enables them to have trust enough in the power of the atonement of Christ to excercise faith and ''try his works to do''(all of which were concieved through Charity).  I want to share my witness to the reality of the Savior and his ressurrection and Gospel in English as it helps me keep it truly real to me.      I know that Jesus Christ lives.  This is the victorious cry that I try to proclaim into darkness of despair in my actions and words.  through the atonement of Jesus Christ and our subsequent acceptance of this and HIs Gospel(Faith, Repentance, Baptism and the reciept of the gift of the Holy Ghost and the remaining Ordinances in the Temple) we can become clean, recieve his name, which I add is THE ONLY NAME GIVEN UNDER HEAVEN BY WHICH WE CAN BE SAVED, and return to our Father in Heaven to live forever with our precious loved ones, our families.  None of these things are said of habit or just the way I learned to express them, but these are what comprise my witness of Christ and my childhood of God.  I know these things.       I love you all and wish the best for you all this week.                  Love,                           Elder Andrews      PS sorry to preach, But when one is separated from family save for a few words a week in writing, your focus shifts to the most important things.

Transfers are this week but we´re both staying put and we are´nt getting another companionship until next transfer so it looks like I could stay here for another two transfers easy.  We got to go to General Conference but it was in Portuguese and they didn´t know how to put a tv up with english like they usually do for the American elders so I didn´t really understand very well.       By far the best thing that I learned was through something that happened in the middle of Joseph B Wirthlin´s talk.  He is getting weaker and therefore was trembling as he was talking, I don´t know if you all noticed, and the pulpit started to shake as well.  I was kind of worried that he might fall backward or something and I noticed President Monson in that backround and that he too was noticing this.  A few moments later, Elder Nelson came out of the dark backround and held Elder Wirthlin up and stood behind him until the end of his talk.  Elder Wirthlin didn´t make it obvious that he noticed but just kept on talking.  It really touched me that Elder Nelson stayed there, supporting his old friend with whom he has served for a long, long time.  It was charity and I could see the concern in the face of Elder Nelson and it reminded me of the way that when we need help to do what is asked of us, there is always the Savior there to hold our arm and steady our trembling selves.      Consequently, I am going to take Dad´s advice to choose something to change in our lives based on somthing we learned in conference and work on charity and doing service spontaneously.  I don´t really feel close to my companion so I´m going to try to be a good companion to influence him to have the confidence to fulfill his mission with honor.  He dosn´t particularly like to work or study, But all missionaries come out on the mission with desires to do a good job and be the best missionaries, but after a few lesser than perfect companions and some time they just don´t have the confidence or will to continue.        I personally cannot live with myself if I do not at least try to do everything possible because if I could only be out here for the time I paid for, I would be home right now, so since my family and friends are paying for me to be here and working, I owe it to you all to do the best I can.  I´m still a greenie, so I´m doing my best not to judge and learn the positive things from my senior companion, so I´m going to try to make him love and respect me through sincere service and better communication.       I´m almost positive that I already told Morgan how my study journals work, but I might repeat it especialy because it might prove helpful in his goal to follow the spirit in his life.  Like Dad said, it is helpful to write down promptings of things to do, with an area to check off the things that you´ve accomplished and to have an area to write down thoughts, memories and ispirations you have.  My study journal has never left my side for almost three years now and Ive refilled it three times already.  Maybe Ill send a photocopy of some pages to him in my next letter to him.  I also have a true study journal specially for studying and a regular journal which, I flatter myself, are well integrated and referenced in each other and in my scriptures.  I try to keep my daily journal as interesting as possible, preserving my humorous, spiritual and intellectual sides to keep it ''diverting''. Always Pray and read the scriptures and you will never fall.  That´s something Ive learned from experience.  well, I love you all and pray for you often.  If you pray for me, ask please that I may have strength against temptations, I hope and pray that you are all blessed for your supporting me on my mission.  I love you. [jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Criciúma 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: mp8-dansiel@myldsmail.netDate: Mon, 10 Sep 2007 20:40:08 +0000Elder AndrewsElder FonteneleCriciúma 1Zona TubarãoDear President Dansie,      This week went well, I have been pondering on an experience we had a few weeks ago when we encountered a man from Assemblia de Deus.  He spoke ALOT and very loudly, and afterwards I wondered about things and the different religions and their truths, and if we really do have the authority of God.  They say that the signs of the gifts of the spirit follow the servants of God and the evangelicals pride themselves in having the gift of tongues.  I felt that I lacked the gift of tongues because I have such a hard time understanding anything in portuguese.  But I made and interesting discovery this week that there are two gifts of tongues, that of speaking and that of interpreting.  I know for a fact that I have been blessed with the gift of speaking in tongues due to my experiences in the CTM and my ability to teach without notes.  Also in relation to the Authority, we were at a stake wide service project and I was wondering who was in charge when I heard a young man yelling for a bunch of people to come to him and every body within the sound of his voice turned around to see what he wanted.  any one can call in a loud voice but there are certain people who kow what must happen in the great service project of life and only htey have the athourity to direct the project.  it is the same with the work of God.  we have a prophet ot direct the work of God and throw down the counterfeits of the devil. ## Subject: Fw: Opa!
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:19:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Opa!From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 3 Sep 2007 17:36:43 +0000Dear Family,      I got a email from Papa that somehow managed to beat my last letter in length or the lack thereof.  I laughed.  Last week we had two baptisms, and three days later Elder Giló was transferred.  I´m sad, the members are sad and the secretary office is pleased with the new secrtary to the president, Elder Giló.  He gets to do President´s dirty work for six months.  Lucky him.       We used to have six umbrellas in the apartment, but apparently they were all elder gilós, so when it rained on friday, there was a broken down black one and a grey one in the kitchen as well.  I kindly let Elder Fontenelle use the black one and quickly learned some things about the grey one.        Most of the umbrellas here form a perfect upside down U or bowl shape.  This grey one however followed a flat plane peaking and decending in the middle.  While these features drew the mind of teh beholder to the designs in architecture furniture and art of the far east, I found that the most intriguing feature of this ''guarda-chuva'' was the designers apparent zeal for interior design.  the observer of the missionary in possesion of teh said umbrella might think  ''that missionary has a grey umbrella which i call peculiar in design.''      however there is more to grey, small, simple, and seemingly drab umbrella than meets the eye.  from the book of JL Andrews vol. one we read about this humble haven to the creature we call man from teh pounding precipitation;     ''Behold I looked into the heavens and gazed into the firmament above my head and lo, a whit wheel filled as it were with purple pimpernels and also the wheel was encircled about with crimson and also after this the white and flowers continuing; and while in the midst of tehis vision of glory, I beheld and percieved that my companion laughed, and behold the heavens were wroth and the rain descended upon him htat he was wet.''      THere are many interpretations of this passage, some of which have drawn on the 'colorfulness' of speach to be interpreted as such preposterous Ideas as a prophecy concerning Icew cream having no bones; a vision of Elvis wearing Mickey mouse ears; or even past generals of Czechoslavakia, all of which are so positivley revolting in their puerile inconsistency.  that we may well presume these to ve the fictitiousimaginations of seekers of fame based on preumed perception of ancient scripture.  we dismiss  all such inventions with ignominious injunction of ignorant infantile egostism.      What we gather from this explicit thouugh rather colorful account through practical analysis is the unique nature of havcing a white circle filled with flowers (probably Lavender, as is included in the footnotes and various commentary from such authorities as Jose Andreas guieseppi andreasini and mickail Ivanovitch) with a large portion of red circling this with a border simulating  design of the center.  Also a warning against making fun of others.      WE also encountered an evangelical preacher whose Right eye wandered and shouted loud enough to drown out ......alot.     well, I love you all and wish he best to you.   love Elder Andrews

## Subject: Fw: Hi Family
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:20:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Hi FamilyFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 20 Aug 2007 20:41:19 +0000Dear Family,      Thank you for the letters this week.  I especially appreciate the advice on getting along with my companion.  Though my companion is practically perfect in every way, I´m sure I won´t always be so lucky in my companions so I´m going to preserve the advice for the rest of my mission and perhaps you should save that letter as I may ask for it again and again in life.  We had zone conference this week and I had a good time.  I have commented to the President several times In my letters that Elder Giló sets up commitments perfectly and ''seamlessly'', so president Dansie asked us to give a demonstration of this ''seamless'' commitment for the four zones present.  He also gave permission to Elder Giló to kill me afterwards for having such a big mouth.        I got a letter from Grandma Woodbury in which she mentioned the importance of keeping the sabbath day holy.  If one looks at the order of the creation in the scriptures, you can notice a symbolism of Important events correlating with the seven millenia that have transpired starting with the fall ending with the sanctification of the earth and setting of man to rule on the earth in righteousness.  This became apparent to me when I went to the temple and noted that the creation is listed in different order.  If you watch for the number seven and ask why that number, such as in the case of the story of Naaman and you will start to see things.  There have been seven Major dispensations since the fall; Adam, Enoch, Noah, Abraham, Moses, the primitive church, and the dispensation of the fullness of times(now).  after being immersed in these seven dispensations, man kind will be clean.  Also it will be worthy of note that the prophet did not see him in person but his servant told him what to do.  Mooey interasontey...       I love you all very much, especially Dd. And Aurelia. And Morgan.  And Anna.  And as I think about it, ''I love you all individually with affection un bounded and unmeasued in this world.  But collectivley...''      Have a good week family and read the scriptures and pray every day in the name of the LORD.                            Elder Andrews

He married Brandy Gaughn. He will start seminary two Mondaysfrom tomorrow. Anna and I went over to the school today and her teacherwill be Mrs. Pitner. ## Subject: Fw: Criciúma 1
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:20:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Criciúma 1From: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: mp8-dansiel@ldsmail.netDate: Mon, 20 Aug 2007 20:16:51 +0000Elder AndrewsElder GilóCriciúma 1zona TuberãoDear Pres Dansie,       I enjoyed my first Zone Conference, though I have to admit I was a little nervous giving the example of a baptismal commitment, and yes I am still alive.  Elder Giló decided not to kill me.       As I have been studying Isaiah, I have begun to see what a priveledge it is to be an elder in Israel.  When I first got my call I was gratefull to be able to be part of the fulfilling of promises made to the prophets of the Book of Mormon and a part of the gathering of Israel.   Isaiah ties in well with the Symbolism in the story of Joseph in Egypt as well.      Elder Giló and I get along well and I try to learn as much as possible in the way he teaches, the way he talks to everybody and especially the way he treats everybody as a friend.  He never gives up when we have more to do and he really cares about the people we teach and have taught.  He also cares a great deal about the members and they are affected very positivley by his friendship.  His presence is not only good for the investigators, but for the members as well.  And he is very merciful in not killing me after zine conference.  We both laughed about that afterwards.      Our area is great and we have wonderful investigators and though it can be difficult to get them to change, if you can find the problem it can be very simple to get them to keep commitments especially if you help them and give them someone to trust and develop faith to act.  Missionary work may be hard, but if you just accept it and get to work, it becomes your way of life and its easier.      Our numbers this week are as follows0014/48111060/0155140/0

## Subject: Fw: Re: letter
From: Joseph Andrews <jakaal@myldsmail.net>
Date: Wed, 03 Jun 2009 04:20:00 GMT

[jakaalhide_hotmail.com]--Forwarded Message Attachment--Subject: Re: letterFrom: jakaal@myldsmail.netTo: skipandrews@sprintmail.comDate: Mon, 13 Aug 2007 21:40:00 +0000Dear Family,        I´m glad to hear that all is well back in Olathe.  Sounds like the summer is finally winding down.  So morgan  had to get a new suit huh?  I sometimes wonder how tall he will ve when I get back.  It always seems that i forget what i was going to write when I sit down to email, so this may get pretty random. today we went to a members house to watch movies and do service.  our district leaders were in our area today to pass pday with us so they helped.  Elder hall´s companion elder Rodriguez mowed the lawn and I had to hold the extension cord.  I don´t think he´s ever mowed a lawn before.  I must have OCD or something because I actually sang hymns to keep myself from screaming.  When I mow, aerate vacuum etc., I make a pattern to follow involving STRAIGHT lines, so the random fan pattern and weird bent lines enraged my soul and my eyes were probably glowing neon red... This week we accomplished our 7 goals yet again, at the price of being out a little later than recommended.  We would have been home on time, but we had six contacts to make and we were in a members car on the way home when we saw 4 people in the street so we had the member drop us of fifty feet away and we made tyhe contacts and searched for two people(we ended up finding two people a block away from our apartment in a parked car) and finished to find the district leader had been waiting for us at our apartment for an hour.  Fun.       My companion is excellent.  His Dad died out of the blue on Saturday and he´s been handling it perfectly.  When Mom died I wasn´t supposed to work for a week but after the family left I felt like I would go out of my mind if I didn´t do something so I went back to work.  I think Elder Giló is the same way.  we worked really hard on sunday.  well we watched fantastic four 2 and harry potter 5 on DVD today.  Neither of them has left the theaters yet but this is Brazil.  I have yet to see a legitamate copy of any dvd or CD.         Os morros aqui no Brasil são muito grande e minhas pernas estão com fogo.  Esta semana foi difícil.  Some of you may ask if you were supposed to understand any of that, to which I would say; "No.  I just wanted you to know haw hard it was"        I love you all and wish the best for you.            Love Elder Andrews-----Original Message-----From: Skip Andrews &lt;skipandrews@sprintmail.com&gt;To: Joseph Andrews &lt;jakaal@myldsmail.net&gt;Date: Sun, 12 Aug 2007 20:53:22 -0500Subject: letter  August 12, 2007Dear Joseph:Well I hope that you have had a good week. Again I apologize that Ididn't get lasst weeks letter to you on time. SOme of your siblings haveor are continuing to write to you snail mail. We remember you in ourprayers and hope that all is well with you.It is Sunday afternoon and I just woke up from a to hour nap and I feelgroggy and not much like doing anything. I hate taking longer naps. Atany rate the weather here has been in the 90's all week with highhumidity and a chance of morning rain for the first three days of theweek. I believe we got some rain on Tuesday evening. So far our weatherpatterns have been quite mild for the last month. Some times we getdumped on but not that much thunder and lightning and the winds havebeen very light. It is supposed to be even warmer this coming week.It has been a typical week for me as far as work goes. Charles workedwith me for several days and then I let him work on his car and getpacked to go. By the end of the week I was almost done with the framingand plumbing of the bathroom. I found out that I needed to run three waywire for the fire alarms instead of two way wire so I need to re dothat. Most of the wiring is accessible still so it won&#25;t be such aterrible thing just aggravating. Thursday we got an emergency call froma longstanding customer. They had problems at both their houses and sowe went and tried to solve them. One house they are having problems withthe refrigerator freezer and the laundry drain turned out to be halfclogged. I fixed the clog but the freezer is out of my league. At theother house they had a flooding problem in the basement and thought thatit was the sump pump but I don&#25;t think so. We rearrange the sump pumpand it seems to be working ok. They had some real good rain on Tuesdayevening in their part of town. Wednesday evening I took the scoutsswimming at a pool in one of their housing divisions. Had some veryunusual cloud formations that evening. There were two strips of cloudsin a generally cloudy sky that ran from one horizon to the other. Thestrips originated from one point on the horizon and spread out over headand then converged to a single point at the other horizon. Kind of aparallel line visual distortion due to distance as the lines followed aspherical curvature. The lines were lit up like the sun was shiningthrough them. Never seen anything like it.This week Brent has been at the Chiefs training camp in Wisconsin doinghis rotation on the IT staff. Nicole and her four kids came up to staywith Erin while Brent was gone. Nicole is an old friend of Erin&#25;s whonow lives in Austin Texas. Erin also came down with walking pneumoniathis week and it has taken a little bit of a toll on her.Charles replaced the drivers side drive axile on his Accura thisThursday evening. By the time he was done he was covered from head tofoot with grease. It is the fourth time he has replaced it. It is oldhat by now but never real easy. Friday late he left for Ruth&#25;s and spentSaturday with her family having fun. I believe that to day he is on theroad to my mothers place. It is actually forty five minutes closer toBellefountaine from her house than from ours. He was going to stop atCatherine&#25;s, in Clarksville, on the way but Catherine and kids are inAugusta Georgia this week with Noah. I talked to Charles a few minutesago and he is still at Ruth&#25;s and will leave early in the morning for Ohio.Morgan and Anna have played with friends and had a good time this weekand enjoyed their last full week of vacation. Anna got to go bowlingwith a friend last night. She enjoyed it. Morgan and I went to seminaryregistration and his teacher will be one of Laura&#25;s girl friend&#25;shusbands. He married Brandy Gaughn. He will start seminary two Mondaysfrom tomorrow. Anna and I went over to the school today and her teacherwill be Mrs. Pitner. She was new last year but Anna knows who she is andis excited to be going back to school. Anna is singing church hymnstonight with Aurelia accompanying her on the piano. She is taking aninterest in music and sometimes sings to herself in her room.Aurelia is working lots now. They dismissed four temps and two othersquit. So now she has lots of work. Thursday she went in late. She didn&#25;tdo the dishes like she said she would when she got home and she neededto fill out her pell grant application. She did the application on linebut she got to work about an hour and a half late.Well that is most of the news from here.LoveDad
